1. Introduction
1.1 Background of environmental and social system assessment
1.       As China's southernmost island province, Hainan has the most diverse coastal ecosystem
among all provinces in China and is one of the most biodiverse regions in China. It stretches for
1,944 kilometers of coastline, which contains unique natural resources and faces challenges such
as deteriorating water quality in some rivers discharging into the sea and the degradation of typical
marine ecosystems such as coral reefs, mangroves, and seagrass beds. In response to the
requirements of major national planning such as the "Master Plan for Major National Important
Ecosystem Protection and Restoration Projects (2021-2035)" and other major national planning
requirements, Hainan Province has applied for World Bank financing and adopted the Program-for-
Results (PforR) financing instrument to implement the Hainan Coastal Regional Ecosystem
Restoration and Protection Program.
2.       Whereas the Hainan Provincial Coastal Zone and Marine Spatial Plan (2021-2035) include
provisions on biodiversity conservation and climate change response that are aligned with
requirements of the World Bank's China Country Partnership Framework. To support the
implementation of this Plan, the World Bank is preparing a Program-for-Results (PforR) operation—
the Hainan Integrated Coastal Ecosystems Management Program for Results Project (P512663)—
with proposed financing of EUR 200 million (approximately US$230 million equivalent) for Hainan
Province. The Project works through activities within three Result Areas (RAs): Result Area 1 (RA1)
– Restore Degraded Coastal Ecosystems; Result Area 2 (RA2) – Enhance Coastal Ecosystems
Conservation; Result Area 3 (RA3) – Strengthen Institutional Capacity for ICEM. The World Bank
and the Chinese government are still working on the Project's preparatory work.
3.       The development of the " Hainan Integrated Coastal Ecosystems Management Program for
Results Project " (hereinafter referred to as the Project) will continue to support the implementation
of the planning content of Hainan Province's "Hainan Coastal Zone and Marine Spatial Planning
(2021-2035)".
1.2 The purpose and task of this assessment
4.       This Environmental and Social System Assessment (ESSA) is guided by the key policies
and core principles identified in the World Bank's World Bank Policy: Program-for-Results Financing
(August 2024) and the World Bank's Guidelines for Environmental and Social Systems Assessment
under PforR (December 18, 2024), which are used in relevant national, provincial, and county-level
systems and institutions' capacity to plan and implement effective measures to manage
environmental and social risks and impacts. Key policy elements of the World Bank include the goal
of "Promote environmental and social sustainability in the PforR Program design; avoid, minimize,
or mitigate adverse impacts; and promote informed decision-making relating to the PforR Program’s
environmental and social impacts." The core principles of World Bank policy regarding environmental
and social management systems include:
•   Core Principle 1: E&S Management Systems: Program E&S management systems are
    designed to (a) promote E&S sustainability in the Program design; (b) avoid, minimize, or
    mitigate adverse impacts; and (c) promote informed decision-making relating to a Program’s
    E&S effects.
•   Core Principle 2: Natural Habitats and Physical Cultural Resources: Program E&S management
    systems are designed to avoid, minimize, or mitigate adverse impacts on natural habitats and
    physical cultural resources resulting from the Program. Program activities that involve the
    significant conversion or degradation of critical natural habitats or critical physical cultural
    heritage are not eligible for PforR financing.
•   Core Principle 3: Health and Safety Management: Program E&S management systems are
    designed to protect public and worker safety against the potential risks associated with (a) the
    construction and/or operation of facilities or other operational practices under the Program; (b)
    exposure to toxic chemicals, hazardous wastes, and otherwise dangerous materials under the
    Program; and (c) reconstruction or rehabilitation of infrastructure located in areas prone to
    natural hazards.
•   Core Principle 4: Involuntary resettlement management systems: Program E&S systems

                                                  1
    manage land acquisition and loss of access to natural resources in a way that avoids or
•   minimizes displacement and assists affected people in improving, or at the minimum restoring,
    their livelihoods and living standards.
•   Core Principle 5: The system of ethnic minorities and vulnerable groups Program E&S systems
    give due consideration to the cultural appropriateness of, and equitable access to, Program
    benefits, giving special attention to the rights and interests of Indigenous Peoples, ethnic
    minorities, and vulnerable groups.
•   Core Principle 6: Social Conflict Management System Program E&S systems avoid
    exacerbating social conflict, especially in fragile states, post-conflict areas, or areas subject to
    territorial disputes.
5.        It is the responsibility of the World Bank to prepare the ESSA Report. The ESSA process is
a common task between the Bank and lenders. The borrower assists the Bank team in research,
data collection, and public consultation on the Project's environmental and social systems and their
operations at all stages of the PforR lending cycle, as well as special matters such as stakeholder
consultations at all levels and the disclosure of this report. This environmental and social assessment
identifies the environmental and social risks of the Project and assesses the environmental and
social management system applicable to the Project, including policies, mechanisms and
performance, identifies areas for improvement in environmental and social risk management under
the existing system, and proposes improvement measures to manage the environmental and social
risks of the Project. The results of the assessment are reflected in the Environmental and Social
System Assessment report and are implemented in the implementation of the Project. This project
environmental and social systems assessment focuses on the following tasks:
•   Identify, investigate, and evaluate the potential environmental and social impacts and risks of
    the Project's activities;
•   Identify the laws, regulations, policies, etc. applicable to the national, provincial and local (county,
    township) environmental and social management of the project;
•   Identify provincial and local institutional establishment and implementation procedures related
    to the environmental and social management of the Project;
•   Evaluate the management performance of the environmental and social management related
    institutions of the Project;
•   Identify and evaluate whether the relevant systems and their performance are consistent with
    the core principles and key planning elements of the Bank's policies;
•   Develop recommendations and plans to improve environmental and social management
    performance as required by national regulations and the Bank's PforR policies.
1.3 The procedure and method of this assessment
6.        During the initial concept stage of the Program, the Bank's Environment and Social
Team has emphasized to the technical team and the borrower that PforR program must exclude
activities that associated with Substantial environmental and social risks, such as large-scale
infrastructure construction (such as major water conservancy works), activities involving significant
land acquisition and demolition with livelihood impacts, and other activities inconsistent with the
PforR exclusion principles, so that the design of activities under the Result Areas should focuses on
restoration of degraded coastal ecosystems and enhancement of coastal ecosystem protection,
thereby clearly defining the scope and boundaries of the Program. During the Project identification
stage, the World Bank's ESSA team conducted an initial screening of environmental and social risks
of project activities through project identification interviews with borrowers' institutions in mid-August
2025. Applying the PforR exclusion principles, activities that did not meet the eligibility criteria for
PforR financing were excluded from the program scope. In mid-September 2025 and late October
2025, the World Bank's ESSA team undertook field visits to the two participating counties to conduct
further due diligence, with a focus on reviewing the environmental and social management systems
applicable to the activities proposed under the counties’ program activities list. During the Project
preparation stage, the World Bank team conducts a comprehensive environmental and social
system assessment according to the agreed project scope. This assessment included (i) evaluating
the environmental and social benefits, impacts, and risks of the Project, evaluating the domestic
environmental and social management system in terms of legal framework, institutional
arrangements, and implementation performance, and proposing improvement measures and action

                                                    2
plans against World Bank policies. The team consulted relevant government departments on this
report and revised it based on feedback. During the Project appraisal stage, the proposed
Program action plan was agreed upon and incorporated into the overall project action plan, and the
final report was disclosed on the World Bank and domestic government websites.
7.         To support the ESSA, the World Bank team applied a range of data collection and
consultations methods. The selection of the two participating counties was based on the following
criteria: (i) coverage of typical Program activity sites and associated downstream facilities or related
activities; and (ii) inclusion of representative ethnic minority villages. In addition, relevant background
materials were collected through the provincial and county Project Management Offices (PMOs).
•   Secondary data collection and desk research: The team collected and reviewed available
    secondary materials, including information provided by provincial and county government
    agencies, publicly available online information, published literature and books, etc. Desk reviews
    were conducted to understand the legal framework, institutional arrangements, implementation
    procedures, and performance of the domestic environmental and social management systems
    relevant to the Program.
•   Primary data collection and analysis: Collect primary data through consultation, discussion,
    visit, questionnaire, on-site survey and other methods. In August 2025, a series of on-site
    meetings and visits were conducted to relevant sector authorities at the provincial and county
    levels in Hainan to understand the basic mechanism of the environmental and social
    management system. Field surveys were also carried out at representative Program activities
    in the sample counties to assess system implementation in practice.
•   Stakeholder engagement throughout the Project cycle: From the early stage of participating
    county identification and training through the preparation and finalization of this report, the World
    Bank ESSA team engaged in continuous consultation with key stakeholders. During report
    preparation, the team consulted provincial and county government departments responsible for
    environmental and social management, as well as community and village leaders, residents’
    representatives, women’s representatives, representatives of poor households, and
    representatives of ethnic minority groups potentially affected by the Program. Consultations
    were conducted through face-to-face meetings, interviews, and virtual meetings.
•   Consultation on the ESSA Report: Consultations on the ESSA report were conducted with
    relevant provincial and county government departments in November and December 2025. The
    first draft of the ESSA report was disclosed by the World Bank team in November 2025 for
    review and feedback from provincial PMOs and relevant government agencies at both provincial
    and county levels. In early December 2025, the World Bank team conducted in-person
    consultations in Lingshui County and Changjiang County to discuss the draft ESSA. Written
    comments were provided by relevant agencies during and after the consultations, and these
    comments have been reflected in the revised report, as summarized in Annex 6.




                                                    3
2. Project Overview
2.1 Government-planned activities
8.         This project will support the implementation of the Hainan Coastal Zone and Marine Spatial
Plan (2021-2035) in Hainan Province. The plan aims to promote the ecological protection and
sustainable development of Hainan's coastal areas, and clarifies seven core tasks: (1) coastal
natural resource management; (2) coastal ecological restoration and protection; (3) optimization of
coastal industrial layout; (4) Improvement of coastal living environment; (5) coastal disaster
prevention and mitigation; (6) coastal spatial planning and guidance; (7) Integrated management of
coastal areas based on ecosystems. The second task specifically includes three major action
directions: i) adopt an integrated ridge-river-reef management model; ii) restoration and protection
of critical coastal ecosystems; iii) Promote coordinated pollution control between land and sea. The
planning scope and typical activities of the Hainan Provincial Government are shown in Annex 1.
2.2 PforR program
9.      Program Scope: The Bank PforR program, hereinafter referred to as the "Project",
supports two areas in the Hainan Provincial Coastal and Marine Spatial Planning (2021-2035) (see
Table 2-1). The World Bank proposes to provide EUR 200 million in financing for the program
implementation period from 2026 to 2031.

10.      Geographical boundaries: The main physical activities supported by Results Areas 1 and
2 of the Project will be carried out in Lingshui and Changjiang counties, Hainan Province. The non-
physical activities supported by Result Area 3 will be carried out in Lingshui County, Changjiang
County, and at the provincial level in Hainan Province.




                                                            4
                                 Figure 2-1 Schematic diagram of the Project location
11.        Development Objectives and Result Areas: The overall Program Development Objective
is to restore degraded coastal ecosystems in selected areas of Hainan Province, strengthen
ecosystem protection, and strengthen institutional capacity for integrated management of coastal
ecosystems. The selected areas, which are two typical counties among the 12 coastal counties in
Hainan Province, namely Changjiang and Lingshui counties, will be achieved by supporting activities
in the following three result areas: Result Area 1: Restore degraded coastal ecosystems; Result Area
2: Enhance coastal ecosystems conservation; Result Area 3: Strengthen the institutional capability
of ICEM.
12.     Typical activities and output indicators: A series of investment activities will be carried
out under each Result Area of this project, and a number of indicators will be used to reflect the
corresponding outputs, including a number of payment-related indicators (DLIs), as shown in Table
2-2.

13.       Linked/Associated Facilities or Activities: Based on the list of typical project activities,
the Environmental and Social Team of the World Bank has identified relevant external
activities/facilities that are necessary for achieving the Project’s objectives but have not been
explicitly defined as project activities or included in the expenditure framework. These specifically
include: Integrated utilization or disposal activities/facilities for eucalyptus trees felled during single-
species stand transformation, or for exotic species (Rhizophora mangle) cleared from mangrove
forests (e.g., pulping and papermaking, or biomass power generation activities and facilities); Final
disposal activities and facilities for residual sludge generated by urban and rural sewage treatment
plants; Post-recovery integrated utilization and production activities and facilities for agricultural
waste (crop straw and agricultural plastic film) recovered under agricultural non-point source
pollution control initiatives. The on-site investigation found that these downstream existing
disposal/recycling facilities have been completed and are operating normally; The relevant units
have completed the EIA/stability assessment and environmental protection acceptance in
accordance with the Solid Waste Pollution Prevention and Control Law, the Circular Economy
Promotion Law, the Environmental Impact Assessment Law, the Regulations on the Administration
of Pollutant Discharge Permits in the Hainan Special Economic Zone, and other laws and regulations,
and hold the pollutant discharge permit issued by the competent ecological environment department
and are subject to regular supervision (see Section 4.2.1 for details).
2.3 Implementation agencies
14.       The effective implementation of the Project will rely on cross-sectoral, multi-level
government coordination. The Provincial Project Leading Group (PPLG) is headed by the Director
of the Department of Natural Resources and Planning, and includes representatives from the
Provincial Development and Reform Commission (PDRC), the Provincial Department of Finance
(PDOF), the Department of Ecology and Environment (DEE), the Department of Water Resources
(DWR), and the Department of Agriculture and Rural Affairs (DARA) and the county magistrates of
the two project counties. The Provincial Project Leadership Group is responsible for: (a) monitoring
the progress of project implementation through annual meetings or meetings held at the request of
participating agencies; (b) Providing leadership and guidance for project management and
implementation; (c) Coordinating cross-sectoral cooperation among participating agencies, when
necessary; (d) facilitating decision-making and ensuring support from other stakeholders and
institutions. The Hainan Provincial Department of Natural Resources and Planning has established
a Provincial Project Management Office (PPMO) with experts in procurement, financial management,
environmental and social impact assessment, community engagement, monitoring and evaluation,
verification and various fields. One of the responsibilities of the Provincial Project Management Office
is environmental and social management, with a commissioner monitoring environmental and social
issues in the Project, ensuring that agreed project action plans PAPs and mitigation measures are
implementing, and managing environmental and social risks in accordance with World Bank policies.
Changjiang County and Lingshui County will set up a county-level project leading group (CPLG)
respectively, with the deputy county magistrate in charge as the team leader. The county-level

                                                              6
project management office (CPMO) is located in each county natural resources bureau, and its
members come from relevant implementing agencies (Project Implementation Units, hereinafter
referred to as PIUs), and implement the Project construction in the region under the guidance of the
provincial project management office (PMO). The county-level project implementation units (PIUs)
are the county water affairs bureau, the natural resources and planning bureau, the forestry bureau,
the agriculture and rural bureau, and the Qichao town government of Changjiang County, which
have signed construction management contracts with two national group enterprises. Among them,
Lingshui County signed a construction management contract with Lingshui County Xingling
Construction Management Co., Ltd., a subsidiary of Lingshui County Ecological Investment Group
Company; Changjiang County signed an agency construction management contract with Changjiang
Urban Construction Investment Co., Ltd. and Changjiang Li Autonomous County Rural Revitalization
Investment and Development Co., Ltd., a subsidiary of Changjiang Development Holding Group Co.,
Ltd., and the above-mentioned enterprises respectively bear the specific responsibility of
organizing and implementing project activities in specific achievement areas and performing
the management responsibilities of the county-level project office.
15.        The Hainan Provincial Department of Natural Resources and Planning (hereinafter referred
to as the Hainan Provincial Project Office) is a constituent department of the Hainan Provincial
People's Government for natural resources and planning in the province. The department was
officially established on September 29, 2018 in accordance with the "Guiding Opinions of the Central
Committee of the Communist Party of China and the State Council on Supporting Hainan to
Comprehensively Deepen Reform and Opening-up" and the "Hainan Provincial Institutional Reform
Plan", integrating the responsibilities of the Provincial Planning Commission, the Provincial
Department of Land and Resources, the Provincial Department of Oceans and Fisheries and other
departments to achieve unified management of land and marine natural resources. The agency
construction management companies contracted by the PIUs of the two project counties are as
follows: Lingshui County Xingling Construction Management Co., Ltd.: Formerly known as Lingshui
Li Autonomous County Water Group Co., Ltd., it was registered on June 5, 2020, with a staff of 46.
Since its establishment, it has undertaken a total of 156 government construction and management
projects. Changjiang Urban Construction Investment Co., Ltd.: Established on November 15, 2005,
it has 36 employees and has implemented 108 projects since 2012. Changjiang Li Autonomous
County Rural Revitalization Investment and Development Co., Ltd.: Registered on August 13, 2013,
it has 41 employees and has completed 175 projects since 2017. Through discussions with the
heads of the three enterprises, it was learned that in terms of environmental and social management,
the management model of the three companies is similar, that is, a preparatory team or preliminary
department of 4-7 people is set up in the early stage of the Project, responsible for implementing the
domestic environmental and social management requirements that must be met in the early stage
of the Project, such as carrying out public surveys, community coordination, etc., and entrusting
professional consulting institutions to complete the preparation, evaluation and filing of documents
such as social stability, environmental impact assessment, soil and water conservation, and special
demonstration of limited promising activities within the red line of ecological protection, as well as
administrative approval and other related work to ensure project compliance. The risks are
controllable, and the public is informed. In the Project implementation stage, a project management
team of 4-6 people composed of different specialties is set up to be responsible for the management
of the Project implementation process, of which at least 1-2 people are responsible for the
environmental and social affairs of the Project, such as: coordination of land acquisition and
demolition/land lease work, environmental protection, water protection supervision and acceptance,
filing of relevant materials, specific implementation of the environmental and social action plan of the
Project, and handling complaints arising from environmental and social issues during the
implementation of the Project.
16.       According to the supervision of the implemented projects, Hainan Province has rich
experience and good track record in environmental and social management and monitoring in
accordance with World Bank standards. There is currently an ongoing construction project in Hainan
Province titled “China Emerging Infectious Diseases Prevention, Preparedness and Response
Project,” with a total investment of US$203.5482 million, of which US$175 million is financed by the
World Bank. In addition to the provincial project management office, special personnel have also
been set up in other relevant provincial, municipal and county-level sector departments to coordinate

                                                   7
and manage the environmental and social issues of the Project. During the investigation period in
Hainan Province and each sample county, the provincial project management office and each county
confirmed that the provincial and county-level project management offices will arrange full-time
personnel to be responsible for environmental and social monitoring and management during the
implementation of the Project. The environmental and social risks induced by downstream activities
and facilities of this project will be managed by the relevant government specific functional
departments in accordance with the corresponding environmental and social regulations. For
example, the environmental and social issues of projects are supervised through current domestic
policies, regulations, technical guidelines, etc., and for projects involving greater environmental and
social impacts, the implementing agency also needs to formulate management measures specifically
for environmentally sensitive points. During the Project implementation at the same time,
government departments and implementing agencies can also obtain external training, technical and
personnel support to strengthen their capacities if needed.




                                                  8
3. Environmental and social effects, impacts and risks of the Project
3.1 Project boundaries and excluded activities
17.      Objective: In the evaluation process of the environmental and social management system,
the Project fully considered the principled requirements of the World Bank policy on environmental
and social impact screening, and selected the activities included in the Hainan Provincial
Government plan, with the aim of: 1) identifying those that may have potentially serious
environmental and social impacts that are not suitable for inclusion in this project; 2) Identify areas
where further Environmental and Social Assessment are needed.
18.      Exclusion Principle: Under the Bank PforR Financing Policy, activities that are “judged to
be likely to have significant adverse impacts that are sensitive, diverse, or unprecedented on the
environment and/or affected people are not eligible for financing and are excluded from the Program.”
More specifically, PforR financing should not be used to support programs, or activities within
programs that in the Bank’s opinion involve the following:
o         Significant conversion or degradation of critical natural habitats or critical cultural heritage
sites;
o         Air, water, or soil contamination leads to significant adverse impacts on the health or
safety of individuals, communities, or ecosystems;
o         Workplace conditions that expose workers to significant risks to health and personal
safety;
o         Land acquisition and/or resettlement of a scale or nature that will have significant adverse
impacts on affected people, or the use of forced evictions;
o         Large-scale changes in land use or access to land and/or natural resources;
o         Adverse E&S impacts covering large geographical areas, including transboundary
impacts, or global impacts such as greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions;
o         Significant cumulative, induced, or indirect impacts;
o         Activities that involve the use of forced or child labor;
o         Marginalization of discrimination against, or conflict within or among, social (including
ethnic and racial) groups; or
o         Activities that would (a) have adverse impacts on land and natural resources subject to
traditional ownership or under customary use or occupation; (b) cause relocation of Indigenous
Peoples/Sub-Saharan African Historically Underserved Traditional Local Communities from land and
natural resources that are subject to traditional ownership or under customary use or occupation; or
(c) have significant impacts on Indigenous Peoples/Sub-Saharan African Historically Underserved
Traditional Local Communities’ cultural heritage that is material to the identity and/or cultural,
ceremonial, or spiritual aspects of the affected communities.

19.     Excluded Activities: In accordance with the above exclusion principles, this project will
exclude all types of activities listed in paragraphs 14 and 16 of the World Bank's Guidelines for
Environmental and Social Systems Assessment under PforR (December 18, 2024). Considering the
characteristics of the activities to be supported by this project, the following activities with Substantial
environmental and social risks should be excluded from the project:
⚫     activities with serious legacy, environmental and social issues in the project areas1;
⚫     Other man-made activities in the core area of the nature reserve except for activities permitted
      by laws, regulations and relevant national regulations, such as scientific research and
      observation, investigation and monitoring, ecological restoration, etc.;
⚫     In marine ecological restoration, large-scale hardware engineering facilities that may change
      hydrodynamics and affect marine ecology, including benthic organisms (such as dredging with
      a project volume of 100,000 cubic meters or more, tidal flat pad elevation projects, temporary
      cofferdams, marine artificial fishing reef projects with a solid matter (theoretical volume)
      delivery capacity of more than 50,000 m3, etc.);


1
  The project does not support agricultural activities such as planting, animal husbandry and aquaculture in abandoned mining areas,
factories and other brownfield lands, which are directly polluted by industrial and mining production activities and have serious legacy
environmental problems and significant environmental risks. as well as social risks such as unclear land ownership.

                                                                     9
⚫      Agricultural non-point source pollution control, involving farmland contaminated soil
       remediation;
⚫      The construction of industrial sewage treatment facilities and the construction of large-scale
       domestic sewage treatment plants with a capacity of more than 100,000 t/d;
⚫      Forest ecosystem restoration and forest management activities involving mine restoration,
       commercial-scale logging or other extractive industries;
⚫      Activities involving the acquisition of basic farmland and the demolition of a large number of
       houses;
⚫      Activities involving land use that do not conform to national or local land use planning;
⚫      Activities that affect the livelihoods of large numbers of people due to large-scale land use,
       resettlement or restrictions on access to land, water and natural resources;
⚫      large-scale land acquisition, transferring farmland to forests, fishing and wetlands, and other
       activities;
⚫      Activities that have a significant adverse impact on ethnic minorities and vulnerable groups;
⚫      Livelihood impacts activities arising from restrictions on use rights or transfer rights.
3.2 Scope of assessment
20.       Physical activities of this project: The physical activities of this project will be
concentrated in Changjiang County and Lingshui County, Hainan Province, including: 1) restoring
mangroves and conserving biodiversity by planting native species, removing alien species; 2)
restoration and monitoring of coral reefs, oyster reefs and seagrass beds; 3) Restore the river
ecosystem into the sea through ecological revetment, dredging and planting of riverside plants; 4)
Restoration of natural shorelines through beach sand replenishment, small hard infrastructure (such
as ding dams or ecological breakwaters), and windbreak improvements; 5) Construction of nature
education facilities; 6) manage farmland non-point source pollution and comprehensive utilization of
agricultural film and straw recycling through nature-based solutions (including constructed wetlands);
7) Improve urban and rural sewage management (new construction or renovation of collection pipe
networks and treatment facilities); 8) sustainable management of forests, including the
transformation of inefficient forests and the construction of forest fire prevention roads, to reduce soil
erosion; 9) Recycling and comprehensive utilization of agricultural film and plastics and recycling of
pesticide packaging waste. These physical activities are widely distributed in forests, farmland, rivers,
coastal wetlands, urban and rural areas, and offshore waters in the two project counties. Some
restoration activities (such as coral reefs, oyster reefs, seagrass bed restoration and monitoring,
estuaries, lagoons and other wetlands) will be within the ecological protection red line and the
general control area of nature reserves within the ecological protection red line that Hainan Province
has delineated2(The current situation is state-owned wetlands, collective unused wasteland, state-
owned rivers, etc.); Some restoration activities (such as single-species degraded and inefficient
forest transformation) will be carried out on existing secondary forest land; Water pollution control
activities involving farmland non-point source, urban and rural domestic sewage and other related
industries will be in habitats or near urban rivers after human activities, and are not within the
ecological protection red line.
21.       Technical assistance activities of this project: Technical assistance activities of this
project will be carried out at the provincial level and in two project counties, including: 1) developing
and implementing an integrated management plan for coastal zone ecosystems at the county level;
2) Install and implement air-ground-sea ecosystem monitoring systems; 3) Provide training program
for capacity-building in integrated coastline ecosystem management; 4) promoting blue employment
and women's leadership; 5) Formulate and implement an integrated management system for coastal
ecosystems at the provincial level.
22.      Associated Facilities / Activities: As defined in the World Bank's Guidelines for
Environmental and Social Systems Assessment under PforR, a project associated facility, or activity
is an activity that is necessary to achieve the Project's objectives but is not explicitly defined as the

2 Ecological protection red line refers to the state delineating ecological protection red lines in key ecological function areas, ecological environment sensitive areas

and vulnerable areas, and implementing strict protection. In the nature reserves (i.e., national parks, nature reserves, natural parks), world cultural and natural
heritage sites, special marine reserves, drinking water source protection areas, cultural relics protection units, mangrove wetlands, important estuaries, coral reef
concentration areas, seagrass bed concentration areas, coastal natural shorelines, other wetlands that have been assessed to have important ecological functions,
extremely sensitive and fragile ecological environment, or potentially important ecological value.

                                                                                    10
Project or is not part of the payment framework. Based on the World Bank's environmental and social
due diligence, the Project identified relevant associated facilities or activities (see paragraph 13) that
are existing facilities and will not have indirect environmental and social impacts as a result of the
Project's implementation.
3.3 Environmental and social benefits
23.        This project activity and related/related borrower project activities are the implementation of
the national major plan - "Coastal Zone Ecological Protection and Restoration Major Project
Construction Plan (2021-2035)" in selected areas of Hainan Province, which will adopt a
comprehensive approach to coastal ecosystem restoration and management - the "3R" approach,
through the priority ecosystems from land to rivers to coastal zones (including mangroves, seagrass
beds, coral reefs, coastal defense forests, oyster reefs, wetland beaches, natural shorelines, etc.),
and the implementation of a package of activities to reduce ecosystem degradation stress factors
(forest management, agricultural non-point source, domestic sewage, plastic waste) to produce
significant positive benefits in ecological environmental protection, biodiversity conservation and
greenhouse gas emission reduction. 3R priority ecological restoration will be conducive to the
protection, restoration and sustainable use of the integrated land-sea systemic ecosystem of
mountains, water, forests, fields, lakes and grasses in the Project area. Provide habitats for marine
and terrestrial organisms, which is conducive to eliminating the damage of alien species to native
and some endangered species, and expand and protect the mangrove wetlands of the coastal zone
project in the Project area to conserve their biodiversity; Enhancing the distribution and abundance
of critical ecosystems at the Project site will enhance fish breeding habitat and improve biodiversity,
while helping to reduce pollution loads on rivers and seas through carbon sequestration and reduced
point and non-point source pollution inputs. This will also promote the ecology of farmland, increase
the output value and output of agricultural products, improve the living environment in urban and
rural areas, and enhance the biological protection, wind and sand fixation and coastal protection
functions of coastal zones. Give full play to the ecological functions of coastal defense forests in
wind and sand fixation, water and soil conservation, water conservation, disaster prevention, disaster
mitigation and ecological balance maintenance in coastal areas. From a social perspective, the
Project involves stakeholders to participate in a wide range of activities, such as ecological
restoration activities such as rural non-point source pollution control, which not only greatly improves
the local ecological environment, but also increases the income from the original land rent or
increases the possibility of land income sharing by improving land utilization rate and improving
farming conditions.
3.4 Environmental and social impact analysis
3.4.1 Direct and indirect impacts
24.      The implementation of the typical activities to be supported by this project will have a certain
degree of adverse environmental or social impacts, which will be comprehensively described in the
following sections, after the excluded activities that may have Substantial environmental and social
impacts (see section 3.1) in the Government planning activities (see section 3.1), the environmental
and social impacts and risk screening and risk assessment of the typical activities are described in
Annex 2. The specific environmental and social impacts of each project activity during the
implementation stage will be evaluated or assessed in accordance with the corresponding domestic
legal requirements, such as environmental impact assessment (hereinafter referred to as EIA) and
thematic demonstration related to ecological red line protection, as well as social stability risk
assessment (hereinafter referred to as SSRA). The construction, operation or implementation of
various physical activities under this project will have varying degrees of direct environmental and
social impacts, as shown below, and the usual mitigation measures are shown in Annex 8.
25. Key environmental impacts:
⚫   Ecological impact: Some of the physical activities of degraded ecosystem restoration under
    Result Area 1 will be within the coastal ecological protection red line area delineated by the
    Hainan Provincial Government (see Table 4-6 for details). Most of the physical activities under
    Result Area 2 were carried out in habitats modified by human activities and did not involve
    ecological protection red lines. The Project activities may disturb the transformed habitat (urban,
    farmland and rural areas) and the natural ecosystem and coastal zone within the ecological

                                                    11
    protection red line, and the civil engineering in the Project may cause physical damage to the
    native environment during the construction period, resulting in short-term and local
    environmental pollution and soil erosion, and temporary disturbance to wild animals and plants
    in land and sea areas. In the sustainable management of forests and the construction of coastal
    defense forests, the blind introduction of non-native species or the transition to relying on a
    single tree species leads to the biodiversity degradation of characteristic diversity and the
    reduction of biodiversity. The plant quarantine of tree and grass species to be replanted is not
    strict, which may cause the spread of plant pests and diseases to offset the restoration effect,
    and may even cause secondary damage to the ecosystem.
⚫   Environmental pollution: 1) During the construction or restoration process, there is a potential
    pollution risk of dust, noise, solid waste, etc., and a certain amount of sewage, solid waste, etc.
    will be generated during the construction process, and the water construction may also cause
    local soil erosion, but these construction impacts are short-term, temporary, and the scale is not
    large, only limited to the vicinity of the construction area, through good construction technology
    and management measures can be properly reduced, and disappear after the construction is
    completed; 2) If all kinds of non-point source and point source pollutant collection and treatment
    facilities are not managed well during the operation period, they may cause accidental
    concentrated discharge. However, the environmental impact during the operation period is
    predictable and can be avoided or reduced through mature technology and management
    measures, and does not pose a significant risk of environmental pollution.
⚫   Health and safety risks: physical injuries caused by contact with mechanical and electrical
    equipment during construction or ecological restoration and operation or management period,
    construction personnel, farmers, workers who operate and manage pollution control facilities,
    tracking and monitoring personnel, etc. The impact of occupational health and safety risks such
    as exposure to chemicals, pesticides, waterborne diseases, and other occupational health and
    safety risks on the health and safety of surrounding communities due to pesticide use safety
    and potential packaging waste recycling activities; Marine ecological restoration activities
    involve water and underwater operations, which may affect navigation safety, and practitioners
    may drown due to wading operations or collide with water transportation facilities, resulting in
    occupational health and safety risks.
26. Key social risks and impacts:
⚫   Land use: In the preparation stage of the report, activities involving large-scale land acquisition
    and demolition, as well as large-scale land use adjustments due to restrictions on use rights or
    transfer of use rights, which have a significant impact on livelihoods, have been excluded from
    the boundaries of this project. The project activities will involve four types of land use, and the
    corresponding potential social risk and impacts are as below.
    1) Use of state-owned land: Most of the physical activities involved in this project will be carried
    out on about 45 hectares of state-owned offshore waters, 3 kilometers of sandy shoreline, 8
    kilometers of coastal windbreaks, as well as rivers, wetlands, state-owned public welfare forests,
    and state-owned construction/industrial land, including: 1) ecological restoration projects (e.g.,
    coral reefs, oyster reefs, seagrass beds, mangrove restoration); ii) Coastal windbreak forests,
    inefficient forests/single tree species transformation; iii) Projects such as sandy shoreline
    restoration are the implementation of protection measures on existing land, such as
    replanting/sand replenishment, installation of monitoring equipment, etc. and 2) major
    estuary/river and wetland restoration projects are ecological restoration work such as ecological
    bank protection and water system connection within the established scope of state-owned rivers
    and wetland parks, and the above activities 1) and 2) do not involve land acquisition and
    ownership changes, and there are no production and livelihood activities within the land use
    area, which has no impact on livelihoods. 3) Some nature education facilities (such as museums,
    etc.) and agricultural waste integrated treatment centers are allocated or converted to use state-
    owned construction land. In conclusion, the use of state-owned land does not involve livelihood
    impact, but may involve compensation for a small number of attachments (such as trees) on
    some state-owned land. Given that domestic policies have corresponding compensation and
    are implemented well, the social risk is relatively low.


                                                  12
    2) Use of collectively owned land: the newly built rural sewage treatment facilities under the
    project, the township pretreatment center of the integrated treatment center of agricultural
    materials and waste, and the township In the restoration of sandy shorelines, the site selection
    of aquaculture centralized intake and drainage facilities will give priority to use collectively owned
    construction land and idle land, or the use of facility type of agricultural land, and try to avoid the
    use of farmland and the change of land nature. Only when the site selection does not meet the
    design requirements will a small amount of land acquisition be involved. After on-site
    investigation, it is understood that the construction scale of a single sewage treatment facility is
    about 0.045-0.15 acres, the total land use of multiple rural sewage treatment facilities will not
    exceed 13 acres, and the construction scale of agricultural waste pretreatment centers is about
    5 acres, and the total land area of all the above activities will not exceed 50 acres. The scale of
    land acquisition by these individual facilities is very small, and they are distributed in various
    townships, therefore the impact of land acquisition is minor. The existing land use management
    system in China has a comprehensive legal system and a clear implementation mechanism,
    and according to onsite investigation the overall implementation performance is good, the risk
    is low.
    3) Temporary land use: A certain amount of land will be used for temporary excavation of urban
    and rural sewage pipelines during the construction stage. Domestic laws have clear
    requirements for compensation for land attachments (such as crops) and for the process
    management and post-use restoration of temporary land.
    4) Collectively owned land leasing: some activities under the project, such as rural non-point
    source pollution control activities etc., will use large areas of land based on land leasing on a
    voluntary basis to carry out activities to improve land efficiency, such as rezoning mechanized
    roads and irrigation systems. The nature of these activities does not involve land acquisition,
    does not change the nature of agricultural land, and is used through negotiation in the form of
    voluntary lease. The domestic land leasing management system is clear, the transaction
    procedures are clear, and there is risk supervision and filing system, and the implementation of
    past cases is good. The project carries out about 900 acres of land lease (Not including Lingshui
    Data), considering that the land leasing activities involve a large area and many towns and
    villages, so the overall social risk is Substantial.
    Based on the above land use, the implementation of this project has minor impact on livelihood,
    in conclusion: 1) the project carried out on state-owned land has no livelihood impact, and only
    involves compensation for some attachments on state-owned land; 2) The compensation for a
    small amount of land acquisition and temporary land use involves a small scope, limited impact,
    clear compensation standards, sound implementing institutions, and will be managed through
    monitoring during the implementation process; 3) For activities that require land leasing, after
    on-site investigation, through rural non-point source pollution control activities, the production
    road and irrigation system will be improved, with the improvement of land cultivation conditions,
    the increase in land rent can not only cover the agricultural income of the original land planting,
    but also the tenants can also obtain Substantial income through work opportunities, so the land
    leasing is widely supported by the villagers.
⚫   Labor and working condition: For mangrove/seagrass beds/coral reefs/oyster reef restoration,
    beach replenishment, small hard infrastructure, windbreaks/Activities such as single-species
    forest transformation, urban and rural domestic sewage management, construction of nature
    education facilities, comprehensive environmental treatment of major rivers and estuaries, and
    non-point source pollution control may pose health and safety risks to workers during the
    construction process, but the construction time of a single site is not long, usually it will not
    exceeded 6 months. And the scale of employment for these activities is not large, about 20 to
    100 people. Local workers are generally employed, so large-scale construction camps will not
    be built, and contractors will manage and enforce environmental and social requirements in
    accordance with relevant domestic policies during the construction period, including on-site
    working conditions requirements, safety construction requirements, personal protection
    requirements, labor contracts and workers' wage requirements, emergency plans, etc. There is
    no risk of forced labor or child labor by reviewing the previous record. In general, the employment
    of this project does not involve significant risk employment, and there is an in place



                                                    13
    comprehensive construction employment management system and management requirements
    in China, so the risk of labor management is minor.
⚫   Ethnic minorities and vulnerable groups: Changjiang and Lingshui counties are both Li
    autonomous counties. Among them, although the ethnic minorities in Changjiang County
    (accounting for 39.02% of the total population) and Lingshui County (accounting for 57.5% of
    the total population) are spread throughout the county, they present a lifestyle of large and small
    settlements. After discussions with the relevant person in charge of the Civil and Religious
    Affairs Bureau of Changjiang/Lingshui County and the baseline survey of ethnic minorities in the
    project county (see Annex 9 for more information), it was found that the ethnic minorities in the
    project area were no different from the Han ethnic groups in the project area in terms of social
    welfare, rights, guarantees, economic, social or political systems; It only has certain uniqueness
    in some cultural customs and daily living habits. Ethnic minorities under this project do not meet
    the four criteria for being classified as indigenous people under ESS7 of the Environmental and
    Social Framework and are not recognized as "indigenous people". Specifically, they lack neither
    a special traditional system independent of the mainstream system nor a collective identity that
    maintains an exclusive collective identity with their ancestral territories. Therefore,
    environmental and social standards are not triggered. In terms of vulnerable groups, the
    assessment found that the protection of the rights and interests of low-income groups, women,
    children, and the elderly has basically built a policy and service system covering the rights and
    interests of vulnerable groups from the state to the local level, which can effectively protect the
    legitimate rights and interests of low-income groups, women, and other projects in various
    projects, and can also effectively manage the support and development issues of various
    vulnerable groups. In general, at the beginning of the preparation of the project, activities that
    have a significant adverse impact on ethnic minorities and vulnerable groups have been
    excluded, coupled with the relevant protection policies for ethnic minorities and vulnerable
    groups in China and Hainan Province, so the social risk related to ethnic minorities and
    vulnerable groups is low.
⚫   Information disclosure and public participation: Through interviews with local governments,
    it is learned that at the project implementation level, especially in major projects (e.g., involving
    land acquisition and resettlement, large-scale land consolidation, and Substantial environmental
    and social impact), there are corresponding policy requirements and implementation
    arrangements for public participation in China. However, at the level of project design and
    decision-making, there is no detailed institutional publicity and participation requirements, and
    there is a lack of a whole-process and systematic participation mechanism. In the process of
    project design, implementation and management, if the participation of various groups is not
    timely and sufficient, it will not only affect the achievement of the project goals, but also lead to
    the lack of inclusiveness of the project design plan and results for the disadvantaged groups.
    Therefore, the risk of inadequate public participation is "moderate". In order to ensure the
    effective participation of stakeholders in the whole process, PAP will establish project level
    stakeholder participation mechanism to ensure that all stakeholders fully participate in the
    project implementation process and equally share the project benefits.
27.      The environmental and social impacts of facilities/activities related to this project and the
downstream environmental and social impacts of technical assistance project activities are indirect,
but they are also within the scope of this report.
28.       Indirect impact of downstream related facilities/activities: During the screening process,
in addition to the project activities, the links between government planning beyond the project
boundaries and the project activities were analyzed, and the initial screening results were
continuously updated during the Project preparation period until the evaluation phase. From the early
stage of construction to normal operation, they have strictly performed the procedures of
environmental impact assessment, environmental protection "three simultaneous", environmental
protection acceptance, etc., and have been strictly supervised under the pollutant discharge permit
and other systems, and their adverse environmental impacts/risks are controllable. No new facilities
with Substantial environmental and social risks such as downstream incineration power plants,
cement plants, pulp and paper mills, and biomass power plants will be built due to the implementation
of this project activities.

29.       Impact of TA activities: In addition to physical activities, the Project includes a number of
soft technical assistance activities, such as the installation and implementation of a sky-ground-
marine ecosystem monitoring system, the implementation of pollution source surveys in two project
counties, the preparation and implementation of county-level integrated coastal ecosystem
management plans, the provision of capacity-building training programs for integrated coastline
ecosystem management, the promotion of blue employment and the promotion of women's
leadership, etc., The implementation of these activities will help strengthen the monitoring and
supervision capabilities of project implementation units, raise public awareness of environmental
protection, and improve the living environment through water pollution control and natural ecosystem
restoration. Except for a few people involved in research, outdoor research, census, and monitoring
activities that have a low and ordinary impact on occupational health and safety, and have certain
risks to the health and safety of personnel involved in water and underwater monitoring, the direct
environmental and social risks of implementing such activities themselves are small or non-existent.
However, the research results supported by certain TA activities (e.g., the preparation and
implementation of integrated coastal ecosystem management plans at the county level) may trigger
downstream investment activities (e.g., ecosystem restoration, water pollution control in various
areas, etc.), thereby indirectly generating environmental and social risks and impacts (see Chapters
4 and 5 for detailed evaluations). Overall, the TA activities under this project do not pose a potentially
Substantial risk to the environment and society.
3.4.2 Cumulative impact
30.       The scope of this project involves natural ecological spaces such as mountains, water,
forests, fields, lakes, grass, and seas, as well as towns and rural areas with frequent human activities,
involving a wide range. As far as the Project activity is concerned, it will be implemented in a planned
phased and regional manner in accordance with the Project implementation process of the two
project counties, and it is very unlikely that many ecological restorations and related water pollution

                                                                   15
control infrastructure construction activities will be carried out in the same area at the same time.
Therefore, the local construction activities of this project will not have significant cumulative negative
environmental and social impacts on a large area. At the same time, the implementation of this
project will be coordinated with other activities to jointly promote the realization of cumulative net
benefits in the region, including the restoration of degraded ecosystems, the sustainable
management of forests, the treatment of urban and rural domestic sewage and agricultural non-point
sources, and the improvement of social and economic effects and management capabilities, which
are mainly reflected in the following aspects: 1) the restoration of degraded ecosystems in coastal
zones; 2) resilient coastlines with increased erosion resistance; 3) Reduction of pollution load into
the sea; 4) Prevent the transportation of plastic waste to water bodies; 5) Reduce greenhouse gas
emissions; 6) more populations benefit from increased resilience terrestrial and aquatic ecosystems;
7) The Project area presents an ocean star landscape with enhanced conservation/sustainable
management. The integrated management capacity of coastline ecosystems in Hainan Province and
the two project counties has been strengthened. From a social perspective, the Project involves
stakeholders to participate in a wide range of activities, such as ecological restoration activities such
as rural non-point source pollution control, which not only greatly improves the local ecological
environment, but also increases the income from the original land rent process or increases the
possibility of land income sharing by improving land utilization rate and improving farming
conditions.
31.      According to the "Hainan Province Coastal Zone and Marine Spatial Planning (2021-2035)",
in terms of spatial layout, marine functional zoning has been delineated, and the red line of marine
ecological protection has been delineated in the marine ecological space and marine development
and utilization space, accurately grasping the relationship between the integrity of the coastal
ecosystem and development and utilization, optimizing the layout of marine fisheries, sea and land
integrated transportation, coastal industry, coastal tourism and other industries in Hainan Province,
adhering to the unity of development and protection, and strictly abiding by the red line of ecological
protection. Therefore, there is no significant increase in regional negative cumulative impacts. In
addition, like the whole country, the ecological environment zoning control system in Hainan
Province and the two project counties has been basically established, and the ecological
environment zoning control system with global coverage and accurate and scientific has been initially
formed. The ecological environment zoning control plan based on the ecological environment control
unit, the ecological environment access list as the means, and the information platform as the
support has been formulated and implemented, and the accumulated ecological environment impact
can also be effectively controlled and managed.
3.5 Environmental and social risk ratings
32.       In accordance with the World Bank's World Bank Policy: Program-for-Results Financing
(August 2024), four criteria are used for environmental and social risk assessment of results-based
lending activities: (1) possible environmental and social impacts; (2) environmental and social
contextual risks, including risks that may lead to sustainability; (3) institutional capacity and
complexity risk; (4) Political and reputational risks. The analysis shows that the environmental and
social risk levels of the proposed project activities are different, and after a few activities with High
risks are excluded, the risk levels of other activities are Substantial, medium and low, which can be
reduced by implementing effective management measures. The following sections provide a general
description of the risk rating, which is analyzed in Annex 2 for a detailed analysis.
3.5.1 Possible environmental and social impacts
33.       According to the analysis of the environmental and social benefits and impacts of the Project
and the aforementioned sections, the Project will have significant positive benefits to the regional
environment and society through a series of activities such as ecological restoration, pollution control
and sustainable forest management, including pollutant emission reduction, soil erosion prevention
and     control,   soil    quality   improvement,      water     quality    improvement       in    major
estuaries/wetlands/lagoons, agricultural ecological environment improvement, rural irrigation and
production conditions improvement, urban and rural sewage treatment capacity enhancement, and
forest tree species structure optimization. These measures will significantly improve the ecosystem
function and human settlements quality in the Project area and provide long-term support for regional
ecological restoration. However, the types of project activities are diverse, and the spatial distribution

                                                   16
is wide, involving urban, rural and offshore areas, and some activities are close to ecologically
sensitive areas, and a certain scale of on-site construction, temporary land occupation and natural
resource management actions need to be carried out during the implementation process. Although
the project adopts a technical route based on nature-based solutions (NbS) and supplemented by
small scale projects, and the relevant departments of Hainan Province and the project county (district)
have experience in implementing similar ecological restoration and pollution control projects, local
and short-term adverse environmental and social impacts may still occur during the implementation
of the project. These impacts need to be effectively prevented, mitigated and managed through
mature technical measures and management systems. Considering the complexity of the type of
activity, the breadth of the area, ecological sensitivity, on-site disturbances during implementation,
the requirements of land leasing and stakeholder participation procedures, and the challenges of
cross-sectoral coordination, the environmental and social risks of this project are manageable but
cannot be ignored. Therefore, the overall environmental and social risk level of this project is set as
"Substantial”.
3.5.2 Environmental and social contextual risks
34.       In addition to policy research and other technical assistant activities covering a large area,
the activities involving various industries and non-point source pollution control under this project are
basically carried out in urban and rural areas in Changjiang and Lingshui counties, which are habitats
after frequent changes in human activities. Such pollution control activities will not be located in
areas with Substantial environmental sensitivity.
35.      All kinds of ecological restoration activities under this project will be concentrated in coastal
zone areas or rivers, estuaries, bays, lagoons, coastal waters and sandy coastlines within 200
meters of coastal defense forests and natural parks, and may also involve provincial, municipal and
county-level nature reserves (experimental areas) and provincial, municipal and county-level scenic
spots (it will not be clear until the specific site selection and line selection of the activities are
determined). Most of these areas have been designated as ecological protection red lines. In view
of the fact that the relevant departments of the Chinese and Hainan provincial governments have
established and continuously improved the ecological protection red line system and nature reserve
system based on the relevant laws, regulations and policies of the state and Hainan Province, and
formulated the "Hainan Province Ecological Protection Red Line Access Management Catalogue
(Revised)", any activities carried out within the ecological protection red line require the special
demonstration of limited human activities in the ecological protection red line, and the institutional
settings and supervision methods of the relevant departments of the provincial to county government
to control the activities within the ecological protection red line are continuously updated and
improved. It also helps its ability to become more and more perfect, and can effectively control the
adverse effects and risks of activities within the ecological protection red line on various natural
habitats that have been included in the ecological protection red line. In addition, these protected
areas were established years ago before the project identification stage and there is no livelihood
and production activities within these areas.
36.      The Project planning activities do not involve large-scale land acquisition and resettlement,
the vast majority of projects are implemented and carried out on state-owned land, and a small
number of new facilities may lead to collective land acquisition of no more than 50 acres. In principle,
all new construction activities will give priority to the use of collective unused land and collective
construction land, and try to avoid the occupation of agricultural land. Only when the site does not
meet the design requirements will agricultural land be requisitioned. Various forms of land use have
established corresponding management systems in Hainan Province, forming a comprehensive
legal framework, policy system, approval and documentation and supervision processes for land
acquisition, land leasing, temporary land use, resettlement and livelihood restoration. Among the
projects implemented by counties and cities every year, projects in various forms of land use are
widely implemented locally, following the principle of relocation, various compensation and
resettlement are in place, and the policies/processes are open during the implementation process,
and the overall implementation performance is good. In addition, although some project activities will
be located in areas with many ethnic minorities, after investigation, no social conflicts related to the
ethnic minorities groups and Han have been found in the project area, ethnic minorities and Han
Chinese are basically integrated, and there is no special difference in daily life and work. Government

                                                   17
departments have widely publicized the treatment of non-point source pollution in rural areas, but
sometimes there is a lack of professional guidance. These problems will be solved by carrying out
activities such as farmer training, facility improvement, management and supervision improvement.
37.      Based on the background impact of the above activities of this project, as well as the
potential environmental and social impacts/risks arising from other ecological restoration and
pollution control activities in the government planning, the overall cumulative environmental and
social impacts and background risk levels of this project are "Substantial” 。
3.5.3 Institutional capacity and complexity risk
38.       The environmental and social impact management of this project will involve many
government departments, such as development and reform, finance, agriculture and rural areas,
water affairs, ecological environment, forestry, natural resources and planning, maritime, human
resources and social security, emergency management, health, market supervision, culture and
tourism, civil affairs, women's federation and other government departments and multiple
stakeholders, as well as groups affected by policies such as land use and water rights, as well as
relevant institutions that may have an impact on the implementation of the plan or have decision-
making power. Each department is managed in accordance with existing laws and regulations, and
corresponding institutions and personnel are set up. As a government department, its institutional
personnel arrangements and budgets are guaranteed. In the implementation of this project, all
relevant industry authorities will implement activities and manage corresponding environmental and
social risks in accordance with their respective responsibilities under the overall guidance of the
central and provincial governments and under the coordination of provincial project offices. Due to
the wide coverage of this project activities, involving different regions and many industries, strong
communication and coordination between different departments are necessary to effectively manage
the Project activities and related environmental and social impacts. If any department, especially in
domestic sewage management, agricultural non-point source pollution management, ecological
protection red line, etc., lacks effective communication and coordination, it will reduce the
effectiveness of the entire project implementation and the operation of the environmental and social
management system. Despite the experience and ongoing work on IPF projects in Hainan Province,
there is still a lack of experience in result-based financing (PforR), such as recruiting qualified third-
party verifiers. This situation is compounded by the fact that the Provincial Department of Natural
Resources and Changjiang and Lingshui counties have not previously participated in the
implementation of World Bank-funded projects. As a result, the overall institutional capacity and
complexity risk level of the project is "Substantial"
3.5.4 Reputational and political risks
39.            The Project will help promote the restoration of degraded coastal ecosystems, reduce
environmental pollution, protect the ecological environment, improve urban and rural sewage
management, and improve farmers' living standards. Therefore, the overall political and reputational
risk level of this project is "low”.
3.5.5 Comprehensive environmental and social risks
40.      Considering the above four factors, combined with the risk screening results and the
proposed risk management measures, the overall environmental and social risk level of this project
is "Substantial ".

4. Assessment of Environmental Management Systems Relevant to the
   Project

     Framework
41. Adverse environmental impacts/risks resulting from Program activities identified in Chapter 3
can be grouped into three: 1) adverse impacts/risks of environmental pollution; 2) adverse impacts
and risks to the ecosystem (both natural protected areas and areas prone to soil erosion) delineated
into ERLs; 3) impact of OHS to employees, as well as the health and safety of surrounding
communities.
42. To manage these environmental impacts/risks, following environmental management systems
(EMSs) are analyzed based on information obtained from interviews with the Program stakeholders
and the data collected (See Table 4-1 below).

4.2 EIA and Follow-Up Management System
43. Following Government authorities are the key ones responsible for managing and controling
impacts/risks of environmental pollution, ecological degradation (including damage to natural
habitats) potentially resulted from the Program activities during construction/restoration, and during
operation.
⚫        Regulatory Authorities for Environmental Pollution: DEE/EEBs (the regulatory oversight one),
         plus: 1) sectoral regulatory authorities for potential environmental pollution, such as DWR/WRBs
         (pollution from urban and rural domestic wastewater), DARA/ARABs (NPS pollution from
         agricultural farmland)
⚫        Regulatory Authorities for Ecological Conservation: Multi-levels coordinated authorities,
         including DEE/EEBs (oversight), DNR/NRBs (ERL), FBs (protected areas and forests),
         DWR/WRBs (soil and water conservation).
44. Legal framework that these authorities relied on to manage environmental impacts/risks brought
about the Program activities, and implementation mechanisms, management organizational
structure, specific management measures and performance are assessed below.
4.2.1. Environmental Pollution Management Sub-System
4.2.1.1 Applicable Legal and Regulatory Framework
45. Based on the Environmental Protection Law the People’s Republic of China (PRC) and Marine
Environmental Protection Law of the PRC , China has established numerous laws and regulations
related to the prevention and control of water pollution, air pollution, solid waste and soil pollution,
and noise pollution, etc., plus Hainan local regulations formulated by Hainan Province in accordance
with these national laws and in light of the local actual conditions and characteristics. These laws &
regulations have provided a legal basis for the above-mentioned authorities to manage the potential
environmental pollution impacts/risks of the Project's PforR activities.
