56. Besides exercising regulatory through strict review and approval process during the early
preparation stage of project activities, these major government authorities also incorporate post-
approval supervision into their daily management work by implementing such mechanisms as ERLs,
natural protected areas, eco-environment zoning control.
57. DNRP/NRPBs are responsible for the formulation and implementation of territorial space
planning. They are the key regulatory agency for delineation of ERLs and supervision of the main
ERLs mechanism by means of control of land use, particularly when pre-reviewing and final approval
of land use for construction projects. Meanwhile, they take the lead and collaborate with other
relevant government authorities to strengthen the supervision and inspection of the implementation
of the ERLs mechanism.
⚫      Delineating ERL scientifically: DNRP/NRPBs regard the delineation of the “three zones and
       three lines” as their core framework in their territorial spatial planning. Following Guidelines on
       Integrating the Delineation of "Three Regions and Three Lines", in parallel with other provinces,
       Hainan initiated the formulation, approval and implementation of territorial space planning in
       2019. Provincial DNRP was responsible for delineating the three control lines, i.e., the ERLs,
       boundaries for protection of permanent basic farmland, and urban development boundaries (the
       so called “three lines and three zones” 16 . During this process, MDNR, together with MEE,
       National FB jointly issued the Notice on Strengthening the Management of Ecological Protection
       Red Lines (2022), requiring the ERLs delineation be the important part of the “three zones and
       three lines” delineation. The result of the delineated ERLs was reviewed and approved by
       Hainan Government. The delineated ERLs cover both terrestrial ERLs and coastal ERLs. Areas
       within the scope of terrestrial ERLs are biodiversity conservation zones, water source protection

15 Coastal Windbreak Forest refer to the forests within the ecological conservation red line (in sandy beach areas, extending 200 meters inland from the average high

tide line of the spring tide)
16 “Three zones and three lines” refer to three types of territorial space: urban space, agricultural space and ecological space, and corresponding three control lines

delineated in urban space, agricultural space and ecological space: i.e., urban development boundary, permanent basic farmland and ERLs.

                                                                                                                 40
    and water conservation zones, water & soil conservation zones, coastal ecologically sensitive
    zones, flood control and regulating zones, tourist function zones and others, covering total area
    of 11535 km2, accounting for 33.5% of the provincial territorial area; The delineated offshore
    ERLs cover total area of 8316.6 km2, accounting for 35.1% of the provincial marine area. Some
    activities to be supported by the Project in Changjiang County and Lingshui County will be
    implemented in parts of national parks (including mangrove wetland park, marine park) areas
    with concentrated distribution coral reefs, seagrass beds boarding important estuaries, natural
    shorelines. The location of these activities is within the scope of the delineated ERLs.
⚫   Strengthening Dynamic Supervision: Once the ERLs areas are determined, no unauthorized
    adjustments are allowed. DNRP/NRPBs, in collaboration with DEE/EEBs and FBs at all levels,
    will use the "one map" of territorial space planning to conduct dynamic monitoring and timely
    early warning of the ERLs. Based on the monitoring of resource and environmental carrying
    capacity, the evaluation of the importance of ecological protection, “once in 5 years assessment
    of the actual implementation of the spatial planning, the ERLs are regularly evaluated and
    adjusted to include other areas that are of extremely significant ecological functions, extremely
    fragile in ecology, with potential important ecological value, such as waters, wetlands,
    mangroves, seagrass beds, and coral reefs, into the scope of ERLs . Hainan Provincial DNRP
    has established a “Hainan Province's Spatial Information Platform for Land Use and Spatial
    Planning”, which include a “post-approval supervision module.           Once any abnormality is
    detected in the satellite images, relevant provincial and county-level government authorities will
    conduct field investigations. If any areas within the scope of ERLs are illegally encroached,
    county-level government authorities will order the violators to make corrections, thereby
    establishing a supervision mechanism that combines satellite images with dynamic law
    enforcement. For those who violate regulations and conduct human activities within the ERLs,
    the relevant Housing and Urban-Rural Bureau, FB, WRB, ARAB, or the Integrated Law
    Enforcement Bureau at or above the county levels, shall handle the cases in accordance with
    their respective duties legally.
⚫   Routine Regulatory of NRPBs at County level: at the county level, there are territorial spatial
    planning section/position (2-3 staff), ecological restoration section/position (2 staff), they are
    responsible for organizing delineation and implementing supervision of the ERLs, undertaking
    the review of land use that may trigger ERLs, developing and implementing ecological
    restoration plans within the jurisdiction.
⚫   Prior regulatory: when reviewing applications for land use for construction projects, they strictly
    control land use that trigger the ERLs in accordance with national and local laws & regulation
    relevant to the ERLs. In case that encroachment of ERLs is unavoidable, they organize experts,
    invite representatives from Provincial relevant government authorities, to review justification
    reports on the limited human activities within the scope of ERLs, and issue the initial recognition
    opinions on the said justification reports, subject to Provincial Government final approval.
⚫   Post-supervision: in their daily work, they conduct supervision precisely on the ERLs by means
    of remote sensing satellites and other geographic information systems (GIS) on terrestrial areas,
    remote sensing satellites + GIS, plus aerial inspection on marine areas uncovered by satellite
    remote sensing. The MNR uses dedicated satellites to monitor the changes in the national-wide
    terrestrial space at any time. Once any land parcels are observed to be non-compliance with
    the requirements of the ERLs, the target can be promptly identified, notified via provincial DNRP
    to the County NRPB, who, together with the county's Integrated Law Enforcement Bureau and
    relevant authorities, verify the case, order the violators to take corrective action, or to punish the
    violators. For example, in 2023, Changjiang County NRB conducted 58 regular inspections and
    patrols to the marine area. During these inspections, any suspected issues discovered were
    promptly informed the relevant authorities for field verification and corrective actions, carried out
    10 aerial inspections to areas uncovered by satellite remote sensing information. The results of
    aerial inspections were documented and mapped promptly for reporting to DNRP. When notified
    by DNRP of suspected cases, the NRPB field 12 surveys and the verification results were
    promptly provided feedback. Their daily work helped maintain the harmony and stability of the
    county's marine and efficiently completed the rectification work for the national marine special
    inspection.

                                                   41
58. FBs: are the government line authorities for managing forests and natural protected areas, as
well as one of the PIUs of activities to be supported by the Project.
⚫       Hainan Provincial FB: there are forest resources and wetland protection management division
        (5 staff), ecological conservation and restoration division (5 staff) in place in the FB. The two
        divisions are responsible for developing and issuing through Hainan Provincial Forestry Chief
        Office Work Plan for Sustainable Forest Management in Hainan Province 2024-2025, The Work
        Plan aims to further upgrade forest quality through tenting of young and mid-aged forests,
        rehabilitation of degraded forests of low productivity, coastal windbreak forest enrichment
        planting, and promotion of natural forest regeneration. The natural protected areas
        management division is responsible for issuing administrative documents, such as Management
        Measures for Local-level Natural Parks in Hainan Province, Opinions on the Recognition of
        Specialized Issues in Cases Involving the Destruction of Forests and Wild Animal and Plant
        Resources and so on in accordance with National Management Measures for Nature Reserves
        (Trial). In the supervision of nature protected areas. If DNRP identified abnormalities in the
        dynamic satellite images within the scope of nature protected areas or coastal windbreak forest,
        they will collaborate with the DNRP and go to the field for investigation. Once violations of
        encroachment of natural protected area, or coastal windbreak forest delineated within the scope
        of ERLs. Relevant government authorities at county level will order the violators to make
        corrections. Hainan Forestry Resources Monitoring Center (Hainan Forest Pests Control and
        Quarantine Station, 16 staff) under the Provincial FB is responsible for coordinating the
        prevention, control, and forecasting of forest pests across the province, as well as supervising
        the quarantine procedures and laboratory establishment, carrying out pests control measures
        to minimize the risk of invasion of potential dangerous harmful organisms.
⚫       Routine management works of FBs at county level are to do with management of natural
        protected areas by implementing the mechanism of natural protected areas, depending on the
        natural protected areas mechanism. In cases there are destruction of forests, grasslands and
        wetlands in the county or violation of the management regulations of nature reserves and scenic
        spots in the county, the County FBs, in collaboration with the County Integrated Law
        Enforcement Bureau to impose a severe punishment to the violators in accordance with the
        Forest Law, Grassland Law, Wetland Protection Law, Regulations on Nature Reserves,
        Regulations on Scenic Spots, Regulations on the Implementation of the Forest Law and other
        laws and regulations according to their duties. Their management work related to the activities
        of this project includes:
    ◼     Make efforts to minimize incidence rate of forest pests and fire through the prevention and
          control of forest pests and fires (as detailed in Section 4.2.2.3) to effectively avoid the
          potential harm to biodiversity caused by the spread of pests, thereby, and to ensure the
          functions of forest ecosystem services (such as windbreak, water and soil conservation, air
          purification, and carbon sequestration, etc.).
    ◼     Protection of coastal windbreak forest, forestry resources management and
          rehabilitation of degraded forest: under a typical country-level FB, there are forestry
          resources and wetland protection section/position (2 staff), ecological public forest
          management section/position (2 staff) + township forestry service stations (8 staff), forest
          rangers (114 staff distributed at non-commercial forest guard stations) in place. Under the
          overall coordination of the Forest Chief Office established under the forest chief mechanism,
          a dynamic supervision approach combining manual patrols (forest rangers and forest chiefs
          at all levels are required to conduct daily patrols) and satellite image technology is adopted.
          These efforts effectively safeguard the safety of forest resources and promote the steady
          increase of forest coverage rate and forest stock volume. In accordance with the plan, all
          forest plots zoned as coastal windbreak forests are fully put under grid-based management.
          Management and protection agreements are signed to clarify and fulfill management and
          protection responsibilities. Joint prevention and control mechanisms are established with the
          Forest Chief Offices of all towns and townships. Forest rangers are organized to carry out
          daily publicity, observation and patrol work. Meanwhile, automatic voice announcers, water
          storage tanks, fire prevention publicity materials and signboards are installed at the
          intersections of key coastal windbreak forest areas.

                                                     42
    ◼     Management of Natural Protected Areas: This work is undertaken by the Nature Protected
          Area Management and Forestry Development Office of the county-level FBs (2 staff members)
          and the respective nature reserve management centers in the county (3–6 staff per center).
          Their responsibilities include organizing the construction of infrastructure required for the
          natural reserves management, monitoring, and scientific research, conducting daily patrols
          and management in the natural reserves, and carrying out science popularization and
          publicity activities in the reserves.
    ◼     Ecosystem Protection and Ecological Restoration：This work is the responsibility of the
          Ecological Restoration Section (1 staff) and the Forest Resources and Wetland Protection
          Section (2 staff) in place under the FBs. It is carried out progressively and combined with
          daily patrols in accordance with the Special Action Plan for the Ecological Protection and
          Restoration of Mangroves in Hainan Province. For example, since 2021, Changjiang County
          has implemented and completed projects of the mangrove ecological restoration in the Zhubi
          River Estuary Wetland of Haiwei Town. A total of 1,414.17 mu of wetland has been restored,
          including 1,237 mu of mangroves planted, as well as 170 mu of Casuarina equisetifolia
          trees—species that are windbreak and sand-fixation capable, salt-tolerant, and suitable for
          tropical coastal zones. Another example, Lingshui County has innovatively adopted NbS
          through the integrated restoration of seagrass beds and mangroves. It has carried out a full
          chain of interventions including pollution reduction, natural shoreline restoration, ecological
          protection and restoration of mangrove, seagrass bed and coral reef ecosystems, protection
          of the Tanka ecological culture, and realization of the value of ecological products. This has
          established a collaborative governance model of "coastal zone ecology-society-economy".
          Within the 32-square-kilometer lagoon area, the county has achieved the multiple benefits of
          improved ecological environment quality, improved community livelihoods, and innovation in
          cultural inheritance. This case was selected as a typical case of marine ecological protection
          and restoration by MNR in 2025.
59. DWR/WRBs are regulatory authorities for water and soil conservation of construction projects,
and the county-level WRBs are PIUs of river ecological restoration activities to be supported by the
Project. There are water & soil conservation and reservoir resettlement service section (2 staff),
water resource and river/lake section (2 staff), who are responsible for following works related to
ecological protection/restoration activities to be supported by the Project:
⚫       Strictly Implement the Management Regulations of Soil and Water Conservation Plans:
        Through the implementation of the classified management mechanism for soil and water
        conservation of construction projects, the water and soil conservation "three simultaneous"
        mechanism. They carry out or assist DWR in conducting technical reviews and acceptance of
        soil and water conservation plans in accordance with laws and regulations. Daily work also
        includes developing county-level soil and water conservation programs, assisting or entrusting
        third-party consulting agencies to carry out soil and water conservation supervision for
        construction projects, and guiding the implementation of key soil and water conservation
        projects.
⚫       Rivers/Lakes Protection and Ecological Restoration: They formulate workplan on the
        comprehensive promotion of river and lake chief mechanism, guide the delineation and
        management of river and lake shorelines and water bodies connection within river/lake
        watershed. They supervise river/lake chiefs at all local levels to implement river management
        and prepare plans for river protection and utilization. (For example, the on-going project
        ecological restoration of Donghai river, a first-level tributary of Shilu River entering into marine,
        is expected to restore 40 macrophytes in the river, reducing pollutants of total phosphorus by 4
        t/d). tons per year through the restoration of more than 40 acres of aquatic vegetation in the river
        waters.
60.     DEE/EEBs: very similar to environmental pollution management system, are responsible
for managing and controlling ecologically sensitive areas that may be triggered by planning and
construction projects at front-end by implementing mechanisms of eco-environment zoning control
and ecological environment access list under the environmental impact assessment system to
reduce the decision-making risks of adverse effects on area with important ecological function,
ecologically sensitive or vulnerable areas in the early preparation phase of the Projects. The shared

                                                       43
information on eco-environmental monitoring and assessment carried out in collaboration with
DNRP/NRPBs, FBs, DWR/WRBs, have laid a good foundation for the protection and restoration of
various nature reserves and natural habitats. Haian DEE has uniformly established an application
system for the ecological environment zoning control plan and the ecological environment access
list. DEE/EEBs at all levels carry out ecological environment supervision and management on
activities within the scope of ERLs. They are responsible for implementing, tracking and assessing,
the ecological environment access lists, and establishing the application system of the said List
under eco-environment zoning control mechanism. The MEE has established a national ERLs
supervision platform, which is backed up by satellite remote sensing plus ground ecosystem
monitoring stations to monitor human interference activities in real time, and circulate dynamic
images to provincial DEEs once in every two months, from which, DEE/EEBs in Hainan can identify
acts that violate the ERLs by comparing the images and conducting on-site investigations, we have
identified and handle cases in accordance with laws and regulations
61.        Routine Management Works of EEBs at County-Level: There are EIA & emission
management section (1-4 staff) in place, who are prepare and update the County-level Eco-
environmental Zoning Control Scheme and their environmental access lists under the guidance of
“Technical Proposal for Municipalities and Counties to Update Eco-environmental Zoning Control
Scheme” issued by Provincial DEE, serving for Plan-EIAs and construction projects EIAs. It is
required for construction project EIAs that the Project investor and the EIA consultancy firm make
justification of the Project compliance with the said Scheme and the List. The reviewer and approval
authorities of the EIA documents shall make verification of the justification and judgment of the
compliance by overlapping the map of selected sites or alignment with Eco-environmental Zoning
Control Map accessible from the public platform. DEE/EEBs are working on baseline survey of
biodiversity. They work together with NRPBs, FBs and grass-root teams to conduct follow-up
regulatory. In the cases of damage to eco-environment within the county, EEBs, in collaboration
with the County Integrated Law Enforcement Bureau to impose severe penalties in accordance with
the relevant laws and regulations such as the Environmental Protection Law, Environmental Impact
Assessment Law, Water Pollution Prevention and Control Law, and Marine Environmental Protection
Law based on our respective duties.
4.2.2.4 Assessment
62.       The objective of the Project is to conserve and restore coastal ecosystems. Activities under
RA 2 being of the Project will be carried out in modified habitats that are highly affected by human
activities. The construction of various domestic sewage networks, WWTPs and WWTFs, agricultural
NPS pollution control facilities for recycling and multi-purpose utilization of agricultural mulch, crop
straw, packaging wastes will not trigger critical nature protected areas habitats. The activity itself will
be beneficial to the improvement of the ecological environment in urban and rural areas and farmland
and reduce the stress on the marine ecological environment. Some Activities for ecosystems
restoration under RA2 of the Project will trigger the ERLs where natural and critical habitats exist.
During the preparation of the Project, the WB team confirmed through on-site visits, interviews with
stakeholders, and extensive data review, that Hainan Province and the two Program counties have
established a pretty mature ecological conservation management system based on improving laws,
regulations and management systems at the national and provincial levels. From the strict control
of early justification and approval at the preparation phase to the dynamic supervision mechanism
supported by remote sensing images and on-site verification at the provincial and county levels
during implementation, ecological conservation management system demonstrated that there is a
strong ecosystem management capability that can effectively prevent and control adverse ecological
impacts potentially arising from the Project activities. The System is with WB’s core Principles on
Natural Habitats, and also consistent with the WB ESF-ESS) 1 – Assessment and Management of
Environmental and Social Risks and Impacts, and ESS 6 – Biodiversity Conservation and
Sustainable Management of Natural Resources.


4.3 Health and Safety Management System
63.       In view of the potential health and safety risks brought about by the activities of the Project
identified in Table 4-1, the following government authorities involved in the management of the OHS

                                                    44
of workers, operators engaged in facilities construction, forest and crops pests’ prevention & control,
operations on and above waters during construction and restoration and operation:
a.     HCs (for OHS management), EMBs (for Emergency Response Plan and Rescue), plus
b.     Relevant authorities who are the PIUs of the activities to be supported by the Project with OHS
       risks, including FBs (for OHS management of workers/operators engaged in forest management,
       ecosystem restoration activities), ARABs (for OHS management of workers/operators engaged
       in the safe use of pesticides), WRBs (for OHS management of workers/operators engaged in
       WWTPs and WWTFs O&M, and EMBs (for management of fire control and safety and
       emergency safety) .

4.3.3 Institutional Organization and Performance
65.      Multi-sectors authorities joint efforts to safeguard health and safety: In principle, the
PIUs of the Project (WRBs, ARABs, FBs, NRPBs at county level), as employers, are responsible for
their respective employees’ OHS during construction or restoration, operation and maintenance or
daily patrol work, through 1) publicity and education; 2) provision their operators with PPE (masks,
goggles, gloves, life jackets for underwater work, etc.); 3) Implementing OHS "three simultaneous"
mechanism; 4) Obtaining relevant permits (such as water and underwater operation permits); 5)
having the health of their respective employees examined regularly; 6) Purchasing OHS insurance
and other means and measures. Meanwhile, these sector authorities are responsible for
safeguarding communities’ health and safety that may be brought about in the process of crop and
forest pest and disease control and forest fire prevention & control. The HCs and EMBs provide
security for the prevention & control and handling of occupational diseases and the response to
emergencies outstanding incidents.
66.       DARA/ARABs are agricultural sectoral regulatory authority of farmers/operators OHS and
village community health & safety. Their main responsibilities are reflected in the process of
agricultural production. Under a county ARAB, there are agricultural development service centers,
agricultural plant protection stations, technology extension centers, etc., in place, who prevent OHS
risks for farmers/operators and surrounding communities through the following measures:
⚫   Pesticides Safety Management: They advocate prioritizing more environmentally friendly and
    IPM methods, such as physical or biotechnological measures, to replace the use of chemical
    pesticides. They recommend using low-toxicity, high-efficiency pesticides. They supervise
    pesticide producers for registration of their pesticide products and obtaining production licenses.
    They supervise pesticide sellers for obtaining sales licenses. Pesticide users are required to
    comply with regulations on the safe use and storage of pesticides, and to use necessary PPE

                                                              48
    (masks, goggles, gloves, etc.) to avoid accidents when applying pesticides. Support professional
    prevention and control service entities to carry out professional prevention and control services
    through government purchase services, funds, material subsidies, etc., and provide technical
    training for them.
⚫   Promotion of Standardized & Specialized Pest Control Service: Compared with vast farmers,
    cooperatives, farms and other crop planting entities, the unified service for pest control provided
    by specialized service entities through government (ARAB) purchasing, the selection,
    application of pesticides are more professional, scientific and reasonable, the PPE of operators
    is more standardized, and the recycling of pesticide packaging waste is easier, which can greatly
    reduce the risk of famers/operators’ exposure to chemical pesticides.
⚫   Farmers’ health awareness education: In the program of ARAB for provision of trainings to high-
    quality farmers, regular training courses on OHS are included to raise farmers awareness on
    health, know-how to prevent occupational diseases, and identify and respond to health risks.
67.       FBs: are the most important sectoral regulatory authority to safeguard OHS of forestry
practitioners. Their main responsibilities are reflected in the construction of coastal windbreak forests
and forest management.
⚫   Forestry pests and forest fire prevention and control: There are fire prevention section (2
    staff), plant inspection section of forestry service centers (3 staff), forest guard stations at
    township level (2 technicians/station), plus a large number of grass-root forest rangers in place
    under county FB. Each forest zone is accessible to forest patrol roads, installed with
    watchtowers, automatic voice announcers, fire prevention publicity and warning signs and other
    facilities. These facilities can be borrowed by above-mentioned entities for monitoring,
    quarantine, control of forestry pests. Specific daily work includes forestry pest epidemic
    investigation, sampling and having samples re-examined by the third certified party in case of
    an epidemic, quarantine inspection to tree species that are to be introduced or removed during
    the nursery and forest management processes to avoid the spread of pest epidemics through
    preventive measures. The FBs have also prepared their respective Emergency Responsive Plan
    for Forestry Pest Emergencies. In the event of an epidemic (such as the common coconut leaf
    beetle in Changjiang County), in line with the principle of who manages, who control, forest
    management entities are guided to adopt IPM approach, dominated by biological control (such
    as releasing parasitic wasps), then, select high-efficiency and low-toxicity pesticides for pest
    control under the guidance of the "List of Commonly Used Pesticides for Garden and Forestry
    Plants" issued by National FB. The county FBs organize and carry out forest fire prevention
    publicity. In the event of a fire, the FB will fully cooperate with the EMB and all towns and villages
    to organize forest fire fighting. For example, in Changjiang County, all resources of institutions
    and facilities are mobilized to manage forest pest and forest fire effectively, resulting in the
    presence of pests without disasters. In recent years, the forest pest disaster rate is controlled
    at 3.08‰, and the forest fire control rate was less than 0.3‰. Therefore, the county’s forest
    resources are sustainably developed and maintained, the health and safety of communities are
    prevented from hazards potentially caused by forest emergencies or disasters
⚫   FBs organize and provide training on forest fire fighting skills and safety knowledge at least once
    a year, purchase personal accident insurance for forest rangers. As a result, forest rangers
    have a high awareness of prevention and response measures for OHS such as falls, bites and
    heat stress in tropical forests.
⚫   Relevant enterprises and cooperatives for forest management are responsible for providing
    necessary PPE employees, carrying out publicity and education on OHS awareness, and
    regularly have their employees’ health regularly examined, purchasing OHS insurance for
    employees.
68.      HCs: at county-level have set up sections responsible for OHS. These sections work on
proposing and implementation of policies and standards related to OHS in the county, coordinating
the prevention and treatment of occupational diseases, organizing the publicity and education of
occupational disease prevention and control and popularize the knowledge of occupational disease
prevention and control, organizing OHS monitoring, special investigation and OHS risk assessment
management of occupational groups. In addition, there are occupational health examination

                                                   49
agencies registered and licensed in Provincial HC, staffed with at least one licensed physician with
occupational disease diagnosis qualification, at least 3 years of working experience on occupational
disease screening and examination, familiar with the relevant standards of occupational health and
occupational disease diagnosis. As per regulations of National HC, the employer shall organize
preservice, in-service and post-service occupational health examinations for the workers who are
exposed to occupational disease-inductive factors and inform the workers of the examination results
in writing. The employer shall bear the expenses for on-the-job health examinations.
69.       EMBs shoulder the important task of preventing and resolving major safety risks, from risky
industry supervision to accident investigation and handling, from emergency plan formulation to
emergency rescue coordination, to protect safe production and disaster response in an all-round
way. The provincial EMB prepares emergency plans for water and fishery emergency plans in
Hainan Province, and the County EMBs prepare forest fire emergency plans, coordinate and
command emergency rescue teams, coordinate professional forces such as fire brigade to
participate in rescue, organize emergency response to disaster sites, and carry out forest fire
prevention, overall monitoring and early warning, and disaster reduction capacity building. EMBs are
also responsible for guiding sectoral authorities at all levels to establish an emergency plan system,
organizing the preparation of overall emergency plans and special plans, and promoting emergency
drills and the construction of emergency evacuation facilities.
70.        Maritime Department is responsible for the registration, training, examination and
certification management of the competency qualifications of personnel working on maritime facilities.
They are to provide safeguard service for transportation vehicles to be used in the offshore
operations for seagrass bed & coral reef restoration activities under the Project, and training to the
personnel engaged in operation in water and underwater.
4.3.4 Assessment
71.      Governments at all levels in China and Hainan Province and relevant PIUs of the Project
have established a relatively complete health and safety management system, which can effectively
manage the potential risks that may be brought to the OHS of employees and surrounding
communities’ health and safety related to the Project activities, such as wastewater management,
forest and crop plants pests control. The system is aligned with the WBG EHS Guidelines for Annual
and Perennial Crop Production, and for Environmental Hazardous Materials Management covering
Good International Industrial Practices (GIIPs). The government authorities for managing and
regulatory of health and safety are well-staffed with management capacities to take their respective
responsibilities for managing health and safety issues under the Project.        In viewing that the
ecosystems restoration activities on coastal zone under the Project involve operations in water or
underwater, requiring cross-sectoral cooperation from maritime department, and in order to ensure
OHS of operators (including operators from construction contractors, monitoring or survey teams,
etc.,) working in water or underwater, an action plan (PAP) is proposed by this ESSA, i.e., in addition
of obtaining permits for operation in water or under water, the operators shall be provided with
continuous safety to enhance their safety awareness and ensure that relevant OHS procedures &
requirements are implemented in practice.
4.4 Analysis of Environmental Management Capacity, by PforR Policy Core Principle
72.      After assessing the two EMSs, namely the EIA and follow-up management system,
(including sub-system of environmental pollution management, sub-system of ecological
conservation management), and health and safety management system, the consistency with the
Bank's core principles and elements is analyzed in this section with details presented in Annex 3.
Core Principle #1: EIA and management. Program environmental management systems are
designed to promote environmental sustainability in the program design; avoid, minimize, or mitigate
adverse impacts; and promote informed decision-making related to a program’s environmental
effects.
73.     China and Hainan Province have established a complete legal and regulatory framework
on environmental management based on Environmental Protection Law, numerous environmental
management laws, bylaws, technical guidelines, standards, such as the Environmental Impact
Assessment Law, the Water Pollution Prevention and Control Law, the Regulations on the

                                                  50
Environmental Protection Management of Construction Projects, the Catalogue for Classified
Management EIA of Construction Projects, the Technical Guidelines for EIA (including more than 20
pollution impact categories and ecological impact categories) and environmental standards. In the
field of marine environmental management, there are articles on marine ecological protection and
land-based pollution control under Marine Environmental Protection Law in place. In the field of
agricultural NPS pollution management related to corps protection and fertilization, there are
Regulations on Crop Pest Control and Pesticides Management Regulations in place. The National
and Hainan local laws & regulations, policies, management measures, technical guidelines, sectoral
standards, etc., provided legal and regulatory framework and implementation mechanisms for
carrying out EIA and follow-up regulatory. Particularly, the eco-environment zoning control, a
comprehensive mechanism established backed up by the legal framework in China and Hainan
Province, imposes restrictions on projects with severe environment risks from entering at preparation
stage. Tt has become the first line of defense for preserving green mountains and clear waters.
74.       China and Hainan Province have been implementing comprehensive EIA system, covering
environmental screening, alternatives analysis, rational analysis of selected sites, assessment of
impacts (including positive and negative, long-term and short-term, direct and indirect, and
cumulative impacts), mitigation measures, institutional arrangement and responsibilities, estimated
cost for environmental management, public participation, information disclosure. From early stage
environmental screening to environmental impact assessment (in terms of positive and negative,
long-term and short-term, direct and indirect and cumulative), from strategic EIA (including Plan-EIA
and Regional-EIA) to implement eco-environment zoning control mechanism, the EIA are carried out
to assess and avoid potential significant adverse environmental impact directly, indirectly and
cumulatively) of regional development plans and proposed construction projects. The EIA also
propose countermeasures to reduce and mitigate adverse impacts identified.              To meet the
requirements specified by Guidelines for EIA, the EIA documents shall include a sub-section on
environmental management, including institutional arrangement, responsibilities assigned to
relevant agencies, cost estimation and sources of the funds, monitoring plan (including elements,
parameters to be monitored, monitoring timing and frequency, etc.) If adverse impact to
environmental sensitive receptors (such as residential areas and so on), the local EEB will
recommend the Project developer/investor to carry out public engagement. As per The Scheme for
Public Disclosure of Environmental Impact Assessment Information for Construction Projects. It is
required that the Project developer/investor disclose such information as selected sites and relevant
environmental data during construction and operation. These procedures, requirements on EIA,
together with lots of examples of EIA documents, EIA approval documents collected by the Bank
task team on project similar to the Project activities as evidences, have demonstrated that there is
a good practice of EIA system, consistency with the WB core principles, and consistency with ESS1-
Assessment and Management of Environmental and Social Risks and Impacts under the WB ESF.
75.        Under EIA and follow-up management system, after excluding activities with Substantial
environmental risk (listed in Chapter 3), EIA-forms will be prepared for urban and rural wastewater
management activities, agricultural NPS management activities to be supported by the Project, as
per Catalogue for Classified EIA Management. These EIA-forms will be subject to the county EEBs’
review before administrative approval. Before commissioning, environmental acceptance check at
completion to ensure wastes treatment facilities are constructed in parallel with the main project.
O&M companies will apply for pollutants discharge permits from EEBs. During operation, the
facilities constructed under the Project activities will be subject to regulatory of EEBs who rely on the
pollutant discharge permits management platform established by MEE and environmental
monitoring networks and random sampling or field inspection. The performance of O&M companies
for urban and rural wastewater collection and treatment will be examined by county WRBs. In order
to improve efficiency of rural WWTFs to fill the gap observed in rural wastewater management, an
action plan (PAP) is proposed by ESSA (see Chapter 7).
Core Principle #2: Natural habitats and Physical Cultural Resource Protection. Program
environmental management systems are designed to avoid, minimize, or mitigate adverse impacts
on natural habitats and physical cultural resources resulting from the program. Program activities
that involve the significant conversion or degradation of critical natural habitats or critical physical
cultural heritage are not eligible for PforR financing.


                                                   51
76.       China and Hainan Province have formulated a set of laws & regulations on natural
ecological conservation and management, such as Wetland Protection Law, Wildlife Protection Law,
Regulations on Wild Plant Protection, Regulations on Nature Reserves, and Opinions on Delineating
and Strictly Uphold ERLs etc. Hainan Province has brought critical or natural habitats into the scope
of ERLs that are strictly conserved and managed. Ecological factors (including critical habitats and
biodiversity) are important sensitive receptors to be identified and assessed in EIA, and ecological
impact assessment is one of the important components of EIA. At a project proposal and early EIA
stage, DNRP/NRPBs, DEE/EEBs will strictly implement the ERL mechanism to comply with Opinions
on Delineating and Strictly Uphold ERLs and local regulations on delineating ERLs to review the
selected sites recommended by the proposal. Once the proposed project is found not to belong to
limited human activities defined in Catalogue for Access Management of ERLs in Hainan Province,
the recommended site would be rejected. Activities under RA1 of the Project are to be located in
modified habitats that are highly affected by human activities, except sustainable forest management
activity in Lingshui County. Activities related to point and NPS pollution management will be
conducive to improving eco-environment in urban & rural and farmland areas, reducing stress on
marine eco-environment. Activities under RA1 of the Project are to do with ecosystem restoration
and most of them will be carried out within the scope of ERLs. These activities aim to restore priority
ecosystems, maintain and enhance biodiversity. They belong to activated defined in Catalogue for
Access Management of ERLs in Hainan Province. Furthermore, during the Project preparation, in
addition to EIA, special justification report on limited human activities will be prepared, reviewed by
DNRP/NRPBs, FBs for recognition, and finally subject to the approval by Provincial Government.
After investigation, it was found that there are above-ground cultural relics within the scope of the
Project activities. If there are any chances find during the construction, they will be handled in
accordance with the relevant policies and procedures established by National Cultural Heritage
Administration. There are cultural relics management sections under County-level Tourism and
Culture Bureau in place, who will establish a special leading group and an inter-government agencies’
joint meeting system for the protection of urban and rural historical culture. The strict management
of ERLs, the natural habitats and physical cultural resources delineated within the ERLs is aligned
with WB’ core principle on Natural habitats and Physical Cultural Resource, and with ESS6-
Biodiversity Conservation and Sustainable Management of living Natural Resources under ESF.
77.        The majority of activities on ecosystem restoration under RA 1 of the Project will not trigger
core zone of natural protected areas, though they will be carried out within scope of the ERLs. The
special justification of them during preparation, followed by continuous monitoring and assessment
guided by relevant technical guidelines or specifications on ecosystems restoration during
implementation can ensure that PforR activities will not result in significant conversion or degradation
of critical natural habitats.
Core Principle #3: Health and safety. Program E&S management systems are designed to protect
public and worker safety against the potential risks associated with (a) the construction and/or
operation of facilities or other operational practices under the Program; (b) exposure to toxic
chemicals, hazardous wastes, and otherwise dangerous materials under the Program; and (c)
reconstruction or rehabilitation of infrastructure located in areas prone to natural hazards.
78.       China and Hainan Provine have established a sound health and safety management
systems that are similar to or even more complex than environmental protection and pollution control
systems under a set of laws, regulations, standards and guidelines. The Project activities involve
low risk factors on OHS except the exposure to pesticides and use of small amount of chemicals in
WWTPs and WWTFs, belong to “general management” specified by Catalogue for Classified
Management of Occupational Disease Hazards in Construction Projects. In accordance with
Regulations on the Management of Occupational Health in the Workplace (2021), Measures for the
Supervision and Administration of Occupational Health Monitoring by Employers, Occupational
Disease Prevention and Control Law, Regulation on Safety Production of Hainan Province, Interim
Measures for Grading and Controlling Safety Hazards in Water Production Accidents in Hainan
Province, the mechanisms of OHS “three simultaneousness”, classified management of OHS
hazards, employers provision of PPE to their employees, regular trainings on OHS, forest
management, crops pest and forest pest prevention and control, procedures for forest fire control
have been established. In the feasibility study report and design documents, a sub-section on the
design, construction and operation of safety facilities are required. Taking safety measures, safety

                                                   52
inspections and necessary remedial measures have become common practices during construction
to ensure the safety of communities, individuals and workers.
79.       According to Pesticide Management Regulations and relevant guidelines for safe use of
pesticides, Safety Guidelines for Confined Space Operations. The sludge from WWTPs and WWTFs
are transferred by sealed tankers to disposal sites. Sludge is disposed of by incineration in biomass
energy power plants, or waste-to-energy incineration plant, or co-processed by cement kiln. The
policy of "prevention first, comprehensive management" is implemented in managing pesticides for
crop pest control and forest pest control. To manage pesticides, mechanism of licensing pesticides
producers and sellers ensure the safety of pesticides in production, selling and application. To
reduce the use of pesticides, various measures are taken, such as healthy cultivation of crops,
planting and managing mixed forest, strict quarantine inspection of species, IPM (integration
biological control, physical control pest and pests’ vectors), etc. The use of chemical pesticides
involves hazardous chemicals such as organophosphorus pesticides and carbaryl, which are
harmful to human health. In accordance with the Regulations on the Safety Management of
Hazardous Chemicals, Catalogue of Hazardous Chemicals, Safety Production Law, Occupational
Disease Prevention and Control Law and other provisions, the service entities providing unified and
specialized services to crop pest control are required to establish their safety management system,
use safe pesticide spraying equipment and take safety measures, provide their operators with
standard PPE. FBs and ARABs provide regular training to operator’s exposure to the hazardous
chemicals or pesticides and carry out publicity of protection knowledge. There are EMBs at
provincial level and county level who formulated emergency responsive plans for forest fires. The
County FB formulated emergency plan for forestry pests & disaster prevention and control. These
emergency plans help to address the challenges of potential community health and safety risk from
accidents events.
80.      China and Hainan Province have established a complete health and safety management
systems that are broadly consistent with the Bank's Core Principle#3 and corresponding planning
elements, as well as the ESS2-Labor and Working Conditions, ESS 4-Community health and safety
under ESF. Typical ecosystems restoration and forest management activities in coastal zones,
marine areas and forest areas, operators may face OHS risks such as drowning, falls, bites and heat
stress, etc. Even though FBs, as the Project PIUs, will continue to pay more attention to the OHS of
workers engaged in inland forest restoration and sustainable forest management. However, OHS
of workers/operators engaged in ecosystems restoration in shoreline, marine areas, and
maintenance, need strong assistance from cross-sectoral agencies, i.e., maritime department to
improve health and safety awareness of the operators, place OHS on an equal footing with
ecosystem restoration, an action plan (PAP) is proposed By ESSA (see Chapter 7).
81.     Consistency analysis conclusions: The environmental management systems of China
and Hainan Province related to the Project are relatively sound in terms of legal framework,
implementation mechanism, institutional setting and personnel arrangement, and the management
performance is demonstrated substantially satisfactory. In general, the EMSs are consistent with the
core principles, the EHS guidelines, meeting the requirements of ESS1- Assessment and
Management of Environmental and Social Risks and Impacts and ESS6- Biodiversity Conservation
and Sustainable Management of Living Natural Resources under ESF. These systems are able to
meet the environmental management needs of activities under the 3 Ras of the Project. A generic
E&S mitigation measure for managing potential E&S risks related to the Project activities is also
attached to Annex 8 for reference of relevant agencies in Hainan Province. Environmental action
plans have been recommended in the ESSA (as presented in Chapter 7) to fill the gaps identified in
the due diligence.




                                                 53
5. Evaluation of the social management system related to this project
5.1 General principles
82.        The Bank’s PforR ESSA Guidance establishes a framework of principles and elements for
the systematic assessment of borrowers' E&S systems. This chapter systematically identifies the
Project's key social impacts and risk categories in relation to the six core principles and thirteen
elements set out in the guidelines. A detailed comprehensive analysis is conducted between
domestic social risk management requirements and capacities and the World Bank's core principles
and key elements (see Annex 3). Based on this analysis, the report provides a comprehensive
evaluation of the project's major risks from three perspectives: relevant social management
regulations; institutional system and capabilities; and implementation performance and effectiveness.
It also proposes recommendations for improvements and action plans to address any identified gaps.
83.       Chapter 3 and Annex 2 identify the risks and social impacts associated with the project's
activities, including land use and public participation. Core Principle #2: Following confirmation by
the Tourism and Culture Bureau of Changjiang and Lingshui County that the project construction
area does not involve any newly discovered above-ground cultural relics, it has been determined
that the project will not have an adverse impact on material cultural resources. Core Principle #5:
Both Lingshui and Changjiang are Li Autonomous Counties, predominantly inhabited by the Han, Li,
and Miao ethnic groups. The project exhibits a mixed pattern of large-scale cohabitation and small-
scale clustering among ethnic minorities. These communities enjoy the same rights, welfare benefits
and protections as the Han population within the social, economic and political systems; only certain
cultural practices and lifestyles differ. Based on findings from baseline surveys and interviews, and
in accordance with the requirements of the Environmental and Social Framework, this project does
not trigger Environmental and Social Standard 7 (Indigenous/Minorities/Communities with Distinctive
Sociocultural Identities). At the screening stage, activities that may marginalize vulnerable groups
(such as low-income populations, ethnic minorities and women), lead to discrimination or trigger
conflicts have already been excluded from the project. To address the needs of these groups, the
project implements Project Action Plans (PAPs), ensuring they benefit too.
84.       In line with the core principles, China has established a social risk management system
(see Table 5-1). Any major decisions that directly affect people's immediate interests and could have
a significant impact on social stability, public safety, etc. must conduct a social stability risk
assessment in order to identify, analyses, evaluate and manage social risks. Additionally, a series
of laws, regulations and policies have been formulated and implemented at all levels of government
to establish the necessary management institutions and work mechanisms for land acquisition and
demolition, labor management, and the promotion of effective information disclosure and public
participation. The effectiveness of this social management system has been evaluated based on
relevant laws and regulations, management institutions and mechanisms, and management
practices.
