5.2 stainable social risk management
85.      A sustainable social risk management system includes two elements: Element 1: At the
Project level, legal frameworks and management institutions are able to adequately guide social
assessments; Element 2: Good practices are adopted in social assessment and management
processes, including the following five elements.
5.2.1 Regulatory and Policy Framework
Element 1: The legal framework and management agencies can direct social assessment
adequately at the PforR Program level.
86.      Social stability risk assessment (SSRA): The Chinese government uses SSRA as a tool
to systematically manage the social risks and impacts that may be involved in development of major
projects, policies and reforms, and mitigates and manages social impacts actively by establishing
and implementing a whole SSRA system, so as to promote scientific decision-making, and
sustainable Program and social development.
⚫    The Opinions on Strengthening Social Stability Risk Assessment for Major Decisions under New
     Circumstances (2021), require that an SSRA shall be carried out on major decisions including
     those on major construction projects. It specifies the contents, methods, procedures, and
     management of SSRA, and application of SSRA results, and underlines that the contents of
     SSRA are integral to the Program's feasibility study and application reports.
⚫    The Interim Measures for the Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major Fixed Asset Investment
     Projects (2012), stating that the Project organization shall investigate and analyze social stability
     risks when conducting preparatory work, collect opinions from relevant people, identify risks,
     risk possibilities and risk impacts, and propose prevention and mitigation measures, and social
     stability risk ratings after such measures are taken.
⚫    The Guidelines on Establishing a Sound Social Stability Risk Assessment Mechanism for Major
     Decisions and Matters (2012), requiring that an SSRA shall be conducted on major decisions,
     projects and policies.
⚫    The Interim Regulations on Major Administrative Decision-making Procedures (2019), require
     that the implementation of major administrative decisions with the potential to adversely affect


                                                             56
    social stability, public safety, and related aspects must undergo risk assessment first. Major
    administrative decisions include: i) the formulation of significant public policies and measures
    related to public services, market regulation, social governance, environmental protection, etc.;
    ii) the development of crucial plans concerning economic and social development; iii) decisions
    concerning major public facilities within the administrative region; iv) decisions on other
    significant matters that have a substantial impact on economic and social development and
    public interests, etc.
⚫   The revised Land Management Law of the People's Republic of China (2020 Revision),
    specifically requires that relevant departments should conduct land condition surveys, social
    stability risk assessments, and negotiations with the affected people before any land acquisition
    or demolition activities commence. If necessary, a public hearing should be organized, and an
    agreement should be signed before the land acquisition approval procedures can be completed.
⚫   The 'Notice on Issuing the Hainan Province Major Decision-Making Social Stability Risk
    Assessment Measures' (Qiongbanfa [2022] No. 4), issued by the General Offices of the Hainan
    Provincial Committees of the Communist Party of China and the Hainan Provincial People's
    Government, establishes detailed regulations regarding the scope, content, assessment entities,
    methods, procedures, management, application of results, implementation tracking,
    performance evaluation and accountability of social stability risk assessments of major decisions
    within Hainan Province. For example, at the county level, Lingshui County issued the
    'Implementation Rules for Major Decision-Making Social Stability Risk Assessment in Lingshui
    Li Autonomous County' (Lingwenpingzu [2023] No. 1), and Changjiang County released the
    'Notice on Deepening the Work of Major Decision-Making Social Stability Risk Assessment'
    (Changzhengzi [2020] No. 41). These documents explicitly state that all major decisions
    affecting people's vital interests, with broad impacts and the potential to trigger social stability
    issues, must undergo social stability risk assessments before being made by Party and
    government agencies. This includes decisions relating to land acquisition and demolition,
    farmers' burdens, state-owned enterprise restructuring, environmental remediation, social
    security, public welfare projects and sensitive government investment projects affecting the
    environment, including major engineering projects and policy formulation. Separate social
    stability risk analysis reports must be compiled for each decision.
Element 2: Incorporate recognized elements of good practice in E&S assessment and management,
including five aspects.
87.      (i) Early screening: During site selection and feasibility study of related projects, the
relevant authorities (for example, the Housing and Urban-Rural Development Bureau/Urban
Renewal Center, Natural Resources and Planning Bureau and Culture and Tourism Bureau, etc.)
shall be coordinated to conduct a joint survey, and risks and impacts screening. For example, the
Measures for the Administration of the Pre-review on the Use of Land for Construction Projects (2017
Revision), and the Land Administration Law (2020 Revision) require that screening be conducted so
that the construction project complies with the land utilization plan and avoids any acquisition of
basic farmland. The revised Cultural Relics Protection Law of the People’s Republic of China (2017
Revision) requires that a survey of cultural relics should be conducted before a project site is selected
in order to avoid affecting cultural relics as much as possible. The Regulations on the Prevention
and Control of Geologic Disasters (2004 Revision) require that the Project area shall not be selected
in disaster areas, and related disaster prevention and control requirements should be defined
through a geological disaster assessment to reduce public security risks if any project to be
constructed in the areas liable to geological disasters. The Opinions on Strengthening Social Stability
Risk Assessment for Major Decisions under New Circumstances (2021), stipulates that SSRA must
be carried out for all major decisions and matters directly affecting the interests of people and
potentially posing significant impacts on social stability, public safety, and related aspects. The
assessment shall investigate the legality, rationality, feasibility, and controllability of major decisions
and matters. The scope of this investigation should cover stakeholders in the affected areas,
ensuring the comprehensive collection of opinions from the public and various stakeholders. It entails
thorough and continuous screening and analysis of potential social stability risks.
88.     (ii) Alternatives: Options should be compared and analyzed during project site selection
and feasibility study. The Administrative License Law of the People's Republic of China (2004), and


                                                    57
the Decision of the State Council on Establishing Administrative License for Administrative Review
and Approval Items Really Necessary to Be Retained (2004), require that the feasibility study of a
project shall compare E&S impacts of different options to avoid or minimize local negative E&S
impacts. The Notice of the General Office of the National Development and Reform Commission on
Issuing the Outline for the Preparation of the Chapter on the Social Stability Risk Analysis of Major
Fixed Asset Investment Projects and Assessment Report(2013) and The 'Notice on Issuing the
Hainan Province Major Decision-Making Social Stability Risk Assessment Measures' (Qiongbanfa
[2022] No. 4), jointly issued by the General Offices of the Hainan Provincial Committees of the
Communist Party of China and the Hainan Provincial People's Government, stipulates that project
implementation units and their assessment agencies must consult local governments, relevant
departments, grassroots organizations and social groups on the support stance for the proposed
project during the planning of site selection, land and housing acquisition compensation,
resettlement arrangements and environmental protection. The aim of this process is to select a
socially stable risk acceptable project option that meets acceptable standards.
89.       (iii) Developing measures to avoid, minimize or mitigate social impacts: The Notice on
Issuing the Outline for the Preparation of the Chapter on the Social Stability Risk Analysis of Major
Fixed Asset Investment Projects and Assessment Report (2013) requires that plans and measures
shall be proposed to prevent and mitigate risks. The Guidelines on Establishing a Sound Social
Stability Risk Assessment Mechanism for Major Decisions and Matters (Interim,2012) and Circular
of the General Office of the CPC Hainan Provincial Committee and the General Office of the Hainan
Provincial People's Government on issuing the 'Measures for Social Stability Risk Assessment of
Major Decisions in Hainan Province' (Qiongbanfa [2022] No. 4):If the assessment report indicates a
Substantial risk, a decision not to implement shall be made, or a decision shall be made after the
plan is adjusted or the risk level is reduced. If a moderate risk is indicated, a decision to implement
shall be made after effective risk prevention and mitigation measures are taken. If a low risk is
indicated, a decision to implement may be made, but actions shall be taken to explain and persuade
those affected, and appeals from relevant individuals shall be handled properly. The SSRA report
shall also address the legitimacy, rationality, feasibility and controllability of the proposed activities
and require the development of an appropriate contingency plan. The Interim Regulations on Major
Administrative Decision-making Procedures (2019) also require the development of mitigation
measures for identified risks.
90.     (iv) Clear articulation of institutional responsibilities and resources to support
implementation of plans: The Guidelines on Establishing a Sound Social Stability Risk Assessment
Mechanism for Major Decisions and Matters (Interim,2012) and Circular of the General Office of the
CPC Hainan Provincial Committee and the General Office of the Hainan Provincial People's
Government on Issuing the "Measures for Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major Decisions in
Hainan Province" (Qiongbanfa [2022] No.4),Article 13: All formulated risk prevention and mitigation
measures (including environmental mitigation measures) must clearly specify the "responsible entity
for implementation" and "guarantees of funds, materials, and technology." Additionally, the
implementation process should allocate sufficient human, material, and financial resources to
conduct assessments.
91.        (v) Public participation, information disclosure and grievance redress mechanism:
The SSRA policies of Hainan require that public consultation be conducted with all stakeholders
involved in a plan to collect their opinions and suggestions, including advice, needs and directions
of public opinion on the proposed project from mass, online, mobile and other emerging media. The
Notice on Issuing the Outline for the Preparation of the Chapter on the Social Stability Risk Analysis
of Major Fixed Asset Investment Projects and Assessment Report(2013) and Circular of the General
Office of the CPC Hainan Provincial Committee and the General Office of the Hainan Provincial
People's Government on Issuing the "Measures for Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major
Decisions in Hainan Province" (Qiongbanfa [2022] No.4), the PIUs and assessment agencies shall
obtain supports of the local governments and related departments, grass-root organizations, NGOs,
etc. for the proposed project, and the completeness of public participation shall be assessed as well,
including if the procedural requirements of public participation, expert consultation and information
disclosure are all well implemented. For any project involving land acquisition and house demolition,
the Land Administration Law (2020 Revision) and the Provisional Measures for Social Stability Risk
Assessment of land acquisition in Hebei Province (2022) requires that once the land acquisition is


                                                   58
approved in accordance with related law, the government at or above the county level shall disclose
the key information, e.g. the purpose and boundary of land acquisition, current status, compensation
rate, resettlement mode, social security, etc. in the township (town), village and village group for at
least 30 days, to collect comments from the affected rural collective economic organization and its
members, village committee and other stakeholders. If the concerned parties refuse to accept the
decisions, the disputes may be brought to court within 30 days after the notification on the decision
is received. No party shall change the status quo of the land before the disputes over ownership and
use right are settled. If a construction unit or individual refuses to accept the administrative
punishment decisions on dismantling the buildings and other facilities, it may bring the case to the
court within 15 days starting from the day when the decision is received. The Standard Guidelines
for Grass-root Government Affairs Disclosure in Rural Collective Land Acquisition (2019) making
detailed provisions on project land acquisition policies, and the scope, time limit and channels of
disclosure during preparation, approval and implementation. The Measures for Hearings on Price
Setting by the Government (2018 Revision), which requires that in the process of setting (including
adjusting) government-guided prices, government-guided price levels, or pricing mechanisms in
accordance with the law, the pricing authority shall take the form of hearings to solicit the opinions
of the operators, consumers, and the relevant parties, and to argue for the necessity, feasibility, and
rationale of the price setting. The Interim Regulations on Major Administrative Decision-making
Procedures (2019) and the 'Notice on the Hainan Provincial Government's Catalogue Management
Measures for Major Administrative Decision-Making Items' (Qiong Fu Ban [2025] No. 35) requires
decision-making units to proactively coordinate with the relevant departments responsible for
supporting, reviewing and evaluating, and ensuring the legal compliance of, major administrative
decision-making matters. A regular consultation mechanism will be established, with the relevant
departments providing comprehensive services and supervision to enhance collaborative efficiency
and ensure the scientific and effective implementation of major administrative decisions.
5.2.2 Implementation mechanism
92.       Social Stability Risk Assessment Mechanism: This refers to a set of institutionalized
procedures and systems designed to predict, evaluate and intervene in advance with regard to
factors that may impact social stability, such as major decisions, significant projects or major events.
The aim is to prevent, mitigate or resolve social stability risks. The mechanism prioritizes the
consideration of social stability risks, requiring systematic assessments of potential social conflicts
before policies or projects are introduced or approved. Corresponding contingency plans must be
formulated to prevent and reduce social instability incidents at source, ensuring that 'all assessments
are conducted, evaluations are thorough, and prevention and control measures are robust’. This
framework integrates legal, institutional and procedural elements to create a systematic approach to
preventing, assessing and mitigating social risks. A comprehensive institutional system
encompassing accountability, operational procedures and standardized protocols has been
implemented at all levels, from central to local, to ensure that risk prevention in major decision-
making processes is conducted in accordance with established guidelines. In compliance with
national and provincial social stability risk assessment standards for major decisions, Changjiang
County and Lingshui County have formulated detailed implementation rules. These regulations
delineate responsibilities for evaluation, methodologies, the scope and content of assessments,
assessment procedures, utilization of results, monitoring of decision implementation, delegation of
assessments, management of third-party institutions, and administration of expert panels. Both
counties have established standardized social risk assessment and management systems, including
project review mechanisms and filing protocols. They also employ a seven-step social stability
assessment methodology. Detailed work logs and aggregated evaluation data are maintained,
implementing highly standardized management practices.
5.2.3 Institutional organization and Implementation Performance
93.       To manage the social stability risks of major projects, China has set up a network of
specialized management agencies at various levels, from provincial (e.g. Provincial Development
and Reform Commission, Provincial Political and Legal Affairs Commission) to county (e.g. County
Political and Legal Affairs Commission, County Development and Reform Commission). These
agencies are responsible for tasks such as comprehensive coordination, guidance and supervision,
and approval and filing. The evaluation subject (i.e. the decision-making/project unit) is explicitly


                                                  59
required to entrust a third-party evaluation agency that has undergone training and registration to
conduct the evaluation, thereby enhancing the professionalism and objectivity of the work. The
governments at all levels in Hainan Province and Changjiang County/Lingshui County have set up
dedicated departments with clearly defined responsibilities. The management agencies and their
functions are as follows:
      Provincial DRC: approving major fixed asset investment projects based on social stability
       risks and other relevant documents (attaching the SSRA report and review comments when
       applying for FSR approval).
      Provincial PLAC: coordinating, supervising and directing SSRA. Instructing the subjects of
       decision making and assessment to convene different political and legal affairs committees,
       and authorities for cross-regional / departmental projects.
      District/county government: conducting district/county-wide social stability risk
       assessment, decision-making, implementation, and supervision, and it is where the SSRA
       report is discussed and approved in the meeting of the standing committee of the
       district/county CPC, the meeting of government executive committee, or the meeting of the
       Party and the government leadership team.
      County DRC/PLAC: formulating local pricing policies of public service under the framework
       of provincial pricing policies.
      Assessor: conducting or appointing an independent appraisal agency to conduct SSRA
       and implementing SSRA measures.
      Independent appraisal agency: attending SSRA training and reviews organized by NDRC
       and getting registered at the provincial PLAC in advance.
94.        At county level, the Political and Legal Affairs Commission of Changjiang County is
responsible for overseeing social risk assessment management. The department responsible for
stability risk assessment is currently located within the Social Security Office of the Political and
Legal Affairs Commission under the Changjiang County Party Committee and is directly supervised
by the Deputy Secretary of the Political and Legal Affairs Commission. The team consists of three
members of staff: one Deputy Secretary and two regular staff. Office operations and salaries are
funded by fiscal resources. Key responsibilities include: 1) Organizing, guiding and implementing
stability risk assessment initiatives in the region; and 2) Accelerating the establishment of a robust
risk assessment framework to create effective preventive and regulatory mechanisms. Develop and
refine local implementation guidelines, evaluation methods, and other regulatory documents.
Conducting assessments, providing guidance and monitoring the progress of stability risk
assessments within the county. 4) Compile assessment findings, conduct regular public opinion
surveys, and promptly understand public sentiment and social attitudes. Analyze and evaluate local
social stability risks to inform decision-making. 5) Apply the results of the assessments and oversee
the implementation process. The Political and Legal Affairs Commission of Lingshui County has set
up a Social Security Office with 10 full-time members of staff. The County Business Environment
Bureau collaborates with the office to oversee social risk assessment management. Together, they
guide the city in conducting social risk predictions for potential instability factors related to major
policy formulation or adjustments, significant events and major activity arrangements. Any identified
risks are evaluated and managed using social stability risk assessment to prevent and mitigate major
social risks.
95.       In terms of implementation performance, Changjiang County and Lingshui County in Hainan
Province have achieved measurable governance outcomes in the management of social stability
risks, demonstrating significant effectiveness in the prevention and resolution of conflicts. For
example, since 2024, Changjiang County has conducted four stability assessments related to
sewage treatment, focusing primarily on controlling the risks associated with land acquisition, public
transportation and noise pollution. Meanwhile, 66 projects have passed evaluation and filing in
Lingshui County since 2024 (90% engineering projects and 10% policy assessment projects),
effectively reducing potential social conflicts at source.




                                                  60
5.2.4 Assessment Summary of Social Risk Management System
96.        The assessment confirms that the social risk management systems implemented in
Changjiang and Lingshui counties in Hainan province are effective and comply with core principles
1 and 6 of the World Bank's guidance. A review of the documents reveals that policies, mechanisms,
standards and management procedures for social stability risk assessment have been established
and enforced at the national, provincial and county levels. This assessment is a key tool in social
risk management, providing comprehensive oversight of critical social impacts and risks associated
with major projects, policies, and reforms. It also serves as a prerequisite for project applications and
feasibility studies and is a mandatory procedure in land acquisition processes. Governments at all
levels, including national, provincial (Hainan) and county (Changjiang/Lingshui) levels, have
established dedicated departments with clearly defined responsibilities and stable financial funding
sources. They have also issued specific implementation requirements and detailed guidelines for
assessing the social stability risks of major decisions at county level. This ensures that all major
projects and decisions undergo comprehensive risk evaluation. Meanwhile, the interview also found
that conducting a social stability risk assessment contributes to conflict mediation and maintaining
social stability during project implementation. Previous project experiences demonstrate that, by
identifying and assessing social risks effectively, targeted risk mitigation measures can be formulated
to resolve and manage potential risks and disputes during the initial project preparation phase.
5.3 Land use and involuntary resettlement
5.3.1 Regulatory and Policy Framework
97.        (i) Minimizing negative impacts related to land acquisition: The Land Administration
Law (2020 Revision), the Measures for the Administration of the Pre-examination on the Use of Land
for Construction Projects (2017), and the regulations on SSRA require that projects and enterprises
shall utilize existing construction land, and avoid any occupation of farmland (especially permanent
basic farmland) where possible, and reduce LAR impacts through design optimization, thereby
reducing social stability risks. At the preparation stage, natural resources authorities will participate
in the survey to confirm the land to be used for the Project, and the feasibility study will compare
different options for LAR impacts. The government authorities will check if the land use plan is
rational during land use review and feasibility study. Hainan Province has issued two official
documents: the 'Notice of the People's Government of Hainan Province on Implementing the
Strictest Farmland Protection System and Strictly Observing the Farmland Protection Red Line'
(Qiong Fu Ban [2022] No. 22), and the 'Notice on Further Strengthening Farmland Protection Work'.
These policies aim to enforce the strictest farmland protection system and land conservation
measures, enhance supervision of farmland protection and strictly observe the red line of farmland
protection. The content is largely consistent with national-level regulations. Additionally, the "Land
Administration Law of the People's Republic of China" (2020 Revision) states that urban
infrastructure and public welfare projects may obtain land through allocation after approval by
county-level or higher governments for permanent occupation of state-owned land. The 'Notice of
the People's Government of Hainan Province on Issuing the "Hainan Implementation Measures for
State Council Authorized Land Use Approval Matters" (Qiong Fu Ban [2025] No. 46)' stipulates the
following: 1) Strict control of new construction land use, with projects required to priorities existing
urban construction land during the site selection process; and 2) Rigorous review of farmland
occupation to ensure a balanced land compensation scheme. County-level land and resources
authorities must conduct surveys and provide review opinions for projects involving large-scale
farmland occupation or permanent basic farmland use when processing land pre-review and site
planning.
98.       (ii) Identifying and addressing economic and social impacts arising from land
acquisition or loss of access to natural resources: The Land Administration Law (2020 Revision)
stipulates, “Owners or users of the land to be acquired shall, within the time limit specified in the
announcement, go to fill the compensation registration form with holding its assets ownership
certificate. The people’s government at or above the county level shall organize the department
concerned to estimate the relevant costs and make them fully available…For those who engage in
unauthorized planting or construction after the date of land acquisition pre-announcement,
compensation shall not be provided.” The land acquisition compensation measures of Hebei



                                                   61
province make systematic arrangements for land acquisition compensation and resettlement in
accordance with the Land Administration Law, including for those lacking legal title. During land
acquisition, affected people shall confirm the results of detailed measurement survey (DMS), and
the land acquisition agency shall enter into compensation and resettlement agreements with
landowners and users before submitting application for project approval. If land acquisition is
required for this project, compensation will be provided in accordance with the standards set out in
the Hainan Provincial People's Government's Notice on republishing the comprehensive land price
for land acquisition zones across the province (Qiong Fu [2024] No. 9), which was issued in March
2024.
⚫   State-owned land compensation: The Hainan Province Land Acquisition Compensation and
    Resettlement Management Measures stipulate the following: 1) For state-owned land granted
    through state transfer and used by affected persons, compensation shall be based on the
    market valuation of comparable land.2) For state-owned land obtained through state allocation,
    compensation shall be determined by referencing the assessed value of the allocated land use
    rights.3) For vacant land with valid state-owned land ownership certificates, idle land shall be
    disposed of by the county-level resources and planning department in accordance with the Idle
    Land Disposal Measures. Non-idle land shall be compensated at market valuation.
⚫   Temporary land use: The Implementation Regulations of the Land Administration Law of the
    People's Republic of China establish clear requirements for the management and post-use
    restoration of temporary land use. Article 20 stipulates that temporary land use must be
    approved by natural resources authorities at or above the county level, with a maximum duration
    of two years. Land users are required to complete land reclamation within one year after the
    temporary use period ends, restoring the land to a usable condition. Cultivated land must be
    restored to planting conditions. In Hainan Province, temporary land use applicants must sign
    contracts with county-level natural resources authorities, rural collective economic organizations,
    or village committees based on land ownership. At county level, Lingshui County implements a
    lump-sum compensation model for young crops, in accordance with the 'Notice on
    Compensation Standards for young Crops and Surface Attachments in Land Acquisition in
    Lingshui Li Autonomous County' (Lingshui Government Office [2023] No. 56). Changjiang
    County, on the other hand, adheres to the 'Announcement on Compensation Standards for
    Green Crops and Surface Attachments in Land Acquisition in Changjiang Li Autonomous
    County' (Changjiang Government Regulation [2024] No. 3). Both documents provide detailed
    compensation standards for young crops and attachments. Compensation for temporary land
    use is usually agreed upon by land users and farmers.
⚫   Land leasing/Management Rights Transfer: the "Measures for the Administration of Rural
    Land Management Rights Transfer" (Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Affairs Order No.1 [2021])
    stipulates that such transfers must adhere to the principles of legality, voluntariness, and
    compensation, with contracts being signed. All proceeds from land management rights transfers
    shall belong to the contracting party. The 'Notice on Standardizing the Management of Rural
    Land Management Rights Transfer' (Qiongnongzi [2022] No. 342), issued by the Hainan
    Provincial Department of Agriculture and Rural Affairs, and the 'Notice on Issuing the Revised
    Pilot Measures for the Entry of Collective Commercial Construction Land into the Market (Hainan
    Province)', issued by the Hainan Provincial Department of Natural Resources and Planning,
    have established detailed regulations covering service responsibilities for the transfer of rural
    land management rights, system improvements and standardized transfer procedures. These
    regulations ensure the orderly implementation of the transfer of rural land management rights
    across the province. At the county level, implementation rules and pricing standard guidance
    documents have been formulated to support rural land management rights transfer. The
    Changjiang County Department of Agriculture and Rural Affairs issued the "Notice on Guiding
    Prices for Rural Land Contract Transfer in Changjiang Li Autonomous County" (Changnong
    Letter [2024] No.196), establishing minimum market-guided prices for rural land contract
    transfers. The "Implementation Plan for Registration of Rural Land Management Rights Transfer
    and Filing of Transfer Contracts in Changjiang Li Autonomous County" provides detailed
    procedures and implementation guidelines for land transfer. Land management rights transfers
    are managed through standardized contracts, with model contract templates formulated by the
    Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Affairs. In Lingshui County, the Department of Agriculture and


                                                 62
    Rural Affairs, Bureau of Natural Resources and Planning, Finance Bureau, and Forestry Bureau
    jointly issued the "Notice on Standardizing Management of Rural Collective Asset Transfer
    Transactions" (Lingnong Bureau [2025] No.158), which outlines procedures for collective asset
    transfers and contract management. Additionally, a comprehensive land acquisition
    compensation appeal mechanism has been established across grassroots rural communities,
    townships, and county-level governments. Affected individuals dissatisfied with compensation
    or resettlement arrangements may file appeals with village chiefs or committees, or apply to
    town or county governments. According to the "Regulations on Petition Work" (2022), petition
    departments at all levels must fulfill responsibilities including case acceptance, referral,
    coordination, and supervision. Dissatisfied parties may also resolve disputes through legal
    litigation to protect their legitimate rights.
⚫   Forest land utilization: The Implementation Regulations of the Forest Law of the People's
    Republic of China set out the operational rules of the Forest Law, providing details on
    procedures such as the approval of forest land use and the collection of forest vegetation
    restoration fees. The Management Measures for the Examination and Approval of Construction
    Projects Using Forest Land, issued by the National Forestry and Grassland Administration,
    serve as the core operational guidelines, outlining the conditions for submitting an application,
    the authority responsible for granting approval, and the materials required for forest land use. In
    accordance with legislation such as the Hainan Province Mangrove Protection Regulations and
    the Hainan Province Coastal Protective Forest Construction and Protection Regulations, the
    permanent occupation of coastal protective forests by construction projects requires provincial
    approval and adherence to the legal procedures for permanent forest land use. In cases
    involving the occupation of public welfare forests, the legal procedures for the land acquisition
    and occupation of public welfare forests must be followed.
⚫   Marine area utilization: In accordance with the People's Republic of China's Law on the
    Administration of Sea Area Use and other relevant legislation, projects such as seagrass bed
    restoration, coral reef rehabilitation, mangrove restoration and artificial fish reef construction are
    usually carried out to protect the environment and restore ecosystems. A marine area use
    feasibility study must be submitted by the intended user to the city, county or autonomous
    county's natural resources and planning departments where the Project is located, for review
    and approval. If the Project involves the occupation of mangrove areas, approval must first be
    obtained from the provincial forestry authorities and then submitted to the National Forestry and
    Grassland Administration for final authorization.
99.      (iii) Compensation and transition subsidy to be fully paid at replacement cost before
land acquisition: The Land Administration Law (2020 Revision) defines compensation policies,
rates, principles, flows, schedules, etc. for different types of land use. Fair and reasonable
compensation shall be granted for land acquisition to ensure that the living standard of the affected
farmers is not reduced, and their long-term livelihoods are secure. In March 2024, Hainan Province
implemented the latest adjustment to its land acquisition compensation standards by issuing the
'Notice of the People's Government of Hainan Province on Re-announcing the Comprehensive land
acquisition Price Standards for the Province' (Qiong Fu [2024] No. 9). This notice specifies that the
comprehensive land acquisition price standard includes compensation fees and resettlement
subsidies for rural collective agricultural land and unused land. However, it excludes social security
expenses for expropriated farmers designated for social insurance contributions, as well as
compensation for any attachment or crops. The 'Hainan Province land acquisition Compensation
and Resettlement Management Measures' (effective from 1 January 2024) and the 'Hainan Province
Rural Land Acquisition Pilot Measures' clearly outline the distribution rules for compensation and
resettlement expenses.
100.     (iv) Policy arrangements for livelihood restoration: The Land Administration Law (2020
Revision) requires that the living standard of the affected farmers shall not be reduced, and their
long-term livelihoods shall be secured. In general, five main resettlement modes are available to
land-expropriated farmers: agricultural production, reemployment, equity participation, non-local
resettlement, and endowment insurance. In addition to the above five modes, state policies, such as
the Notice on Doing a Good Job in Employment Training and Social Security for Land-expropriated
Farmers (2006), also requires that local government shall establish a social security system suited


                                                   63
to the characteristics and needs of land-expropriated farmers, secure employment training and social
security funds, promote land-expropriated farmers to get employed and be incorporated into urban
society, and ensure that the living standard of land-expropriated farmers is not reduced due to land
acquisition, and their long-term livelihoods are secured. For eligible land-expropriated farmers,
employment and startup supporting policies should be implemented, occupational training should be
further strengthened, and public employment services should be improved to promote their
employment and startup. The 'Measures for the Participation of Land-Expropriated Farmers in Basic
Old-Age Insurance in Hainan Province' (Qiong Fu [2025] No. 11) stipulates that the government shall
allocate social security funds for each batch of land acquisition, providing one-off payment subsidies
to enable affected farmers to participate in basic old-age insurance. These subsidies are included in
the costs of land acquisition.
101.      (v) Policy arrangements for infrastructure restoration: For potential infrastructure
impacts arising from land acquisition and house demolition, the Land Administration Law (2020
Revision) and the Regulations for the Implementation of the Land Administration Law (2021)
stipulate, after the land acquisition plan is approved and announced, the county government shall
organize a land details measurement survey within the range of land acquisition and disclose the
results to the public for at least 30 days. The Land Administration Law (2020 Revision) stipulates,
“For rural residential houses, fair and reasonable compensation shall be provided on the principle of
compensation before relocation and residential condition improvement, ….”
102.      (vi) Information disclosure, public participation and informed decision-making: Public
participation runs through the whole project lifecycle and is an important measure to ensure the
success of LAR activities. The Standard Guidelines for Grass-root Government Affairs Disclosure in
Rural Collective Land Acquisition (2019) and Hainan Province Construction Project Land Use
Element Guarantee Service Manual June 2025 sorting out matters to be disclosed, regulating the
disclosure process, and improving modes of disclosure to protect the people’s rights of information,
participation, expression, and supervision practically. For projects involving land acquisition and
demolition, the county government shall issue a pre-announcement of land acquisition in the relevant
township, village or village group, with a minimum period of ten working days for public feedback.
The government shall then issue an official land acquisition announcement within the same
jurisdiction for at least thirty days. If the majority of members of the rural collective economic
organization whose land is to be expropriated believe that the proposed compensation and
resettlement plan violates laws and regulations, the local people's government at or above county
level shall organize a public hearing to gather opinions. Prior to making a land acquisition decision,
the county government must conduct a social stability risk assessment in accordance with the
relevant regulations. Compensation funds must be fully disbursed, stored in a dedicated account
and used exclusively for their intended purpose. The housing demolition department shall publicly
disclose the investigation results of the expropriated properties to the affected individuals within the
designated land acquisition area. For cases of temporary land use, the Ministry of Natural Resources'
Notice on Standardizing Temporary Land Use Management (Document No. 2 [2021]) requires the
public disclosure of approval information. The County Natural Resources Bureau also requires
applicants to display approval documents at construction sites while the Project is being
implemented. Regarding land contract management rights transfers, operators must first sign
transfer contracts legally with contracted farmers and obtain their consent.
5.3.2 Implementation Mechanism
103.      China has established a comprehensive land use management system covering all regions
and types of land use management, spanning the entire process from planning and approval to
utilization and supervision. Based on this project's activity type, the main land management
mechanisms involved are as follows:
   ⚫ Land Acquisition and Livelihood Restoration Mechanism: This mechanism centers on the
     Land Administration Law and aims to balance the statutory framework of public interest with
     the rights of farmers whose land is expropriated and the need for sustainable development.
     Through a comprehensive land price compensation system by region, diversified resettlement
     measures and mandatory inclusion in the social security system, it strives to ensure that
     farmers' original living standards are not reduced, and their long-term livelihoods are secured.
     Interviews with Changjiang County, Lingshui County, the Hainan Provincial Bureau of Natural


                                                   64
        Resources and Planning, and township offices, along with field research, indicate that in
        accordance with national and Hainan Province's land acquisition policies, these counties have
        implemented compensation measures based on project requirements and the replacement
        value principle. They legally and promptly pay full land compensation fees, resettlement
        subsidies, and compensation for surface attachments and crops. Specific standards will be
        formulated under the "Hainan Provincial Government Notice on Re-announcing
        Comprehensive land acquisition Price Zones" (Qiong Fu [2024] No.9). Regarding the land
        acquisition mechanism, counties have established effective management and supervision
        systems in line with existing regulations, featuring clear division of responsibilities and
        successful implementation in past cases. Additionally, pursuant to the "Hainan Province
        Measures for Expropriated Farmers' Participation in Basic Old-Age Insurance" (Qiong Fu
        [2025] No.11), social security funds for affected farmers have been allocated, and eligible
        farmers have been incorporated into the pension insurance system.
     ⚫ Temporary Land Use Mechanism: The allocation of temporary land for projects is negotiated
       between land users and farmers. Compensation is determined based on land acquisition
       compensation standards and the duration of the temporary use. In compliance with the Land
       Management Law, the village committee and natural resources department ensure that land
       use complies with policy requirements and that the land is restored to its original agricultural
       condition after the usage period ends.
     ⚫ Land Leasing Management Mechanism: This mechanism aims to uphold collective
       ownership of rural land, providing greater stability for farmers' management rights under
       contract while increasing the flexibility of land management rights. Operating within the legal
       framework, it involves coordinated efforts across departments to ensure orderly transfers,
       manageable risks and safeguarded farmers' rights. The Administrative Measures for the
       Circulation of Rural Land Contractual Management Rights (March 2021) set out detailed
       provisions regarding circulation procedures, contract management and risk prevention. Under
       this mechanism, the circulation or leasing of land must adhere to three core principles: 1)
       Legality, Voluntariness and Compensation: Circulation must comply with legal provisions,
       respect farmers' wishes fully, and must not involve coercion or obstruction. Circulation terms
       shall be determined through equal negotiation between both parties. 2) No change in land
       use: Agricultural land must be used for agricultural purposes only; non-agricultural
       construction is strictly prohibited. 3) Protection of arable land and farmers' rights: The transfer
       must not compromise soil quality, and the principal status and lawful rights of contracted
       farmers (including their right to rental income, information and oversight) must be safeguarded.
       Land transfer management involves multiple tiers and departments, forming a collaborative
       governance framework characterized by 'Party committee leadership, government
       responsibility, departmental coordination, rural collective economic organizations as the
       foundation, farmers as the principal actors, and participation from social forces'. The transfer
       of land management rights is governed by standardized contracts, with model contract
       templates formulated by the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Affairs. Both Changjiang County
       and Lingshui County have issued detailed guidelines for the transfer of rural collective land
       management rights tailored to their local circumstances. These guidelines provide
       comprehensive stipulations covering all aspects of the process, including principles and
       methods, conditions and procedures, contracts and filing requirements, relevant
       responsibilities, and dispute resolution mechanisms.
5.3.3 Institutional organization and Implementation Performance
104.     The governments of Hainan Province, Changjiang County and Lingshui County have
established specialized departments responsible for different types of land management, including
land acquisition, land transfer, temporary land use, resettlement and livelihood recovery. These
departments have clearly defined responsibilities and effective management systems. Their specific
organizational structures and functions are as follows:
◼     Land/Forest use approval agencies：
 •     MNR: reviewing project-specific impact on basic farmland and ecological conservation redlines.

•       Provincial NRBs: reviewing project-specific permanent requisition of collective land (except

        documents to the competent government.
•       Provincial Forestry Bureau: responsible for reviewing the occupation of permanent forest
        land (on behalf of the National Forestry and Grassland Administration) and approving the
        requisition of public welfare forests. The Bureau also collaborates with the Provincial
        Department of Natural Resources and Planning to conduct reviews of coastal shelterbelt land
        use at provincial level. For projects involving important or mangrove wetlands, the forestry
        department must propose optimized disposal measures and notify stakeholders in advance. If
        the impact is deemed controllable and protective measures are feasible, expedited review and
        approval procedures will be implemented to ensure the Project is executed lawfully and in a
        timely manner.
•       Municipal/county forestry department: Responsible for reviewing and reporting on
        permanent forest land occupation (entrusted by the National Forestry and Grassland
        Administration), public welfare forest land acquisition, and coastal shelterbelt land use at the
        municipal/county level.
    •    Government at and above the county level: approving land use within the scope of its

          landowners. etc.

          LA will be subject to social security. Usually, the application for covering by social security is
          raised by the expropriated farmers, discussed by the village collective economic organization,
          verified by township government or sub-district office and publicized for seven days, reviewed
          by the natural resources department in conjunction with the public security department,
          approved by the local government, then the subsidy funds will be allocated by the local
          finance bureau, and finally registered by the HRSSB. Land-expropriated farmers may cover
          basic endowment insurance for urban workers, or basic endowment insurance for urban and
          rural residents voluntarily.

          the scope of its jurisdiction.

        •          Third-party appraisal agency: A qualified real estate appraisal agency will be appointed by

        •          Audit bureau: auditing resettlement costs regularly according to the statutory process and

◼             Facility agriculture land18 use (FALU)
        •          National and provincial NRBs, and ARABs: regulating FALU by various technical means;
        •          Municipal NRBs, and ARABs: supervising and guiding the management of FALU,
                   establishing and improving the inspection system, implementing the supervision of FALU,
                   and submitting FALU registration records to the provincial authority annually;
        •          County NRBs, and ARABs: responsible for routine FALU supervision, guiding the site
                   selection of facilities in accordance with the requirements of economical and intensive use of
                   land, identifying whether the tillage layer is destroyed, examining land restoration and
                   reporting the records to the competent prefecture (municipal) authorities quarterly. The
                   natural resources authorities, upon receipt of the approval documents and relevant records
                   of the FALU from the township governments, shall timely review and upload the relevant
                   information to the FALU regulation platform, carry out the annual survey on the change of
                   FALU according to regulations. The ARABs at the county level should strengthen the
                   guidance on FALU. Any unavoidable occupation of general farmland for any facility
                   agriculture should be incorporated into the annual plan of maintaining balance of cultivated
                   land of the county and can only be implemented after the plan is approved.
        •          Township governments: organizing rural collective economic organizations and operators
                   to determine the location and area of land used for facility agriculture properly based on the
                   facility construction plan and under the guidance of NRBs and ARABs at the county level in
                   accordance with the national spatial planning and land use planning, agricultural development
                   planning, village development planning, as well as policies on natural resources, agriculture,
                   and forestry, etc., provided that cultivated land is protected and land is used rationally;
                   organizing rural collective economic organizations and operators to conduct site selection,
                   complete LMRT, and sign land use agreement; tracking the whole process of FALU;
                   supervising the land restoration and hand-over process; disclosing the information of FALU;
                   and submitting the records to the NRB and ARAB at the county level on a monthly basis. The
                   plan of maintaining balance of cultivated land should be developed by the township
                   government if any contracted cultivated land is changed to other types of land like forest land.
                   After the plan is approved, instructions are given to the parties to the LMRT contract to re-
                   sign the or update land contract and relevant certificates.
        •          Rural collective economic organization: monitoring whether the operators conduct FALU
                   and fulfill the responsibility of land restoration in accordance with the agreement, and
                   disclosing the information of FALU on the bulletin board in the village.
◼           Land management right transfer (LMRT)
        •          MARA: directing nationwide LMRT and LMRT contract management.
        •          ARABs (rural management authorities) at or above the county level: establishing sound
                   operating rules, conducting policy inquiry, information disclosure, contract signing,
                   transaction attestation, equity appraisal, financing guarantee, file management and other
                   services in relation to LMRT; establishing a shared rural land contracting information platform
                   for at the national, provincial, municipal and county level in accordance with unified standards
                   and technical specifications, improving mechanism of signing LMRT contracts online,
                   managing LMRT in a standardized manner, and using information technology to facilitate

18 Facility agricultural land refers to land directly utilised for agricultural production, encompassing production facilities for livestock and poultry farming, crop cultivation, aquaculture, and their ancillary supporting facilities. It may be categorised into three types:

          LMRT; directing the work of township rural land contracting management authorities;

◼       Livelihood restoration
    •     Livelihood restoration measures include agricultural resettlement, reemployment
          resettlement, shareholding dividends, relocation and social security resettlement, among
          others. involving different management agencies. Specifically, agricultural resettlement is
          usually conducted by the village collective economic organization, which may decide to
          allocate undistributed collective land to households affected by land acquisition, or conduct
          land reallocation if no undistributed collective land is available; reemployment is chosen by
          affected households based on their own needs, where free training and employment support
          are provided by the county labor and employment authority; shares resettlement is
          determined by the PIU in consultation with affected households; relocation is requested by
          the affected households for new land farming at other areas, and decided by local
          governments after assessment and consulting with the host village collective economic
          organizations; social security for land-expropriated farmers is implemented by the county
          human resources and social security authority with the support of the township government
          and village/community committee.
105.     At the county level, Changjiang County's Natural Resources Bureau has established a Land
Use Control Division with four staff members to guide township governments in implementing land
acquisition and demolition procedures. For specific projects involving land and ancillary facility
acquisition, this division collaborates with the Project's implementing authorities, township
governments, and village committees to form a joint land acquisition management team. In Lingshui
County, a dedicated Farmland Protection Supervision Office with three full-time staff members
oversees land acquisition and demolition management county-wide, while a Natural Resources
Rights and Development Office with four full-time staff members manages land transfer operations.
At the Project implementation level, three entities—Lingshui Xingling Construction Management Co.,
Ltd., Changjiang Urban Construction Investment Co., Ltd., and Changjiang Li Autonomous County
Rural Revitalization Investment Development Co., Ltd. — have appointed 1-2 dedicated personnel
to handle social work management tasks, including coordinating land acquisition and demolition
processes, filing relevant documentation, and addressing complaints arising from social issues
during project implementation.
106.      In terms of implementation performance, a field visit found that, over the past three years,
Changjiang and Lingshui counties in Hainan Province have effectively managed land use for key
projects in the Hainan Free Trade Port, as well as for major infrastructure and industrial development.



                                                      68
Changjiang County has focused on industrial parks and sewage treatment projects, while Lingshui
County has prioritized tourism, high-end services, and supporting infrastructure. These efforts have
ensured a sufficient land supply for major projects, protected the legitimate rights of farmers, and
achieved a balance between 'development support' and 'resource conservation and farmer rights
protection', thus meeting national strategies and local development requirements. Regarding the
transfer/leasing of land operation rights, standardized procedures have concentrated land use
among large-scale specialized farmers, family farms, cooperatives, and agricultural enterprises. This
has significantly boosted high-value agriculture such as tropical fruits in Changjiang, winter
vegetables in Lingshui and southern breeding programmes, thereby enhancing agricultural efficiency.
A three-tier rural property rights trading system at provincial, county and township levels provides
services including information disclosure, contract certification and dispute mediation, substantially
reducing risks. Meanwhile, stable land rents from leasing have become a crucial source of cash
income for many farmers, particularly those from migrant worker households, effectively increasing
their income from property.
5.3.4 Assessment of Land Acquisition and Resettlement Management System
107.      The assessment of the relevant land acquisition and resettlement regulations in China is in
line with the requirements of Core Principle 4 and Element 9. A comprehensive legal framework and
policy system has been established and implemented at the national, Hainan Province and county
levels (Changjiang County and Lingshui County), covering land acquisition, land leasing, temporary
land use, resettlement and livelihood restoration. The above laws and regulations require that land
acquisition is avoided or minimized as much as possible. Where this is unavoidable, compensation
and resettlement must be provided for those affected to ensure their living standards are not reduced
and their long-term livelihoods are secured. In terms of land acquisition, temporary land use and
land transfer for the project, Changjiang County and Lingshui County have formulated specific policy
documents in accordance with national and provincial laws and regulations. In accordance with the
principles of equality, voluntariness, fairness and good faith, and subject to compliance with urban
and rural planning and the land use plan, land acquisition, resettlement and land leasing shall be
carried out in accordance with the policies, as shall land storage and allocation.
108.       The project's activities do not involve large-scale land acquisition or resettlement. The
exclusion list explicitly states that activities requiring large-scale land acquisition or resettlement are
not included in the project boundary. Therefore, the project will not have a significant social impact
in terms of land use. The potential impacts of land use may include When the site selection fails to
meet design specifications, the project will use a small area to construct a rural sewage treatment
station, an integrated agricultural waste processing center and a centralized livestock
intake/drainage well at the township pre-treatment facility. The total land use area will not exceed 50
mu (approximately 3.3 hectares).2) Temporary land use for sewage pipeline excavation during
construction. Furthermore, rural non-point source pollution remediation projects may involve
voluntary land leasing, which is triggered by adjustments to plot boundaries, improvements to
production roads, the construction of new irrigation facilities or irrigation ditches. These actions are
spontaneous and voluntary, and are taken by villagers through negotiation. Villagers can choose
whether or not to lease the land, or where to lease it, based on their preferences; therefore, this does
not constitute involuntary resettlement impacts. In response to the two aforementioned impacts on
land use caused by the project, the revised Land Administration Law (effective January 1, 2020) has
significantly standardized land acquisition and resettlement practices in both rural and urban areas.
It clarifies the scope of public interest land acquisition, strengthens pre-approval risk management,
enhances information disclosure and public participation (including hearings) during the process,
and requires signing agreements with landowners and users before approval. The law mandates
advance allocation of compensation funds and establish compensation standards based on
"comprehensive land price zones," which must be adjusted or reissued at least every three years. It
explicitly guarantees fair compensation for affected individuals, ensuring "no reduction in the original
living standards of farmers whose land is expropriated." This comprehensive approach safeguards
affected parties’ rights, sustains livelihoods, and improves living conditions, aligning with the World
Bank's core principles. For projects involving marine areas, on-site verification confirms all activities
are conducted within state-owned waters, posing no livelihood impact. Such marine area usage
requires only domestic administrative approvals.



                                                    69
109.     The assessment found that, in terms of practical effectiveness, the land acquisition and
resettlement policy management system currently lacks requirements for process supervision and
monitoring of other types of projects, including land leasing, except for compensation and
resettlement in hydro power resettlement projects. Furthermore, under the existing land acquisition
management system, Changjiang County and Lingshui County are not required to conduct due
diligence on the land acquisition and resettlement process, nor are they obligated to supervise and
evaluate potential historical legacy issues. As the project involves compensation for attachments to
state-owned land, as well as compensation and resettlement for small-scale collective land use and
temporary land use, and large-scale land leasing activities, and Project Action Plan is being
developed to ensure the project is implemented smoothly and to prevent any lingering issues. The
PAP will involve conducting due diligence and oversight on social risks related to land use, including
a) Conduct due diligence on minor collective land acquisition activities under the project, such as
constructing rural sewage treatment plants, aquaculture water supply/drainage systems, integrated
agricultural waste treatment centers or nature education facilities. Ensure proper compensation and
resettlement measures are in place and that there are no unresolved land issues. b) Participate in
and supervise the entire process of land leasing activities, such as farmland non-point source
pollution control, guarantee voluntary land leasing by farmers and the effective implementation of
the consultation mechanism.
5.4 Labor and Employment
5.4.1 Regulatory and Policy Framework
110.       The Labor Law of the People's Republic of China (2018 Revision) and the Labor Contract
Law of the People's Republic of China (2012 Revision). These laws cover a wide range of issues,
including the conclusion, performance, modification, termination, and dissolution of labor contracts,
as well as labor safety and health, special protection for female workers and juvenile workers,
vocational training, social insurance, and welfare. Their purpose is to protect the legitimate rights
and interests of laborers, adjust labor relations, and promote economic development and social
progress. Specifically, the Labor Law of the People's Republic of China (2018 Revision) stipulates
that laborers have the rights to equal employment and selection of occupations, obtainment of labor
remuneration, rest and vacation, labor safety and health protection, receipt of vocational skill training,
enjoyment of social insurance and welfare, and filing of labor disputes. It explicitly prohibits the use
of child labor and forced labor. Meanwhile, the Labor Contract Law of the People's Republic of China
(2012 Revision) further clarifies the obligation of employers to sign labor contracts with laborers,
stipulates the conditions for the conclusion of indefinite term labor contracts, and specifies the
circumstances under which labor contracts may be terminated.
111.     Furthermore, there is a series of supporting labor and social security laws and regulations,
such as the Labor Supervision Inspection Regulations (2004) and the Regulations on Ensuring
Timely Payment of Migrant Workers' Wages (2020), which promote the implementation of the system
norms through enhanced policy interpretation and law popularization, to safeguard the legitimate
rights and interests of specific groups such as migrant workers.
112.     In accordance with national regulations, the Hainan Provincial Government has enacted a
series of laws and regulations to protect workers' rights. These include the 'Opinions on the
Implementation of the Regulations on Guaranteeing Migrant Workers' Wage Payments' (Qiong Fu
Ban [2021] No. 56), issued by the Hainan Provincial People's Government Office; the 'Measures for
the Guarantee of Migrant Workers' Wages in Construction Projects'; and the 'Provisions for the
Implementation of the Trade Union Law of the People's Republic of China (2025 Revision)'. These
regulations aim to safeguard migrant workers' legal rights, including personal, property, and labor
rights, while ensuring their homestead use and land contract management rights are legally
protected. The laws also define employers' responsibilities, such as establishing robust corporate
governance systems and ensuring migrant workers participate in democratic management. They
also specify wage payment standards, methods, cycles and deadlines to ensure that workers receive
their due compensation. Clear responsibilities have been established for governments and relevant
departments at all levels to effectively protect migrant workers' rights.




                                                   70
5.4.2 Implementation mechanism
113.     Overall, China and Hainan Province have established a comprehensive, systematic, and
continuously improving labor security system. This mechanism features a complete legal framework,
based on the Constitution and dominated by labor laws and regulations, supplemented by numerous
administrative regulations, departmental rules, and local regulations. It clarifies rights in various
aspects such as labor contracts, wage payment, working hours, rest and leave, labor safety and
health, social insurance, and women's protection. Specifically:
⚫   Labor Rights Protection and Dispute Resolution Mechanism: 1）1) Fully implement the
    labor contract system to clarify the rights and obligations of employers and employees alike,
    thereby standardizing employment practices from the outset;2) A wage payment guarantee
    mechanism has been established, including the wage guarantee fund system and the
    emergency revolving fund system for unpaid wages, to severely crack down on malicious wage
    arrears. The minimum wage standard system is dynamically adjusted to ensure the basic living
    standards of low-income workers;3) Established a comprehensive social security system
    covering all urban and rural residents, including pension insurance, medical insurance,
    unemployment insurance, work-related injury insurance, and maternity insurance, thereby
    building a robust labor protection framework;4) Continuous enhancement of occupational safety
    and health, with the legal and regulatory framework for workplace safety becoming increasingly
    robust; 5) Establishment of a labor dispute resolution mechanism, forming a diversified system
    of "negotiation, mediation, arbitration, and litigation" that are interconnected. Labor and
    personnel dispute arbitration institutions have handled a large number of labor dispute cases,
    efficiently and conveniently safeguarding the legitimate rights and interests of workers.
⚫   Labor Law Enforcement: A four-tier labor inspection network has been established, spanning
    the national, provincial, municipal and county levels. Regular special enforcement campaigns
    (e.g. the Wage Arrears Eradication Initiative) address persistent violations in key sectors such
    as construction, as well as emerging employment models. These violations include child labor,
    forced labor, unpaid overtime, and non-compliance with social insurance. A 'blacklist' system for
    wage arrears owed to migrant workers has been implemented, with joint sanctions imposed on
    entities and individuals with severe credit deficiencies in areas such as government funding,
    procurement, bidding, production licensing, financing, and market access, thereby increasing
    the cost of violations. Cases suspected of criminal offences such as refusal to pay labor
    remuneration are promptly referred to by public security authorities for criminal prosecution.
⚫   Women's Rights in Enterprises: 1) Legislative prohibition of gender discrimination: The
    Employment Promotion Law and the Women's Rights Protection Law (2024), for example,
    explicitly prohibit the refusal of employment on the basis of gender, as well as higher hiring
    standards, except for occupations deemed unsuitable for women by the state. These laws
    ensure that women have the same labor rights as men, thus upholding gender equality and
    ensuring that they receive equal pay for equal work. 2) Special labor protections: Strict
    enforcement of prohibited occupations for female employees. Women in the 'three periods'
    (pregnancy, childbirth and lactation) are given special protection, including protection against
    wage reduction, dismissal or unilateral termination of employment contracts during these
    periods. 3) Women's career advancement: The state implements various measures to support
    women's participation in vocational training and skill certification, enhancing their employability.
5.4.3 Institutional organization and performance
114.      In order to address labor and employment management, the governments at all levels in
Hainan Province, as well as in Changjiang and Lingshui Counties, have set up management
institutions that coordinate the work of various functional departments. These institutions have clearly
defined responsibilities and effective management systems. The specific institutions and their
functions are as follows:
115.     The provincial human resources and social security department: 1) is responsible for
drafting relevant laws and regulations, formulating departmental regulations, and organizing their
implementation to ensure the implementation of policies and regulations; 2) coordinates the
establishment of a comprehensive social security system covering urban and rural areas, including



                                                   71
social insurance for old-age, unemployment, and work-related injuries, as well as supplementary
insurance. Formulates policies for the transfer of social insurance relationships to ensure smooth
transfer and continuation of social insurance relationships. Assumes the administrative supervision
responsibility for social insurance funds to ensure the safety and effective use of funds; 3) Formulate
and implement medium-to-long-term development plans and regulatory systems for labor and social
security supervision. Investigate and supervise major labor law violations, and participate in handling
emergencies caused by such violations. Promote the establishment of a law-abiding and integrity-
based labor system, and oversee the public disclosure of nationally significant labor law violations.
116.      County Human Resources and Social Security Bureau:1) Ensure effective
implementation of all labor laws, regulations, and rules, and safeguard the legitimate rights and
interests of laborers;2) Conduct supervision and inspection of employers' compliance with labor laws,
regulations, including labor insurance, labor safety, labor environment, working conditions, minimum
wage guarantee, and labor contracts;3) Coordinate the establishment of a multi-level social security
system covering urban and rural areas, formulate and implement policies and standards for social
insurance, including pension, unemployment, and work injury insurance, as well as supplementary
insurance;4) Implement the labor dispute mediation and arbitration system and labor relations
policies, improve the consultation and coordination mechanism for labor relations, organize the
implementation of labor inspection, coordinate workers' rights protection work, and investigate and
deal with major cases in accordance with the law.
117.      The All-China Federation of Trade Unions/Local Trade Unions/Industrial Trade Unions:
Oversee and assist government agencies and enterprises in implementing national policies, laws,
and standards on occupational safety and health. Provide guidance to help workers legally establish
and fulfill labor contracts with employers, while establishing collective bargaining mechanisms to
protect workers' rights. Monitor continuous improvements in working conditions, document major
accident risks and severe occupational hazards for future reference, and ensure follow-up on
corrective actions by enterprises.
118.     Township government: responsible for the daily work and routine inspection of public
safety, workers' health and safety, and emergency rescue in the area
119.      Changjiang County and Lingshui County Human Resources and Social Security
Bureaus: Responsible for rights protection, labor disputes, and skills training management. Their
office operations and staff salaries are funded by public finances. In order to strengthen the
protection of labor rights, the Human Resources and Social Security Bureau of Lingshui County have
set up a Labor Security Office with one member of staff. This office is dedicated to standardizing
employment practices, actively resolving labor disputes and fostering harmonious workplace
relationships. Meanwhile, Changjiang County's Human Resources and Social Security Bureau
establish Three-Level Management Mechanism and One-Stop Comprehensive Governance,
Employment and Labor Relations Office with one member of staff, responsible for overseeing
corporate labor relations management, including labor contracts, collective agreements,
employment registration and labor dispatch administration. The office ensures compliance with
regulations on working hours, rest periods and holidays, while implementing special labor protections
against illegal child labor, female labor and underage labor. Four personnel are also stationed at the
County Comprehensive Law Enforcement Bureau to coordinate city-wide efforts in addressing wage
arrears, managing the National Wage Arrears Platform and supervising cases involving unpaid
wages for migrant workers. The Lingshui County Labor and Social Security Bureau have set up a
Labor Security Office, staffed by one person, to strengthen governance of the root causes of wage
arrears, promote implementation of the wage payment guarantee system and effectively safeguard
workers' legitimate rights and interests. Meanwhile, Changjiang County has set up a Labor and
Personnel Dispute Arbitration Institute comprising five members of staff. The Institute is responsible
for mediating and arbitrating labor and personnel disputes across the county, guiding and
participating in the handling of major cases, and providing guidance on preventing labor and
personnel disputes. In terms of vocational skills training, the Human Resources and Social Security
Bureau in Changjiang County has assigned one staff member to the Employment Division.
Meanwhile, the Employment Service Center (a secondary unit) has three personnel in the Vocational
Capacity Building Section who are responsible for overseeing vocational training programmes
across the county. In Lingshui County, two members of staff operate a dedicated training center that


                                                  72
manages all vocational training activities via the 'Hainan Vocational Training Information
Management System'. In response to market demands, the county collaborates with townships to
mobilize local surveyors, employment service stations and village committees to conduct thorough
assessments of residents' employment and training preferences. Third-party training institutions are
then engaged to deliver vocational skills programmes based on these needs.
120.      Based on interviews with the Human Resources and Social Security Bureaus of Changjiang
and Lingshui Counties, as well as field research, both counties have achieved remarkable results in
protecting workers' rights. Since 2025, Changjiang County has helped 490 workers recover
6,764,805 yuan in unpaid wages. From January 2024 to February 2025, Lingshui County resolved
240 cases of unpaid wages involving 5,232 workers, totaling 120.7565 million yuan. By February
2025, 132 cases had been resolved, recovering 47.2804 million yuan for 2,550 workers and
effectively resolving numerous wage disputes while safeguarding the legitimate rights of migrant
workers. In 2025, 134 cases were filed, of which 140 were concluded through arbitration (including
eight unresolved cases from the end of 2024). This included 107 adjudicated cases and 32 mediated
cases, with one case withdrawn. The total amount involved exceeded 1.2 million yuan. Additionally,
