Changjiang County has set up employment stations tailored to the local industries of each township
and organized specialized training programmes for ethnic minorities, such as leather stool making.
Since 2025, 53 training sessions have been conducted, benefiting 3,071 participants. Lingshui
County utilizes the 'Hainan Vocational Training Information Management System' in alignment with
market demands. In collaboration with townships, the county mobilizes township investigators,
employment stations and village committees to conduct in-depth surveys on employment and
training preferences. Third-party training institutions then provide vocational skills training based on
these needs. From 2023 to September 2025, a total of 284 vocational training programmes were
conducted, covering occupations such as electrician, elderly care worker, landscape gardener, drone
pilot, Chinese chef, Western pastry chef, childcare worker and Dajia seafood porridge maker. A total
of 16,840 people participated in the training, including 8,369 female trainees.
5.4.4 Assessment Summary of Labor Rights and Protection System
121.       The assessment found that the labor rights risk management systems in Changjiang and
Lingshui counties comply with the World Bank's Core Principle#3. Firstly, a relatively comprehensive
labor rights protection system has been established and implemented at national, provincial (Hainan),
county (Changjiang and Lingshui) levels. This system aims to safeguard workers' rights and promote
harmonious and stable labor relations. Secondly, dedicated administrative departments have been
set up at all levels of government with clearly defined responsibilities and stable funding. Third, a
tripartite consultation mechanism involving government authorities, trade unions and enterprises has
been established to address major labor-related issues jointly. This mechanism ensures the
enforcement of labor laws and the protection of workers' rights through consultations between the
government, employers and workers. Furthermore, county-level governments have established
comprehensive labor dispute resolution mechanisms, including arbitration and court litigation, to
provide workers with legal recourse and protect their legitimate rights. For migrant workers, who are
a vulnerable group, the government has implemented measures such as the 'Regulations on
Ensuring Migrant Workers' Wage Payments' to strengthen wage supervision and prevent wage
arrears. Field research and interviews revealed that, thanks to daily monitoring, green channel
services and platform management, migrant workers receive their wages on time and in full.
5.5 Ethnic minorities and vulnerable groups
5.5.1 Regulatory and Policy Framework
122.      Policy Basis for Safeguarding Ethnic Minority Development Rights: The Law of the People's
Republic of China on Regional Ethnic Autonomy stipulates that when developing resources or
undertaking construction projects in ethnic autonomous areas, the state shall consider the interests
of these areas, make arrangements conducive to their economic development, and accommodate
the production and living needs of local ethnic minorities. Furthermore, higher-level state organs
should incorporate major ecological balance and environmental protection projects in ethnic
autonomous areas into national economic and social development plans. From the perspective of
public consultation, the Interim Regulations on the Procedures for Major Administrative Decisions
stipulate that prior public participation must be conducted when formulating important plans and


                                                   73
decisions concerning economic and social development, or when implementing major public
construction projects within an administrative region. These regulations systematically outline the
timing, formats, procedures, and documentation requirements for public participation. Based on
these two regulations, Hainan Province has formulated a five-year plan for the development of ethnic
minorities. On 4 January 2022, the Hainan Provincial Ethnic and Religious Affairs Commission
issued the 'Hainan Province 14th Five-Year Plan for the High-Quality Development of Ethnic Affairs',
setting out a series of requirements, including promoting common prosperity and development
among all ethnic groups, accelerating economic growth in ethnic regions, developing distinctive
ethnic cultural tourism industries and fostering extensive exchanges and integration among ethnic
groups. The 'Hainan Province Regulations on the Protection of the Rights and Interests of Dispersed
Ethnic Minorities' are tailored to the specific circumstances of ethnic minorities in Hainan. Adopting
multiple measures, it focuses on three key areas: promoting the socio-economic development of
ethnic minority towns; enhancing urban ethnic work mechanisms; and addressing urgent issues in
the protection of dispersed ethnic minorities' rights. The regulations provide detailed provisions to
tackle these urgent challenges. At county level, the 'Autonomous Regulations of Changjiang Li
Autonomous County' and 'Autonomous Regulations of Lingshui Li Autonomous County' stipulate that
quotas and proportions of the Li ethnic group and other ethnic representatives in autonomous county
People's Congresses shall be determined in accordance with legal provisions. The Standing
Committee of the People's Congress of autonomous counties must include ethnic minority members,
and Li citizens exercising regional autonomy must serve as chairpersons or vice-chairpersons. The
People's Government of autonomous counties shall comprise ethnic minority personnel, and the
county magistrate shall be a Li citizen. These provisions ensure, from an organizational perspective,
the status of ethnic minorities as masters of their own affairs, as well as their right to manage internal
ethnic affairs. When handling special issues involving local ethnic groups, autonomous organs must
consult representatives of all ethnic groups fully and respect their opinions. This guarantees ethnic
minorities' right to express their views and participate in matters affecting their interests and ethnic
development.
123.       Vulnerable groups constitute a special segment of society characterized by economic
disadvantage in resource allocation, low quality of life, and fragile resilience. In China today, these
groups primarily include impoverished urban and rural residents, displaced farmers, persons with
disabilities, women, the elderly, and children. China and Hainan Province have established a series
of systems to support vulnerable groups, as follows:
124.      Poverty Alleviation System: China achieved comprehensive poverty eradication by 2020.
Current efforts primarily focus on households that have escaped poverty but face relapsed risks due
to various factors, general farming households at risk of falling into poverty, or those experiencing
severe hardship in basic living due to significant rigid expenditures or drastic income reductions
caused by emergencies or other factors, thereby facing risks of returning to or falling into poverty. In
response, the General Office of the CPC Central Committee and the General Office of the State
Council issued the "Opinions on Reforming and Improving the Social Assistance System" (Document
No. 18 [2020]) in August 2020. This document mandates the coordinated development of the social
assistance system to consolidate poverty alleviation achievements and effectively safeguard the
basic livelihood security floor. It provides minimum living allowances to households where the per
capita income of cohabiting family members falls below the local subsistence level and meets
specified asset criteria. Special assistance and support shall be provided to urban and rural elderly
people, people with disabilities, and minors who lack the capacity to work, have no source of
livelihood, have no legally obligated people to provide support, or whose legally obligated people are
unable to fulfill their obligations. At the same time, corresponding specialized social assistance in
areas such as medical care, housing, education, and employment shall be provided based on actual
needs. Low-income families that do not qualify for subsistence or special hardship assistance, as
well as families facing severe basic living difficulties due to significant fixed expenditures, shall
receive targeted social assistance in areas such as medical care, housing, education, and
employment, or other necessary relief measures based on actual needs. Emergency social
assistance shall be provided to families or individuals facing temporary hardship in basic living due
to sudden events, accidental injuries, major illnesses, impacts from infectious disease outbreaks or
other public health emergencies, or other special circumstances, as well as to those temporarily in
distress or without means of subsistence. Assistance should be provided to victims of natural


                                                   74
disasters. Based on this foundation, the General Office of the Hainan Provincial People's
Government issued several policy documents, including the 'Implementation Plan for Reforming and
Improving the Social Assistance System in Hainan Province' (Qiong Ban Fa [2021] No. 52), the
'Measures for Identifying Persons Eligible for Special Support in Hainan Province', and the 'Notice
on Further Strengthening and Standardizing Care Services for Persons in Special Need Receiving
Dispersed Support' from the Hainan Provincial Department of Civil Affairs. These documents clarify
the identification criteria and procedures for various assistance recipients, including those eligible for
subsistence allowances, special support and temporary assistance. Hainan Province publishes
urban and rural subsistence allowance standards, special hardship support standards and policies
annually, which are formulated uniformly by local governments at or above county level. Standards
vary across regions.
125.       Protection of Women and Children's Rights: Regarding gender equality and women's
development, the Law of the People's Republic of China on the Protection of Women's Rights and
Interests (revised in 2018) mandates safeguarding women's lawful rights and interests, promoting
gender equality, and explicitly guarantees women's equal rights to labor and social security. For
instance, the law stipulates that women enjoy equal rights with men in rural land contracting
operations, distribution of collective economic organization income, use of compensation for land
acquisition or requisition, and residential land use. No organization or individual may infringe upon
women's rights within rural economic organizations on grounds of marital status, including being
unmarried, married, divorced, or widowed. In September 2022, the State Council issued the China
Women's Development Outline (2021-2030), setting the following development goals: thorough
implementation of the fundamental national policy of gender equality, and innovation and
improvement of institutional mechanisms to promote gender equality and women's comprehensive
development. Women shall enjoy equal access to comprehensive health services throughout their
entire life cycle, with their health levels continuously improving. Women shall enjoy equal rights to
education, with their quality and capabilities continuously enhanced. Women shall enjoy equal
economic rights, with their economic status steadily improving. Women shall enjoy equal political
rights, with their level of participation in the management of state affairs and economic, cultural, and
social affairs gradually increasing. Women will enjoy equal access to multi-tiered, sustainable social
security with steadily improving benefits. The legal and policy framework supporting family
development will be further refined, and socialist family values and new social norms will be widely
promoted. The concept of gender equality will become more deeply rooted in society, and the
environment for women's development will be further optimized. The legal system will be
strengthened to effectively safeguard women's legitimate rights and interests. Women's sense of
fulfillment, happiness, and security will be significantly enhanced. Women's federations are
established at the township level, and village women's federations (village management
organizations' two committees: village committee and Party branch committee must include at least
one female member). The Law of the People's Republic of China on the Protection of Minors (2020
revision) stipulates that minors enjoy all rights equally under the law and shall not be discriminated
against on the basis of their own or their parents' or other guardians' ethnicity, race, gender,
household registration, occupation, religious beliefs, educational background, family circumstances,
or physical and mental health status. This law details provisions for family protection, school
protection, social protection, online protection, governmental protection, and judicial protection of
minors.80. At the provincial level, the Hainan Women's Development Plan (2021–2030) prioritizes
equal access for women to the five main types of social insurance: maternity, medical, pension,
unemployment and work injury insurance. The Plan explicitly strengthens social assistance safety
nets for women facing economic hardship and enhances care services for women. For women's
development, the Plan establishes eight domains — health, education, the economy, participation in
decision-making and management, social security, family building, the environment, and law —
proposing 74 primary objectives and 90 strategic measures. The Hainan Provincial Regulations on
Safeguarding Women's Rights and Interests (2008) aim to protect women's rights comprehensively,
emphasizing the fundamental national policy of gender equality and prohibiting all forms of gender
discrimination. The provisions offer specific guidance on political, cultural and educational, labor and
social security, property, personal, and marriage and family rights. The Hainan Provincial Children's
Development Plan (2021–2030) sets out 71 primary objectives and 84 strategic measures across
seven areas: child health and safety; education; welfare; family life; the environment; and legal
protection.


                                                   75
5.5.2 Implementation mechanism
126.      Ethnic Minority Management System: At the institutional level, China's ethnic minority
management system complies with the Constitution and relevant laws and regulations on ethnic
affairs. When dealing with issues affecting different ethnic groups in the region, they must consult
their representatives fully and respect their views. Autonomous organs in ethnic autonomous regions
ensure that all ethnic citizens within their jurisdictions enjoy the civil rights stipulated by the
Constitution. Meanwhile, in compliance with the general requirements for the evaluation and
management of construction projects, relevant public consultations are conducted. Every five years,
each county formulates development plans based on the unique characteristics of ethnic minority
regions and implements projects for regional development and cultural preservation. These plans
require economic, cultural, educational and healthcare policies to priorities ethnic minority areas,
thereby promoting shared prosperity and the development of all ethnic groups. In ethnic minority
regions, economic development projects are usually started by villages and townships based on
local requirements. Each year, village officials organize public consultations through community
meetings and other locally appropriate communication methods to collect input from the grassroots.
These proposals are then submitted to township governments, who forward them to the Ethnic and
Religious Affairs Department or other relevant authorities. After reviewing the reports, these
departments conduct on-site inspections and evaluations. Based on the necessity and urgency of
the Projects, they compile a consolidated list and submit it in batches to higher authorities for funding
approval. This demonstrates that the Project was developed to address the specific needs of ethnic
minority regions, incorporating their perspectives fully, thereby securing broad support from local
communities. Existing mechanisms in these regions, such as feasibility studies and social stability
risk assessments during the preparatory phase, have been maintained in managing individual
projects. These evaluations systematically incorporate public consultation and negotiation processes
to ensure respect for ethnic minority communities. Understanding provincial and county-level
governance frameworks enables the current ethnic affairs management system to guarantee
thorough consultation with minority residents and safeguard their right to prior informed consent. The
effective operation of these management systems ensures widespread support from ethnic minority
populations.
127.      Vulnerable Groups Rights Protection System: The protection system for the rights and
interests of vulnerable groups is a comprehensive and systematic project. Based on robust laws and
regulations, it provides a solid legal foundation for safeguarding the rights and interests of vulnerable
groups. Through collaboration between multiple departments, the legitimate rights and interests of
vulnerable groups, such as the elderly, disabled people, women and children, are fully protected.
The All-China Women's Federation, corporate women's affairs departments and grassroots women's
organizations work together to safeguard the rights of low-income groups and protect women's rights,
providing comprehensive support for women's development. National and local governments have
established robust institutional mechanisms for low-income groups, including policy frameworks,
budget allocations and organizational arrangements. These mechanisms protect the legitimate rights
of impoverished households in various programmes and effectively manage support and
development initiatives for disadvantaged families.
5.5.3 Institutional organization and Implementation Performance
128.      Minority Affairs Management Institutions have been established at national, provincial and
local levels in accordance with the law. These institutions comprise multiple departments that are
jointly committed to safeguarding the equal rights and legitimate interests of ethnic minorities, as
well as promoting the common prosperity and development of all ethnic groups. The main
management institutions and their responsibilities are outlined below.
   •    Provincial Ethnic Affairs Departments: Responsible for coordinating and promoting
       relevant departments to fulfill their duties in ethnic affairs, facilitating the implementation and
       integration of ethnic policies in economic development and social undertakings; drafting
       special plans for ethnic minority affairs and supervising their implementation; participating in
       the formulation of development plans for ethnic minorities and ethnic regions in relevant
       economic and social fields; promoting the establishment and improvement of a
       comprehensive evaluation and monitoring system for ethnic minority affairs development;



                                                   76
      advancing the construction of ethnic affairs service systems and the informatization of ethnic
      affairs management; Research issues concerning economic development and social
      undertakings in ethnic minority groups and regions, proposing special policy
      recommendations; participate in coordinating scientific and technological development and
      economic-technical cooperation in ethnic regions; contribute to formulating plans for ethnic
      minority talent development, assisting relevant departments in cultivating, educating, and
      utilizing ethnic minority cadres.
  •    County Ethnic Affairs Departments (County Ethnic Affairs Bureaus): Implement the Party and
      state's policies, laws, and regulations on ethnic affairs, and execute decisions and
      deployments from provincial and county Party committees and governments; Organize
      publicity campaigns on ethnic theories, policies, laws, regulations, and fundamental
      knowledge to uphold ethnic unity and foster a sense of community for the Chinese nation;
      Oversee and guide the implementation of ethnic laws, regulations, and policies within the
      county while strengthening compliance inspections; Supervise the handling of matters
      concerning the protection of ethnic minority rights and interests; Coordinate major matters
      concerning ethnic relations, maintain social stability and national unity; participate in drafting
      development plans for economic and social sectors in ethnic areas across the county, analyze
      issues in economic development and social undertakings in ethnic regions, and propose
      policy recommendations; organize the county government's Li and Miao ethnic groups' "March
      Third" festival celebrations and coordinate participation in provincial-level ethnic cultural and
      sports events; implement ethnic education policies and participate in formulating and
      executing plans for ethnic minority talent development; undertake specific tasks related to
      liaising with ethnic minority cadres.
129.      At the county level, the Changjiang County Ethnic Affairs Bureau shares office space with
the County Party Committee United Front Work Department. Its staff includes one director and two
deputy directors, with the bureau director concurrently serving as deputy director of the United Front
Work Department. The United Front Work Department allocates one ethnic affairs management
position. The Lingshui Li Autonomous County Ethnic Affairs Bureau has four administrative positions:
one director, one deputy director, and two leadership positions within its internal departments.
Internal departments include the General Affairs Office and the Ethnic Affairs Development Office.
The County Ethnic Affairs Bureau is responsible for implementing national and Hainan provincial
laws, regulations, and policies concerning ethnic affairs; coordinating ethnic relations; promoting
ethnic unity and progress; and advancing the development of ethnic minority culture, economy, and
other undertakings.
130.     In order to support different vulnerable groups, national, provincial and municipal
governments have set up specialized departments, including Rural Revitalization Bureau, Women's
Federations and Civil Affairs Offices. These agencies are responsible for formulating policies and
plans to consolidate achievements in alleviating poverty and supporting vulnerable populations.
They coordinate assistance programmes for low-income groups, develop plans for women and
children, and oversee the management of persons with disabilities, the elderly left behind, and
minors. Each department allocates personnel and budgets and conducts performance evaluations.
The specific measures are as follows:
  •   Civil Affairs Bureau: As the primary and core department for building the social assistance
      system, its support for low-income populations primarily includes: 1) Minimum Living
      Allowance (MLA): Providing basic living assistance to residents whose per capita household
      income falls below the local MLA standard;2) Assistance and Support for Persons in Extreme
      Poverty: Providing basic living conditions and care services to elderly individuals, persons
      with disabilities, and minors who lack the capacity to work, have no source of income, and
      have no legally obligated caregivers or whose legally obligated caregivers are unable to fulfill
      their duties; 3) Temporary Assistance: Providing emergency and transitional assistance to
      families or individuals facing basic living difficulties due to sudden, urgent, or temporary
      circumstances.
  •   Women's Federation: Responsible for organizing and guiding women to play a unique role
      in production and daily life, safeguarding the lawful rights and interests of women and children,



                                                  77
       providing assistance to abused women and children, and organizing initiatives such as the
       creation of civilized families.
   •   Disability Federation: Responsible for safeguarding the civil rights of people with disabilities,
       listening to their opinions and needs, and serving their interests. Promote awareness of
       disability issues, mobilize society to understand, respect, care for, and assist people with
       disabilities, and eliminate discrimination, prejudice, and barriers. Assist the government in
       formulating and implementing development plans for disability-related undertakings,
       advancing rehabilitation, education, employment, poverty alleviation, rights protection, cultural
       and sports activities, social security, application of science and technology, and disability
       prevention. Improve the environment and conditions for people with disabilities to participate
       in social life.
   •   Rural Revitalization Bureau (or relevant functions may be undertaken by the Department of
       Agriculture and Rural Affairs): Responsible for development-oriented assistance in industries
       and employment for low-income rural populations, consolidating the achievements of poverty
       alleviation, and preventing households that have escaped poverty but remain unstable,
       households at risk of falling back into poverty, and households facing sudden severe hardship
       from relapsing into poverty.
   •   Human Resources and Social Security Bureau: Responsible for providing vocational skills
       training, employment assistance, and entrepreneurship support to low-income individuals.
   •   Medical Security Bureau: Responsible for implementing medical assistance policies to
       reduce the medical cost burden on low-income individuals.
   •   Education Bureau: Responsible for implementing educational assistance policies to ensure
       equal access to education for students from low-income families.
   •   Housing and Urban-Rural Development Bureau: Responsible for providing housing
       security to low-income families facing housing difficulties, including public rental housing and
       housing rental subsidies.
   •   Township Governments, Communities/Villages: Townships have appointed supervisors
       for left behind (or vulnerable) minors and established regional elderly care service centers;
       villages/communities have set up elderly care service stations. Township governments have
       established Women's Federation offices, while communities/villages have implemented
       Women's Federation chairperson mechanisms.
131.       At county level, the institutional framework for safeguarding low-income populations in
Changjiang County comprises six departments: the Civil Affairs Bureau, the Education Bureau, the
Housing and Urban-Rural Development Bureau, the Human Resources and Social Security Bureau,
the Agriculture and Rural Affairs Bureau, the Medical Insurance Bureau and the Health Commission.
The Civil Affairs Bureau is responsible for implementing social assistance policies and standards,
coordinating the development of social assistance systems, and managing urban and rural minimum
living allowances, support for destitute individuals, temporary relief, and households near the poverty
line. The bureau oversees the allocation and supervision of financial assistance funds for
disadvantaged groups at the central, provincial and county levels. It also administers county-wide
social assistance information management and guides the identification of low-income families. The
bureau has a dedicated 'Social Assistance Unit' comprising four members of staff: one civil servant,
one public institution employee and two contract workers. This team submits monthly reports on the
management of assistance for online review, conducts quarterly coordination and notification work,
and performs biannual door-to-door inspections covering 30% of newly identified cases.
132.      The consolidation and expansion of poverty alleviation achievements, along with their
integration into rural revitalization, are usually overseen by the Rural Revitalization Bureau. At county
level, a Rural Revitalization Strategy Leadership Group is formed, comprising key officials such as
county and municipal government leaders, township Party committee heads, village Party branch
secretaries and resident work team leaders. This group convenes ad hoc consultation meetings as
needed to address implementation challenges. To prevent poverty relapses, dynamic monitoring and
targeted assistance are implemented, alongside a rapid detection and response mechanism for



                                                   78
populations at risk of falling back into poverty. A grid-based management system ensures the timely
inclusion of eligible individuals in assistance programmes through tiered classification and
standardized procedures. Targeted support measures, including education, healthcare, housing,
social safety nets, access to safe drinking water, employment assistance, financial aid and follow-up
support for relocated poverty alleviation beneficiaries, are delivered to enable early detection,
intervention and assistance. These efforts aim to sustain poverty alleviation outcomes and prevent
relapse into poverty.
133.      In terms of performance implementation, Changjiang County maintained an overall stable
number of urban and rural residents receiving subsistence allowances throughout 2025. The
coverage rate significantly exceeded the provincial average, surpassing the national evaluation
benchmark ahead of schedule. The county has enrolled 359 urban and rural households (866
individuals) in the subsistence allowance programmed, provided assistance to 106 households (113
individuals) living in extreme poverty and made dynamic adjustments to the welfare system for 71
households (99 individuals), ensuring strict policy implementation and precise beneficiary
identification. A total of 683 households (2,648 individuals) were accurately identified as being at the
subsistence allowance threshold, as were 448 families facing rigid expenditure difficulties. By 2025,
a total of 47.414 million yuan in various relief funds had been distributed. Temporary assistance
programmes were implemented, achieving 95% public awareness and supporting 5,000
disadvantaged individuals annually at a cost of 4.5 million yuan. In 2024, 12,830 individuals
(including 5,817 women) received assistance, with 72.862 million yuan in relief funds being
disbursed. In 2025, Lingshui County recorded 2,086 households (2,113 individuals) living in extreme
poverty in both urban and rural areas, as well as 4,020 households (10,309 individuals) receiving
urban and rural subsistence allowances. Temporary assistance covered 1,200 households (4,858
individuals), with 5,303,540.5 yuan in relief funds being disbursed.
5.5.4 Assessment of the Ethnic Minority and Vulnerable Groups Rights Protection
Management System
134.       Field visit found that Lingshui and Changjiang County as Li Autonomous County, there is a
special minority development fund available every year to support the development of various
minority projects in the county. In 2024, Changjiang County allocated 10.84 million yuan from its
Ethnic Minority Development Fund towards regional economic, social and infrastructure projects.
Specifically, 7.1 million yuan was invested in ethnic cultural tourism initiatives, while 3.74 million yuan
was invested in constructing village access roads. These investments have significantly improved
the living and working conditions of residents in ethnic minority areas, thereby contributing to rural
revitalization efforts. The special fund of 80,000 yuan is mainly used for promotion of ethnic culture
in 2025. Changjiang and Lingshui both have plans to protect the culture of ethnic minorities, and
carry out relevant projects every year. For example, to actively explore, protect, inherit and develop
the cultural resources of ethnic minorities, the 'Lingshui Li Autonomous County Intangible Cultural
Heritage Project Representative Inheritors Recognition and Management Measures' were
introduced in Lingshui County. The third batch of 30 intangible cultural heritage inheritors was
officially recognized in 2024. The county organized training for intangible cultural heritage inheritors
and held 11 Li folk song workshops across townships, with almost 600 participants. 66 villages in
eight ethnic minority townships were designated as 'Lingshui Li Autonomous County Intangible
Cultural Heritage Training Centers'. These centers hosted cultural talent performances, band
activities and village engagement programmes, fostering a vibrant rural cultural atmosphere and
advancing the preservation and transmission of intangible heritage. In 2024, "Cultural and Natural
Heritage Day" will host a series of activities to promote and exhibit intangible cultural heritage (ICH).
Through innovative approaches such as 'ICH + cultural creativity', 'ICH + tourism' and 'ICH +
festivals', these events will make ICH more accessible, enabling people of all ethnicities to appreciate
its cultural significance. The initiative aims to foster a vibrant atmosphere for preserving, passing on,
and developing outstanding traditional culture.
135.      Regarding the protection of vulnerable groups' rights: The assessment found that in order
to protect the rights and interests of low-income groups, women, children and the elderly, China has
established a policy and service system that covers the protection of vulnerable groups at all levels,
from national to local. The country has also continuously improved service quality through capacity
building. At county level, in addition to distributing basic support, "full coverage" of assistance has


                                                    79
been ensured. Disabled Persons' Federations (DPFs) at county, township and village levels have
coordinated effectively to implement higher-level policies and local innovative measures at
household and individual levels. This ensures the precise delivery of various subsidies and services
with favorable implementation outcomes.
136.      In conclusion, the assessment shows that the existing provincial and county-level
management systems for ethnic minority affairs ensure thorough consultation and communication
with minority communities. None of the physical activities under this project negatively impact on the
cultural lifestyles or livelihoods of ethnic minorities. Through ecological restoration initiatives and
upgrades to sewage and non-point source pollution control systems, the project contributes to
environmental improvement in the local area, supporting systematic ethnic minority development
plans. Once implemented, the project will generate additional development opportunities for
residents in ethnic minority areas. For instance, the project has created more employment
opportunities. The rural non-point source pollution control project will increase land rental values
through land remediation, enabling migrant workers to earn higher incomes. Incorporating ethnic
minority perspectives into the project's design and implementation requires the adoption of culturally
adaptive measures to solicit feedback from minority groups, ensuring effective participation and
establishing a shared benefit mechanism for all stakeholders.
5.6 Information disclosure and public participation
5.6.1 Regulatory and Policy Framework
137.      In the field of government information disclosure on approval and implementation of major
construction projects. The Opinion of the General Office of the State Council on Promoting
Government Information Disclosure in the Approval and Implementation of Major Construction
Projects (2017) and The "Hainan Provincial People's Government Information Disclosure Measures",
the "Hainan Provincial People's Government Office Government Information Disclosure Guidelines
(2016)", and the "Notice on Issuing the Implementation Opinions on Comprehensively Promoting
Government Affairs Disclosure in the Province" (Qiongbanfa [2016] No.69) jointly issued by the
General Office of the CPC Hainan Provincial Committee and the General Office of the Hainan
Provincial People's Government., require highlighting the focus of disclosure, and in the process of
approval and implementation of major construction projects, focus on disclosing eight types of
information, including approval service information, approval result information, tendering and
bidding information, land acquisition information, major design change information, construction-
related information, quality and safety supervision information, and completion-related information.
Clarify the disclosure subject, and all levels of government and relevant departments shall adhere to
the principle of openness as the norm and non-disclosure as the exception, strictly follow the relevant
provisions of the Regulations on the Administration of the People's Republic of China on the
Disclosure of Government Information, and disclose the information on the Projects they have made
or preserved. Expand disclosure channels, and all levels of government and relevant departments
shall disclose various types of project information in a timely manner through government gazettes,
government websites, new media platforms, and press conferences. Respond promptly to public
concerns. Strengthen the timeliness of disclosure, and the government information generated or
changed during the approval and implementation of major construction projects shall be disclosed
in accordance with the Regulations on the Administration of the People's Republic of China on the
Disclosure of Government Information, and be made public within 20 working days from the date of
the formation or change of the information.
138.    In the area of government information disclosure on public resource allocation, the
Opinions of the General Office of the State Council on Promoting Government Information
Disclosure in the Field of Public Resource Allocation (2017) and The "Hainan Provincial
People's Government Office Government Information Disclosure Guide" (2016) states that the
Hainan Provincial People's Government Website (http://www.hainan.gov.cn) is a
comprehensive platform for the Hainan Provincial People's Government and its departments,
as well as the people's governments of cities, counties (districts), to release government
information and provide online services on the international internet. It requires highlighting key
areas of disclosure, focusing on regulatory information such as work safety, ecological
environment, health and epidemic prevention, land and resources, social credit, transportation,
tourism market, and public resource transactions. The disclosure entities are clearly defined,


                                                  80
adhering to the principle of "who approves, who discloses; who implements, who discloses; who
produces, who discloses." Information on approval results involving administrative approvals
for public resource allocation is disclosed by the approving departments. Channels for
disclosure are expanded, fully leveraging the primary role of government websites to timely
release various types of information in the field of public resource allocation and ensuring
smooth channels for information disclosure upon request. Timeliness in disclosure is
emphasized, adhering to the principle of routine disclosure with non -disclosure being the
exception. Government information generated during the process of public resource allocation
should be disclosed in a timely manner according to the law, except for content involving state
secrets or commercial secrets. In 2024, the total number of information releases on the
provincial government's official website was approximately 31,300, including 25 posts from the
Standing Committee of the Provincial Government, 29 documents from the Provincial
Government, 46 documents from the General Office of the Provincial Government, and 24
issues of the Government Gazette, with a total visitation of 65.11 million. The "Hainan Provinci al
Government Website" WeChat official account published 2,313 pieces of information, with
293,000 followers; Sina Weibo published 3,020 pieces of information, with 28,000 followers.
139.     In terms of public participation and openness regarding major administrative decisions.
The Interim Provisions on Procedures for Major Administrative Decisions (2019) and the
Circular of the General Office of the CPC Hainan Provincial Committee and the General Office
of the Hainan Provincial People's Government on Issuing the Implementation Opinions on
Comprehensively Promoting Government Affairs Disclosure in the Province (Qiongbanfa [2016]
No. 69) stipulate that major administrative decisions must be made in accordance with the
principle of democratic decision-making, with full consideration given to all parties' views. The
public should be able to participate in the decision-making process through various channels
and forms. Opinions can be solicited through various means, such as roundtable discussions,
hearings, on-site visits, written and public opinion surveys, and questionnaires. (2) When a
decision involves the interests of a specific group, the decision-making agency should
communicate with and consult relevant people's organizations, social organizations and public
representatives to fully consider that group's views and suggestions. 3) When a decision is
made public for the purpose of soliciting opinions, the decision-making agency should publish
the decision draft and related materials on government websites and official media accounts
that are easily accessible to the public. The agency should also specify the ways and deadlines
for submitting opinions. The public consultation period should generally be no less than 30 days.
If an urgent situation requires a shorter period, this should be explained. (4) For issues of
general public concern or of a technical or professional nature, the decision-making agency can
provide explanations through expert interviews. 5) If a decision directly affects the interes ts of
citizens, legal people, or other organizations or if there is significant disagreement, a public
hearing may be held. If there are other provisions on holding public hearings in laws, regulations,
or rules, they shall be followed.
140.      Complaints and appeals. The Hainan Provincial Government has set up a
comprehensive petition system to provide citizens with straightforward channels through which
to express their concerns and grievances. The 'Petition Work Regulations' require state bodies
to set up online petition platforms, providing petitioners with a convenient way to submit matters
and check the progress of their petitions online. Petitioners generally use forms such as letters,
phone calls or online submissions to clearly state their name (or organization), legal
identification information, contact details, requests, facts and reasons. State organs must
register all petitions received and make a decision on acceptance within fifteen working days,
informing the petitioner in writing. Where laws and regulations are provided otherwise, those
provisions shall apply. The government promotes the timely and lawful handling of petitions by
state organs through the supervisory role of news media such as television, radio, the internet,
and newspapers. At county level, in addition to setting up the 12345-complaint hotline online,
Lingshui/Changjiang County has also set up an online complaint’s platform
(http://xf.hainan.gov.cn) for collecting public opinions and providing feedback. The
comprehensive governance centers of each county also handle petition work offline promptly
and efficiently.




                                                81
5.6.2 Implementation Mechanism
141.      Information Disclosure and Public Engagement: Interviews with the governments of
Changjiang County and Lingshui County, along with field research, there are two key findings:
1) In compliance with the 'Changjiang District People's Government Disclosure Guidelines', both
county governments have set up official websites and public suggestion boxes. These are used
to publish progress reports on major projects, share policies and best practices for ecological
restoration and environmental protection, and encourage public participation in these initiatives.
2) in recent years, Hainan Province has conducted legislative research through various methods,
including surveys, to gather public feedback on challenges and suggestions regarding coastal
zone ecological protection and restoration. Government representatives have held symposiums
with project implementers, county authorities and stakeholders to address critical issues. The
province has also implemented a public hearing system for major government decisions, legally
soliciting public opinions through hearings and other procedures.3) In addition, the county -
level government's official website now features a 'Government Affairs Updates' column, which
publishes daily updates on the work of county - level government leaders. This further expands
the scope of government transparency and strengthens the connection between the government
and the general public. For instance, the official website of the Changjiang County People's
Government published 10,251 pieces of government information in 2024, while the offici al
website of the Lingshui County People's Government published 422 pieces. As of December
2024, in addition to the government website, Lingshui County had 11 units operating 18
government new media accounts, covering various types of government informatio n disclosure
platforms, such as WeChat subscription accounts, Sina Weibo, TikTok short videos and Toutiao.
This provides the public with more timely and convenient access to information.
142.     Complaint and Grievance Management: Interviews with petition offices in Changjiang
County and Lingshui County, along with field research, there are 3 key findings: 1) Both counties
have established comprehensive mechanisms for preventing, mediating, and resolving social
conflicts in accordance with petition regulations. 2) By enhancing preventive measures,
improving screening and resolution systems, implementing leadership reception channels, and
establishing early warning mechanisms, they have strengthened root cause governance while
expanding the functions of multi-level dispute resolution centers. The county-level case
assignment system for Party and government leaders has been strictly enforced, with dedicated
task forces improving efficiency in handling initial petitions and promptly addressing citizens'
legitimate concerns. 3) To address complaints during project implementation, three effective
mechanisms were developed: Firstly, a joint meeting system for street-level petition work was
established, with chief officials acting as conveners and deputy leaders as co -conveners.
Community committees, local police stations and relevant departments participate in regular
conflict screening and analysis in order to resolve complex cases. Secondly, a grid officer
system was implemented at community level, with each grid staffed by officers to strengthen
risk identification through multidimensional monitoring. Thirdly, a public communication platform
featuring scheduled reception times was created and prominently displayed in communities.
District and street leaders engage directly with citizens to identify root causes and implement
comprehensive solutions to address urgent public concerns.
5.6.3 Institutional organization and Implementation Performance
143.      Provincial and county governments and their township-level institutions, along with
competent authorities at all levels (such as the Bureau of Natural Resources and Planning,
Water Resources Bureau, Ecology and Environment Bureau, Forestry Bureau, etc.): 1)
Safeguarding public participation rights: Governments at all levels should ens ure the public's
rights to information, participation, expression, and supervision, promoting democratic and
scientific decision-making. This includes involving the public in major administrative decision -
making processes through methods such as public consultations and hearings; 2) Disclosure
of government information: Governments should legally disclose government information in a
timely and accurate manner, including but not limited to information on major administrative
decisions, public services, and market regulation. This enhances transparency in government
operations and promotes information symmetry between the government and the public; 3)
Public participation in major administrative decisions: For major administrative decisions


                                               82
involving overall economic and social development and closely related to people's interests,
extensive public opinions should be solicited through methods such as symposium discussions,
consultative consultations, and public opinion surveys. For decisions with high social at tention
and involving people's vital interests, hearings should be held or draft proposals released to the
public to ensure scientific and democratic decision-making; 4) Petition handling: Petition work
serves as an important channel for understanding public sentiment. Governments at all levels
should address public appeals through petition channels, maintain close contact with the people,
and promptly resolve issues raised by the public; 5) Supervision and evaluation: Major
administrative decisions should be subject to oversight by the People's Congress and its
Standing Committee at the same level, in accordance with the law. Incorporating the decision -
making process into government performance evaluations ensures scientific validity and
effectiveness.
144.      Petition institutions and their functional counterparts at all levels to (1) Formulate,
implement and enforce policies, laws and regulations related to petition work. (2) Represent
provincial, county - level and county Party committees and governments in receiving public
petitions and providing legal policy consultations. (3) Handle petition matters assigned by higher
authorities, issue petition requests to relevant units, supervise the resolution of major ca ses
and close cases. (4) Coordinate cross-regional and interdepartmental petition activities, monitor
significant cases, and provide handling recommendations to responsible officials. (5) Solicit
public feedback, promptly submit petition information to government agencies and propose
solutions to critical issues. (6) Guide petition work at all levels, share best practices and develop
improvement measures, and organize training for petition officers, supporting office automation
initiatives. 7) Manage publicity and information dissemination for petition work.
145.     The petition offices in Changjiang and Lingshui counties are responsible for managing
complaints and appeals. Specifically, the Lingshui County Petition Service Center employs two
full-time members of staff in its Letters Processing and Supervision Office, while the Changjiang
County Petition Center employs three. The salaries of both the offices and their personnel are
funded by public funds. Their primary responsibilities include formulating county -wide petition
work strategies, implementing relevant laws and regulations, processing public correspondence,
handling in-person visits, accepting online complaints and investigating petition cases. They
also assist in ensuring the smooth running of major national, provincial and county-level events,
participate in managing incidents affecting social stability, and coordinate issues relating to
petitions that cut across regions, departments and industries. They also support public security
authorities in maintaining normal operations at county Party committees and government offices.
146.      In terms of performance implementation, Changjiang County set up a Comprehensive
Social Governance Center to handle disputes, petitions and significant risks via a one-stop
service system. Eight township mediation centers and 92 village-level service stations were set
up, ensuring comprehensive coverage of mediation institutions at township and village levels.
Since 2024, efforts have focused on resolving conflicts at source. To date, 800 disputes have
been investigated, with 714 successfully resolved, achieving a resolution rate of 89.3%.
Lingshui County has successively established an informatics social management platform (the
Comprehensive Governance Platform), a public legal service network platform, the Fengqiao
'e-Spirit' platform, and a mediation platform. The county has explored innovative social
governance mechanisms, including the '12345 + grid-based + direct linkage' approach, the
'1+2+N' model (one police officer, two auxiliary officers and N grid workers), the 'one village,
one police assistant' model, and the 'public interest litigation + 12345 hotline' approach. In 2024,
mediation organizations at all levels in Lingshui County conducted 1,520 dispute screening
visits, effectively preventing 42 potential conflicts. They mediated 668 disputes, successfully
resolving 648 cases for a success rate of 97.0%, and fulfilled 603 cases for a fulfillment rate of
93.0%.
5.6.4 Assessment Summary of Information Disclosure and Public Participation
System
147.    Firstly, National-level, Hainan Province and the counties of Changjiang and Lingshui
have established comprehensive laws and regulations regarding the implementation of major
projects. These include mechanisms for information disclosure, public participation, appeals,


                                                 83
supervision and evaluation. Secondly, the national and Hainan provincial governments, as well
as the governments of Changjiang and Lingshui counties, have established specialized
administrative departments with clearly defined responsibilities and stable funding sour ces.
These government agencies focus on key areas such as project investment, fiscal funds, critical
livelihoods and public services, in order to implement government information disclosure and
public participation management. Through investigations and interviews, it was found that
Changjiang County and Lingshui County had extensively involved the public in their
environmental remediation and ecological restoration projects. This involved carrying out social
stability risk assessments and environmental impact assessments, as well as other procedures
such as on-site inspections, addressing public concerns and seeking opinions. These efforts
ensured that the public had the right to be informed, to participate, to express their views, and
to supervise project development. Furthermore, the governments of Hainan Province,
Changjiang County and Lingshui County have set up a comprehensive complaints and appeals
system to give citizens easy access to channels through which they can express their concerns
and grievances. The assessment found that Changjiang County and Lingshui County have well-
established and effective public participation mechanisms for key and large-scale projects, with
complaint and appeal mechanisms functioning effectively at all levels.
148.      However, the assessment also found that non-priority, small-scale project activities,
particularly those exempt from social stability risk assessments and environmental impact
assessment, such as rural non-point source pollution control, aquaculture wastewater pipeline
upgrades and urban-rural sewage treatment sub-projects, have historically lacked
comprehensive stakeholder participation mechanisms throughout their entire project cycle.
Most critically, these projects failed to establish effective, timely, whole process community
engagement frameworks for diverse stakeholder groups. Therefore, the current public
participation mechanisms in both counties need to be further refined at the sub -project level.
This requires ensuring that each sub-project utilizes multiple channels to promptly conduct
meaningful public consultations and information disclosure. It is essential to identify and assess
potential environmental and social impacts and risks, while understanding the needs of various
stakeholders—particularly vulnerable groups (such as the elderly, women, and low-income
populations) and those directly affected. Public feedback and targeted mitigation measures
should be incorporated into the planning, design, and implementation of relevant project
activities. As mentioned in the previous section, special attention should be paid to ensuring
participation of, and equitable benefits for, vulnerable groups. During the participation process,
measures should be taken to adapt to the cultural appropriate way of ethnic minorities, based
on local conditions. For example, their oral local languages could be used for communication.

149.      Stakeholder engagement is an important part of this report and one of the core

identified by categorizing them into groups that are affected by the activities, interested in the
activities, and able to influence the activities. It mainly includes government agencies at all
levels, villages and communities, social organizations such as activity implementation and
operation agencies, and affected people. The identification of stakeholders for this project is
shown in Annex 4. In the process of evaluating and preparing the report, a large number of
stakeholder engagement and consultation activities were carried out in Changjiang County,
Lingshui County and the Project implementation area, including online meetings and on -site
discussions and visits to relevant government departments in Changjiang County and Lingshui
County in August 2025 and September 2025, and public consultation meeting were held with
stakeholders on this report in early December 2025.

Program-for-Results (PforR) financing instrument to the government departments of Changjiang
and Lingshui counties in August 2025 and September 2025, including its relevant requirements,
environmental and social policies, implementation and management arrangements, operational
procedures, and the preparation of assessment and program documents.

(Lingshui County), etc., including such as town-level land acquisition departments, staff of
affected sub-district offices / neighborhood committees, and units and residents that are
expected to be affected by the proposed project activities (see Annex 9 for detailed consultation
records).The cumulative number of participants in the discussion was about 50. At the same

governments/communities in Changjiang County and Lingshui County were also collected for

6.1.2 Participation in this report
152.    The first draft of the first version of this report was sent to the Project Management
Offices (PMOs) of Changjiang County and Lingshui County on November 18, 2025, which
subsequently circulated it to relevant provincial government departments, government
departments in the Project implementation areas, as well as community residents and
enterprise representatives for comments. The World Bank team received written feedback on
November 30, 2025. In parallel, the PPMOs and PMOs of Changjiang and Lingshui counties
organized three consultation meetings between stakeholders and the World Bank team in early
December 2025 on the ESSA report. Participants included the Political and Legal Affairs
Commission, Petition Office, Ecology and Environment Bureau, Natural Resources and
Planning Bureau, Department of Agriculture and Rural Affairs, Forestry Bureau, Water
Resources Bureau, Civil Affairs Bureau, Human Resources and Social Security Bureau, Ethnic
and Religious Affairs Bureau, Culture and Tourism Bureau, the Women’s Federation, the Project
Implementation Company, as well as key representatives from Qicha Town in Changjiang
County, Sancai townships in Lingshui County, and other relevant localities. The Project and
summary of the report were presented, including the purpose, mandate, content, research
methodology, conclusions and recommendations of the ESSA. The main issues discussed at
the meeting included:
1) whether the laws and regulations cited in the report are accurate and complete;
2) whether the analysis and assessment of the legal and regulatory framework are consistent with
   actual conditions;
3) whether the description of institutional arrangements is accurate and whether the assessment of
   institutional capacity is appropriate; and
4) whether participants agree with the report’s conclusions, in particular the identified gaps between
   China’s domestic environmental and social systems and the World Bank Program-for-Results
   (PforR) policy requirements, and whether the proposed action recommendations are feasible.
Overall, consultation participants expressed positive views on the report, endorsed the
proposed action recommendations, and provided written comments and suggested revisions,
including comments on the validity period of certain policy documents, supplementary
regulatory references, and institutional mandates and responsibilities. The World Bank
Environmental and Social team carefully considered all comments, maintained detailed records,
and made corresponding revisions to the report. The main comments raised during the
consultation and the corresponding revisions are documented in detail in Annex 6.
6.2 Project grievance mechanism
153.     Existing grievance mechanisms at project level. It usually includes two types: one is the
Grievance Mechanism for community residents: it is used to receive, handle and feedback the
problems raised by community residents and related entities in the Project area during the
Project implementation and operation stage; The second is the grievance mechanism for project
workers: it is used to receive, handle and feedback work-related issues raised by workers
employed by project contractors and staff related to project activities.
154.     For community residents, the grievance mechanism operates at three levels. First, residents
may directly report issues to the relevant implementing entities and seek resolution. Second,
grievances may be raised through the village committee or neighborhood committee, with grassroots
government authorities responsible for coordination and handling, typically completing the process
within one to two weeks. Third, complaints may be submitted through the county-level Petition Office,
the county mayor’s hotline, or official email channels. This process generally includes complaint



                                                  86
registration, initiation within seven days, and resolution and feedback within two months. In addition,
residents may resolve disputes through civil litigation in the courts in accordance with applicable
laws. Grievances raised by project workers are mainly addressed through a three-tier labor dispute
resolution mechanism. First, workers may seek resolution through the internal labor grievance
mechanism of the employing enterprise. When workers believe that their rights and interests have
been infringed, have differing views on management measures, or identify violations of company
regulations, they may submit complaints to their department or directly to senior management.
Second, if internal mechanisms fail to resolve the issue, workers may apply for arbitration through
the Labor Dispute Arbitration Commission. The commission should accept the case and, in
accordance with the Rules for Handling Cases of the Labor Dispute Arbitration Commission, entrust
the competent administrative authorities to conduct verification and make determinations based on
which decisions are issued in line with national regulations. Third, if arbitration does not resolve the
dispute, workers may pursue judicial remedies. If dissatisfied with the arbitration outcome, workers
may file a lawsuit with the People’s Court. In accordance with relevant laws, labor dispute cases fall
under the jurisdiction of the primary people’s court where the employer is located or where the labor
contract is performed.
155.     Based on interviews with neighborhood committees and community representatives,
the grievance procedures in both Lingshui County and Changjiang County are considered to be
relatively mature. The vast majority of grievances are effectively resolved at the community
level, with very few cases escalating to civil litigation. Enterprise -level employee grievance
mechanisms are generally well managed and standardized, and are able to resolve most worker
complaints, with only occasional cases proceeding to judicial channels.
7. Conclusions, recommendations and action plans
7.1 Conclusion
156.       The overall environmental and social risk level of this project is set at "Substantial".
Activities that may have Substantial environmental and social risks have been excluded through
environmental and social screening process during project preparation. The direct environmental
impacts and risks that may arise from the project include: 1) environmental pollution impact during
the construction or restoration period and operation or management period, ecological impacts such
as disturbance of the transformed habitat (town, farmland and rural areas) and 2) disturbance of
natural ecosystems and coastal zones within the ecological protection red line, health and safety
impacts, etc.; Social impacts and risks include: 1) land use impact by project activities, such as small-
scale land use that may be caused by small-scale civil construction activities under the project, rural
non-point source pollution control activities may require the land leasing through voluntary lease,
etc.; 2) labor and employment risks brought about by civil engineering; 3) Protection of the rights and
interests of ethnic minorities and vulnerable groups; 4) The risk of insufficient public participation of
individual groups in the process of project implementation. Although some short-term, localized,
small-scale adverse environmental and social impacts that can be mitigated are inevitable in
implementation, on the whole, these adverse impacts are temporary and small-scale, and can be
effectively mitigated and managed by existing environmental and social management systems at the
national, Hainan and county levels. However, in view of the fact that the project will carry out various
types of activities in Lingshui County and Changjiang County of Hainan Province, including multiple
types of civil engineering activities in urban areas/rural areas, as well as the cumulative impact of
the implementation of various project activities under the coastal restoration plan, the large number
of stakeholders involved in the project activities, the complexity of the need for a large amount of
public participation, and the need for multi-departmental coordination and cooperation, the
comprehensive risk rating is "Substantial".
157.     This project aims to restore degraded coastal ecosystems by strengthening the protection
of coastal ecosystems and enhancing the capacity of integrated management of coastal ecosystems.
The Project enhances shoreline resilience by supporting restoration activities of various coastal
ecosystems, such as degraded coral reefs, mangroves, seagrass beds, major
estuaries/lagoons/coastal wetlands, damaged sandy shorelines, and the improvement of coastal
windbreaks. Reduce the stressors contributing to coastal ecosystem degradation through
sustainable forest management, improve and enhance urban and rural sewage management,



                                                   87
reduce agricultural non-point source pollution, and ecological restoration of inland rivers and coastal
areas, and build some education facilities to create a platform for enhancing public environmental
awareness. The implementation of project activities will bring broad and visible environmental and
social benefits. Although the Project activities involve a wide range of activities, it is very unlikely that
many ecological restoration and related water pollution control infrastructure construction activities
will be carried out in the same area at the same time. The local construction activities of this project
will not have significant cumulative negative environmental and social impacts on large areas. At the
same time, the implementation of this project will be coordinated with other activities to jointly
promote the realization of cumulative net benefits in the region, including the restoration of degraded
ecosystems, the sustainable management of forests, the treatment of urban and rural domestic
sewage and agricultural non-point sources, and the improvement of socio-economic effects and
management capabilities, such as 1) the restoration of coastal degraded ecosystems; 2) resilient
coastlines with increased erosion resistance; 3) reduction of pollution load into the sea; 4) Prevent
the transportation of plastic waste to water bodies; 5) reduce greenhouse gas emissions; 6) more
people benefit from increased resilience of terrestrial and aquatic ecosystems; 7) the Project area
demonstrates an enhanced coastal and marine landscape characterized by improved conservation
and sustainable management. The integrated management capacity of coastline ecosystems in
Hainan Province and the two project counties has been strengthened. From social perspectives, the
Project engaged stakeholders to participate in a wide range of activities, such as ecological
restoration activities, rural non-point source pollution control, which not only greatly improves the
local ecological environment, but also increases the income from the original land rent by improving
land utilization rate and improving farming conditions, or increases the possibility of land income
sharing: such as the distribution of abandoned land after remediation, the land rent obtained from
corner land, etc.
158.      The environmental and social management system assessment of this project believes
that China, Hainan Province, Lingshui County and Changjiang County have established
comprehensive and effective environmental and social management systems in relevant fields
to identify, assess, mitigate, manage and monitor the environmental and social impacts and
risks of related activities, including: 1) sound regulatory framework: relevant laws, regulations,
policies, standards, and technical guidelines have been formulated and issued at both the national
and local levels; 2) Clear implementation mechanisms: well-defined administrative procedures,
institutional arrangements, and functional responsibilities are in place for the management of
environmental and social risks and impacts, with professional staff and financial resources allocated
at all levels; and 3) Effective implementation performance: random reviews of representative past
cases indicate that environmental and social risk and impact management measures have been
effectively implemented and have achieved generally positive results. Overall, the assessment
concludes that the environmental and social management systems applicable to the Program are
broadly consistent with the policy requirements of the World Bank Program-for-Results (PforR)
financing instrument.
159.    Based on the detailed assessment of environmental and social systems in Chap ter 4
and Chapter 5 and the above analysis, the ESSA identifies areas where environmental and
social management could be further strengthened, including the following:
1) In current land acquisition and resettlement practices, except for hydro power resettlement
   projects, developers are generally not required to conduct land-use due diligence for other
   types of land acquisition and resettlement activities, nor are they required to monitor and
   evaluate the land acquisition, demolition, and resettlement process. For projects involving
   land leasing, there is also a lack of full-process stakeholder engagement mechanisms,
   which may result in prolonged unresolved land disputes or affect the timely disbursement
   of land compensation and the equitable distribution of land leasing benefits
2) Sub-projects that involve extensive stakeholder participation, such as rural non-point source
   pollution control, rehabilitation of aquaculture water intake and drainage networks, and
   urban and rural wastewater management, currently lack project-level, full-cycle stakeholder
   engagement mechanisms, and the existing community participation arrangements in the
   two counties require further strengthening. Each sub-project should conduct early,
   meaningful public consultation and information disclosure through multiple channels to


                                                     88
     identify and assess potential environmental and social impacts and risks, understand the
     needs of different stakeholders—particularly vulnerable groups (such as the elderly, women,
     and low-income populations) and directly affected groups—and integrate public feedback
     and targeted mitigation measures into project planning, design, and implementation. In
     addition, special attention should be given to the participation and equitable benefit -sharing
     of vulnerable groups, and, where relevant, culturally appropriate measures for ethnic
     minority communities should be adopted, such as communication in local minority
     languages.
3) Some rural wastewater collection and treatment facilities face operational challenges, including
   the entry of household solid waste and kitchen residues into collection systems, misconnections
   at drainage outlets of newly built rural houses, blockages in sewer networks due to the lack of
   grease traps, screens, and other essential components, lack of effluent discharge from treatment
   stations, and combined wastewater and stormwater overflows during rainy periods. These
   issues reduce the efficiency of rural domestic wastewater collection and treatment. There is a
   need to strengthen awareness and participation of beneficiary villagers in the operation and
   maintenance of wastewater facilities, and the Program should address infrastructure gaps and
   deficiencies in existing systems.
4) Workers engaged in coastal ecosystem restoration and sustainable forest man agement
   activities face occupational health and safety risks, including drowning, falls, bites, and heat
   stress. Particular attention is required for personnel involved in the operation and
   maintenance of coastal and marine ecological restoration activities. In addition to enhanced
   oversight by sector authorities (such as the Forestry Bureau and the Natural Resources and
   Planning Bureau), cross-sectoral support from maritime authorities is also necessary to
   improve awareness and implementation of OHS measures for workers engaged in water-
   related operations. Occupational health and safety should be treated as equally important
   as ecological restoration objectives.
7.2 Recommendations
160.     For the four findings proposed in Section 7.1, the ESSA team discussed with the Hainan
Provincial Department of Natural Resources and Planning, Changjiang County, Lingshui County
governments at all levels and relevant competent departments, and this report put forward the
following improvement suggestions as a project action plan:
 ⚫    Recommendation 1: Strengthen social risk supervision and management related to land
      use under the Program. Conduct due diligence for project activities involving land
      acquisition, or temporary land use, and establish full-process supervision and
      management mechanisms for project activities involving land leasing.
 ⚫    Recommendation 2: Establish a project-level stakeholder engagement mechanism.
      Ensure that all relevant stakeholders are meaningfully engaged throughout project
      implementation and are able to equitably share project benefits.
 ⚫    Recommendation 3: Improve rural domestic wastewater management. a) Require design
      institutes to coordinate closely with operation and maintenance (O&M) entities to address
      gaps in existing facilities and incorporate infrastructure suitable for rural domestic
      wastewater collection and treatment into project design; b) Establish co-management
      mechanisms that enable beneficiary villagers to participate in the operation and
      maintenance of rural wastewater facilities.
 ⚫    Recommendation 4: Strengthen occupational health and safety (OHS) in marine
      ecological restoration activities. Provide regular occupational health and safety training
      for workers engaged in surface and underwater operations, including personnel from
      construction contractors and subsequent operation and maintenance entities.
7.3 Action Plan
161.     In order to effectively implement the above recommendations, the action plan for this
project in Table 7-1 is developed and implemented during the implementation of the Project .
