                                                 91
8. Implement management and monitoring
162.    According to the relevant policies of the World Bank 19and the agreement between the
Bank and the borrower, the World Bank and the Borrower will manage and monitor project
implementation from their respective roles and perspectives throughout the implementation
period.
8.1 PIUs
163.     The Borrower is responsible for the day-to-day implementation of the Project, including
monitoring implementation progress, assessing achievement of results indicators, and fulfilling
all commitments and obligations set out in the Project legal documents, including the Project
Action Plan (PAP). These responsibilities include maintaining an effective environmental and
social management system (ESMS), monitoring the implementation of agreed action plans,
identifying issues in a timely manner, and taking appropriate corrective actions. In particular,
the Borrower shall:
      •      Develop and implement environmental and social risk management measures in accordance
             with the Project Management Manual (POM).20
      •      Implement all agreed environmental and social action plans in the Project action plan and
             maintain the environmental and social management system and its capacity at a level
             consistent with the assessment conclusions of this report.
      •      Submit an environmental and social management monitoring report (which may be a
             thematic section of the county's overall progress report on the overall progress of the Project
             or as a standalone report) on a semi-annual basis, including the implementation of an
             environmental and social action plan, training program, external monitoring, etc., to
             demonstrate continued compliance with the environmental and social management
             mechanisms applicable to the Project.
      •      Conduct regular monitoring, evaluation and audit of the performance of the environmental
             and social management system as required.
      •      The PIUs shall regularly review the performance, procedures and complaint handling of the
             grievance mechanism, and specific grievance cases need to be reflected in the
             environmental and social management monitoring report.
      •      Consult with the Bank before making any changes to the relevant environmental and social
             management systems during implementation.
164.      Hainan Provincial Department of Natural Resources and Planning (The Provincial Project
Office is the overall PPMO of the Project and is responsible for managing the overall
implementation of the activities in each project area. The main PIUs of the activities in each
project area are Lingshui County Xingling Construction Management Co., Ltd., Changjiang
Urban Construction Investment Co., Ltd., Changjiang Li Autonomous County Rural
Revitalization Investment and Development Co., Ltd., the relevant functional departments of the
Development and Reform Commission, the Ecological Environment Bureau, the Natural
Resources and Planning Bureau, the Agriculture and Rural Bureau, the Forestry Bureau, the
Water Affairs Bureau, and the Qicha Town of Changjiang County, who are responsible for the
approval and supervision of various work in the process of project implementation. Each
implementing agency shall designate specialized departments and personnel to manage the
implementation of environmental and social actions, report to the Project office, and provide
institutional settings and relevant information, which shall be supervised and monitored by the
Hainan Provincial Project Office and the World Bank.



19 In paragraph 12 of the Bank's PforR policy, the borrower is responsible for preparing and implementing results-oriented projects. The scope and objectives of the results-oriented

project, as well as the obligations of the borrower, are specified in the loan agreement. These obligations include due diligence and necessary monitoring and evaluation of results-
oriented projects (including payment correlation indicator verification mechanisms), financial, environmental and social systems and management mechanisms.
20 When this report is finalized, UNOPS will prepare a specific "Project Management Manual (POM)", which will be an independent document that clarifies each environmental and

social problem and corrective measures in project management, the corresponding responsible units and responsible persons, training plans, cost budgets, time nodes, etc.



                                                                                         92
8.2 World Bank
165.     Support the implementation of the Project, focusing on the consistency of the
environmental and social management performance of the Project implementation with the
requirements of this report, in particular with the requirements of the Project action plan. The
Bank will monitor borrowers' compliance with environmental and social risk management
commitments, including actions to strengthen mechanisms and capacity-building. The Bank will
regularly evaluate the entire project based on the risk assessment identified during the
preparation phase, using the risk assessment to respond to and help borrowers address
predictive and emerging risks, and to recommend improvements to the risk assessment. The
Bank also conducts site visits to work with stakeholders to provide appropriate support to the
borrower and review project audit reports and progress reports. The World Bank project team
regularly reports to management on project implementation in the form of Aide Memoire,
including document review, consultation with the borrower and stakeholders, and site visits. The
main activities are as follows:
   •   Verification of the implementation of any agreed actions, including any agreed capacity-
       building activities and any designated environmental and social impact mitigation measures;
   •   Conduct regular monitoring to ensure that the performance of the borrower's ESMS is
       acceptable to the Bank throughout its implementation period;
   •   Identify any additional administrative measures that may need to be taken to address poor
       performance or unexpected challenges during project implementation;
   •   Review the operation of the grievance mechanism through the semi-annual monitoring report
       to confirm the effective operation of the mechanism;
   •   The Bank will conduct regular site visits to complement the borrower's self-monitoring and
       provide other mutually agreed support.

Annex 3 Comparative analysis of environmental and social management systems and World Bank policies
PforR         core                                        China and Hainan E&S Management Requirements and Practices                                                    Consistency analysis and conclusions
Principles       or
Elements
Principle 1: Program E&S management systems are designed to promote E&S sustainability in the program design; avoid, minimize, or mitigate adverse impacts; and promote informed decision-making relating
to a program’s E&S effects.
Element          1: Environment: The PforR has an adequate environmental legal and regulatory framework. China and Hainan Province have formulated a                   The existing legal frameworks of China and
Operate within an series of environmental management laws, regulations, standards and norms based on the Environmental Protection Law, such as the                     Hainan Province, especially the EIA Law, have
adequate      legal Environmental Impact Assessment Law (2018), the Water Pollution Prevention and Control Law (2017), the Regulations on the Environmental            established an EIA system for both planning and
and      regulatory Protection Management of Construction Projects (2017), the Construction Projects EIA Classification Catalogue’ (2021), the Technical               construction projects, which will become the
framework        to Guidelines for EIA (including more than 20 Guidelines on pollution impacts and ecological impacts) and environmental standards. In marine          management framework to guide such works as
guide E&S impact sector, the Marine Environmental Protection Law has articles on marine ecological protection and land-based pollutant control. In agricultural        EIA, mitigation, management and monitoring of
                     sector   and   urban & rural domestic  sewage   pollution prevention   and control sector, there are the Regulations on   Crop  Pest  Control and the PforR activities at the planning level.
assessments,
mitigation,          Pesticide Management for agriculture NPS control, that are related to crop protection, fertilizer management, etc., as well as relevant local
management, and regulations and policies of Hainan Province, relevant national and local management measures, technical guidelines, sectoral environmental
                     standards, etc. This legal and regulatory framework provides a legal basis and implementation mechanism for the EIA and follow-up
monitoring at the
                     management of various activities to be supported by the PforR. In particular, the eco-environment zoning control management mechanism
PforR level.
                     established in China and Hainan in recent years has become the first line of defense for protecting the clean waters and green mountains
                     which restrict environmental access of projects at the front end of planning. The government authorities from provincial level to county level
                     of Hainan staffed with full-time personnel are responsible for supervising the implementation of these laws and regulations. In order to
                     implement this PforR, a PLG at the provincial and the Program County levels have been established, comprising members from officials of
                     relevant government authorities. These governmental-line authorities at provincial county level are the statutory regulatory agencies
                     responsible for mobilizing resources, taking action, implementing environmental laws and regulations, and managing the environmental
                     impact and risks of the PforR. This assessment is a review of the adequacy of China's environmental management system, demonstrating
                     that China and Hainan Province have a well-established legal and regulatory framework to guide the EIA, take mitigation measures for
                     management and monitoring of the PforR.
                     Specifically, the national and local environmental management systems in Hainan were also compared with the ESS1 Assessment and
                     Management of Environmental and Social Risks and Impacts under WBG’s ESF and EHSGs and their GIIP. Urban and rural domestic
                     wastewater management and crop production management systems are comparable to the WBG’s EHSG for Water and Sanitation, EHSG
                     for Health and Safety and EHSG for Annual and Perennial Crop Production, respectively, covering GIIP good practices in these
                     industries/sectors.
                                                                                                                                                                       The establishment of a comprehensive social,
                      Social: From the perspective of social law and the management framework, relevant policies, mechanisms, standards and management                 legal and management framework has been
                      procedures have been formulated and implemented at state, provincial, county and local levels to standardize social stability risk               accomplished at the national, provincial and
                      assessment. At the same time, social stability risk assessment is also an important procedural requirement in project application, feasibility   county levels. This framework is designed to
                      study and land acquisition processes. At the national level, the Interim Measures for Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major Fixed Asset      facilitate effective evaluation, reduction and
                      Investment Projects (2012) stipulates that project units must investigate and analyze social stability risks, solicit relevant public opinions,  management of social risks in the early stages
                      identify and catalogue risk points, evaluate the possibility and degree of impact of risks, and propose plans and measures to prevent and        of implementation. This is consistent with
                      resolve risks. The "Guiding Opinions on Establishing and Improving the Social Stability Risk Assessment Mechanism for Major Decision-            Core Principle 1 of a sustainable social risk
                      Making Matters (Trial)" (2012) stipulates that social stability risk assessment should be conducted for major decision-making matters, major     management system.
                      engineering project construction, and major policy formulation. The Interim Regulations on Major Administrative Decision-Making
                      Procedures (2019) stipulate that the decision-making unit or other relevant units responsible for risk assessment are obliged to organize an
                      assessment of the risk controllability of the draft decision for the implementation of major administrative decisions that have the potential to
                      adversely affect social stability and public safety. Major administrative decisions include: 1) formulating major public policies and measures
                      related to public services, market supervision, social management, environmental protection, etc.; 2) Formulate important plans for economic
                      and social development; 3) Decide on major public construction projects to be implemented in the administrative region; 4) Decide on other
                      major matters that have a significant impact on economic and social development, involve major public interests or vital interests of the
                      public, etc. The "Opinions on Strengthening the Construction of Social Stability Risk Assessment Mechanism for Major Decisions under the
                      New Situation" (2020) requires that social stability risk assessment must be carried out before making decisions on major matters, including
                      important construction projects. The opinions stipulate the content, assessment methods, assessment procedures, assessment
                      management, and application of assessment results of social stability risk assessment. In addition, the opinions also emphasize that social
                      stability risk assessment is an essential part of project feasibility study and project application report. The Land Administration Law of the
                      People's Republic of China (revised in 2020) requires that before the start of land acquisition and demolition activities, relevant departments

                                                                                                         107
PforR        core                                      China and Hainan E&S Management Requirements and Practices                                                         Consistency analysis and conclusions
Principles     or
Elements
                    need to conduct land status surveys, social stability risk assessments, and consult with affected persons. From the provincial level: The
                    General Office of the Hainan Provincial Committee of the Communist Party of China has issued a notice regarding the printing and
                    distribution of the Measures for Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major Decisions in Hainan Province (Qiong Banfa [2022] No. 4). The
                    aim of this notice is to provide clarification on the scope and content of social stability risk assessment for major decisions in Hainan Province.
                    The subject and method of assessment, assessment procedures, assessment management, application of assessment results, and
                    decision-making implementation tracking are all covered in this document. A comprehensive set of provisions has been established to
                    address matters pertaining to the assessment process, the allocation of rewards and sanctions, and the establishment of accountability
                    frameworks. At the county level: Lingshui County has issued the "Implementation Rules for the Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major
                    Decisions in Lingshui Li Autonomous County" (Lingwen Evaluation Group [2023] No. 1), and Changjiang County has issued the "Notice on
                    Further Promoting the Social Stability Risk Assessment of Major Decisions" (Changzheng Zi [2020] No. 41). These documents explicitly
                    delineate major decision-making matters that are directly related to the vital interests of the populace, encompass a wide range of domains,
                    and are susceptible to social stability issues. Party and government organs are obliged to conduct a social stability risk assessment and
                    prepare a separate social stability risk analysis report prior to decision-making, including the construction of major engineering projects,
                    major policy formulation, and other major decision-making matters that have a greater impact on social stability. Such matters include land
                    acquisition and demolition, farmers' burdens, state-owned enterprise restructuring, environmental improvement, social security, public
                    welfare undertakings, garbage and sewage treatment, and other sensitive government investment projects that affect the environment.

    Annex 4 Stakeholder Analysis
    The ESMS of the Project Program will involve different stakeholders, including individuals, government
    authorities, and other agencies. Stakeholders are either affected by any activity or affect the construction
    and operation of any activity. Therefore, for each activity under the Program, stakeholders involved will be
    identified through a mechanism. Stakeholders under each type of outcome under the ESMS of the Project
    Program are consistent, including affected parties, interested parties, and management authorities. Refer

Annex 8 E&S Risks Mitigation Measures
The following general E&S impact measures are summarized in this report based on previous
experiences in similar project or program management. Specific mitigation measures for each
main activity under the PforR Program will be detailed in the specific and standardized
subsections on E&S management, with estimated cost, and included in the bidding documents
and contracts
                                                          Table A8-1 E&S Risks Mitigation Measures
 Item                               Main            Main Impacts      Generic Mitigation Measures
                                    Activities
                                    Excavation,     Air pollution due to   1.     Fencing the construction site with enclosure separating the site
                                    backfill for    fly-dust and exhaust   from outside. Spray devices are installed to the top of the enclosure wall
                                    pipelines                              2.     scheduling excavation to avoid dry and windy weather properly,
                                    installation,                          adopting advance construction and procedures, adopting wet -
                                    hauling of                             processing gravels and concrete system equipped with vacuum
                                    constructio                            cleaning equipment, regularly watering construction roads for dedusting
                                    n materials
                                                                           3.     Applying netting or impermeable dust -proof cloth to the Earthwork
                                    during civil
                                                                           and Aggregate piles. Materials prone to generating dust should be
                                    works
                                                                           unloaded gently and placed slowly and stored in sealed containers.
                                    constructio
                                    n                                      4.     Washing transportation vehicles before leaving at design ated
                                                                           platform, preferably located inside the entrance. During washing tires
                                                                           and vehicles, attention shall be paid to avoid slurry from sticking to
                                                                           surface of vehicles. Building material loaded in vehicles shall be
                                                                           covered with tarpaulins of height lower than the upper edge of the
                                                                           vehicle's trough.
                                                                           5.     Vehicles shall not be powered by inferior fuels. Strictly implement
                                                                           the relevant regulations on vehicle emissions to avoid emitting black
                                                                           smoke. Increasing the use of electronic cargo trucks.
                                                                           6.     No concrete mixing station or asphalt mixing station is set up at
                                                                           the construction site.
                                    Civil works     Noise impact on        1. Comply with the Emission Standard of Environmental Noise for




 Pollution prevention and control
                                    constructio     Residents and               Boundary of Construction Site (GB 12523-2011) by reasonably
                                    n               construction workers        scheduling construction activities. Construction during nighttime
                                                                                hours (22:00–06:00) should be avoided as far as practicable or
                                                                                limited to low-noise operations, particularly near noise -sensitive
                                                                                receptors close to the project alignment. Where continuous
                                                                                construction is required for special reasons, prior approval from the
                                                                                competent authorities shall be obtained and advance
                                                                                communication with affected residents shall be conducted.
                                                                           2.     Select low-noise construction equipment to the extent practicable.
                                                                           Implement good construction practices and strengthen site management
                                                                           to reduce noise generated by human activities, and operate machinery
                                                                           strictly in accordance with relevant regulations.
                                                                           3.     Reasonably arrange the timing of construction material
                                                                           transportation. On road sections with nearby noise -sensitive receptors,
                                                                           vehicles shall reduce speed, and horn use shall be prohibited.
                                                                           4.     Install “No Honking” warning signs in noise -sensitive sections, and
                                                                           implement controls on noise sources, transmission paths, and traffic
                                                                           noise. Provide construction workers with appropriate personal
                                                                           protective equipment, such as noise-reducing earplugs.
                                                                           5.     Strengthen noise monitoring during the construction phase. Where
                                                                           noise levels at sensitive receptors exceed applicable standards,
                                                                           temporary or mobile noise barriers should be installed as necessary.



                                    Surface         Environmental          1.    Temporary storage stie for earth and gravels shall be located

                                    site            from earthworks and    residential areas. The temporarily piled-up earth and gravels are
                                    leveling,       construction waste     compacted, rolled, and covered with tarpaulins.

                          Civil works    Construction            1.    Wastewater from aggregate processing systems shall be treated by
                          constructio    wastewater              sedimentation tank or floc settling tank. Treated effluent can be used for
                          n                                      watering the construction site for dedusting. Slurry can be pumped into

                                                                 evaporation.
                                                                 The wastewater from mechanical equipment cleaning is treated by a

                                                                 be discharged into the nearby water bodies
                                                                 2.    Contractor worker shall use public toilets/latrines

                                                                       traffic.

Annex 9 Socio-economic and ethnic minorities baseline survey
Annex 9.1 Socio-economic overview of the Project area
Hainan Province: In 2024, the province's GDP was 793.569 billion yuan. The primary industry
contributed 162.763 billion yuan, the secondary industry 149.792 billion yuan and the tertiary
industry 481.014 billion yuan. The industrial structure ratio was 20.5:18.9:60.6. The annual per
capita GDP was 75,903 yuan, while the province's per capita disposable income for permanent
residents totaled 34,829 yuan. Urban residents earned an average of 44,307 yuan, while rural
residents earned an average of 22,146 yuan. Annual per capita living expenses averaged 25,908
yuan, with urban residents spending 31,507 yuan and rural residents 18,415 yuan.
Changjiang County: In 2024, the county's GDP is expected to reach 16.519 billion yuan,
marking a 1.3% year-on-year increase (calculated at constant prices). Of this total, the primary
industry is expected to contribute 5.019 billion yuan, representing a 3.2% year-on-year increase.
Meanwhile, the secondary industry is expected to contribute 5.397 billion yuan, marking a 1.9%
year-on-year increase, while the tertiary industry is expected to contribute 6.102 billion yuan,
reflecting a 0.5% year-on-year decrease. The ratio of the three industrial sectors was
30.38:32.67:36.94. The country’s per capita GDP was 69,966 yuan, an increase of 1.2% year-
on-year.
Lingshui County: In 2024, Lingshui County's gross domestic product (GDP) is expected to
reach 27.537 billion yuan, marking a year-on-year increase of 6.1%. The added value of the
primary, secondary and tertiary industries was 7.786 billion, 3.733 billion and 16.018 billion yuan
respectively, representing year-on-year increases of 1.3%, 3.6% and 8.7%. The three industries
accounted for 28.3%, 13.6% and 58.1% respectively. In 2024, Lingshui County's per capita GDP
will be 71,871 yuan, a year-on-year increase of 5.2%. The per capita disposable income of
permanent residents in Lingshui County will be 29,066 yuan in 2024, representing a year-on-
year increase of 5.3%. The per capita disposable income of urban residents was 39,299 yuan,
an increase of 4.2% year on year, while the per capita disposable income of rural permanent
residents was 20,966 yuan, an increase of 7.0%.

Annex 9.2 Administrative division and population of the Project County
Hainan Province: Hainan Province has four administrative divisions at the county - level (four
prefecture-level cities), 25 at the county level (ten county - level districts, five county-level cities,
four counties and six ethnic autonomous counties) and 218 at the township level (22 streets, 175
towns and 21 townships). The prefecture-level cities are Haikou, Sanya, Sansha and Danzhou.
County-level cities: Wuzhishan, Wenchang, Qionghai, Wanning and Dongfang. Counties:
Ding'an County, Tunchang County, Chengmai County and Lingao County. Autonomous counties:
Baisha Li Autonomous County, Changjiang Li Autonomous County, Ledong Li Autonomous
County, Lingshui Li Autonomous County, Baoting Li and Miao Autonomous County and
Qiongzhong Li and Miao Autonomous County. As of the end of 2024, Hainan Province had a
permanent population of 10.48 million. The urbanization rate of the permanent population is
63.08%. In terms of gender composition, there are 5.56 million men and 4.92 million women. By
the end of the year, the urban permanent population had increased by 96,900 to reach 6,612,800,
while the rural permanent population remained at 3,870,400. The urban permanent population
accounted for 63.08% of the total population of the province.



                                                                   136
Changjiang County: Changjiang Li Autonomous County is located in the northwestern part of
Hainan Island, spanning the latitudes of 18°53' to 19°30' north and the longitudes of 108°38' to
109°17' east. It borders Baisha Li Autonomous County to the east, Ledong Li Autonomous
County to the south, Dongfang City to the southwest (with the Changhua River forming the
boundary), the Beibu Gulf to the northwest, and Danzhou City to the northeast (separated by the
Zhubi River). The county has jurisdiction over seven towns and one township: Shilu, Chahe,
Shiyutian, Wulie, Changhua, Haiwei, Qicha and Wangxia. It has 17 community residents'
committees and 74 villagers' committees. By the end of 2024, the county's total population is
expected to reach 253,000, comprising 109,700 urban residents and 143,600 rural residents.
The county's permanent population at the end of 2024 will be 236,600, with an urbanization rate
of 61.41%.
Lingshui County: Lingshui Li and Miao Autonomous County is located in the southeast of Hainan
Island. It is bordered by Qiongzhong Li and Miao Autonomous County to the north, Wanning City
to the northeast, Baoting Li and Miao Autonomous County to the west, Sanya City to the
southwest, and the South China Sea to the southeast. It has a total land area of 1,128 square
kilometers, a responsible sea area of 1,223 square kilometers, and a coastline measuring 118.57
kilometers. Lingshui County comprises 11 townships: Coconut Grove, Xincun, Yingzhou, Benhao,
Guangpo, Sancai, Li'an, Longguang, Wenluo, Timeng and Qunying. There is a total of 107
administrative villages, 586 natural villages, 1,151 village groups, nine communities, two
residences and 169 resident groups. In 2024, the population birth rate in Lingshui County will be
8.96 per thousand people, the death rate will be 6.68 per thousand people, and the natural growth
rate will be 2.28 per thousand people. The permanent population is 384,000, comprising 384,000
urban and 199,000 rural residents, giving an urbanization rate of 46.18%.

Annex 9.3 Overview of vulnerable groups
The vulnerable groups include people with disabilities and low-income groups (e.g. Urban and
Rural Persons of Extreme Poverty, low-income households). The statistics of vulnerable groups
in the Project counties are shown in Table 9-4.
In 2024, Changjiang County provided minimum living allowance to 3,144 households (7,777
individuals) across urban and rural areas, including 2,373 rural households (6,139 people) and
771 urban households (1,638 people), with total subsidies amounting to 54.0309 million yuan.
The county also distributed support funds totaling 7.5755 million yuan to 682 urban and rural
households (700 individuals) in extreme poverty, and provided temporary assistance of 3.9025
million yuan to 726 households (2,862 individuals). Additionally, welfare benefits were granted
to 120 orphans (168,100 yuan), 3,974 children in difficult circumstances (1.7864 million yuan),
and 576 children without parental care (574,600 yuan). Longevity subsidies totaling 8.6384
million yuan were distributed to 49,142 seniors aged 80 and above, while disabi lity care and
living allowances reached 12.9468 million yuan for 69,320 recipients.
In 2024, the number of urban residents receiving minimum living allowances in Lingshui County
reached 1,121, up 11.2% year-on-year, while the rural figure stood at 8,053, up 10.51%. The
number of urban and rural residents receiving special hardship support increased by 8.72% to
1,932.

Annex 9.4 Natural resources
Land resources in Changjiang County: The total area of the county is 162,050.58 hectares,
including the state-owned Bawangling Forest Farm. Of this, 37,277.23 hectares is cultivated land,
accounting for 23.00% of the total area. Of this, 13,380.19 hectares are paddy fields, and
23,897.04 hectares are dry land. Garden land covers a total area of 18,945.60 hectares,
accounting for 11.69% of the total land area. This includes 4,061.69 hectares of orchards and
14,883.91 hectares of other garden land. Forest land accounts for 52.30% of the land area,
totaling 84,748.64 hectares. Pasture covers 2,465.03 hectares, accounting for 1.52% of the land
area. There are 3,844.89 hectares of other agricultural land, accounting for 2.37% of the land
area. There are 8,072.09 hectares of construction land, accounting for 4.98% of the total area.
There are 7,036.99 hectares of unused land, accounting for 4.34% of the total area.

hectares, including:2,172.23 hectares of wetlands,19,189.05 hectares of cultivated
land,32,106.22 hectares of garden land,35,748.61 hectares of forest land,178.84 hectares of
grassland,13,300.83 hectares of urban, village, industrial and mining land,1,247.11 hectares of
transportation land,118.56 hectares of hydraulic construction land,5,104.97 hectares of water
area,1,529.44 hectares of other land Shoreline resources: The total coastline length of Lingshui
County is 118.57 kilometers, accounting for 6.09% of Hainan Province's total coastline. The
natural coastline length is 83.48 kilometers, with a retention rate of 70.4%.

Annex 9.5 Baseline survey of ethnic minorities in project counties
Annex 9.5.1 Overview of ethnic minorities in the Project area
Hainan Province is a multi-ethnic province, with 8,498,241 Han people 21, accounting for
84.30%; The population of various ethnic minorities totals 1,582,991, accounting for 15.70%.
More than 30 ethnic minorities live on the island, among which the hereditary ethnic minorities
are Han (the Han population mainly lives in the northeast, north and coastal areas of Hainan), Li
and Miao (mainly living in Ledong, Lingshui, Changjiang, Baoting, Qiongzhong, Baisha and other
autonomous counties in the central and southern parts of Hainan Island, as well as Sanya,
Dongfang, Wuzhishan and other cities), and the Hui mainly live in Sanya City. At present, there
are six ethnic autonomous counties of Ledong, Lingshui, Changjiang, Baot ing, Qiongzhong, and
Baisha 22 , Wuzhishan City and Dongfang City, which are subject to the provisions of ethnic

     21 Source: Communiqué of the Seventh National Census of Hainan Province (No. 1)

22 Ethnic minority autonomous counties: According to Article 12 of the Law of the People's Republic of China on Regional Autonomy for Ethnic Minorities,
autonomous regions may be established based on one or more ethnic minority settlements, taking into account local ethnic relations, economic development and
historical conditions. Ethnic autonomous counties must be based on ethnic minority settlements and usually require a certain proportion of the ethnic minority
population (generally not less than 30% in practice). An ethnic autonomous county is a county-level administrative region established by China in areas inhabited
by ethnic minorities. The aim of their establishment is to guarantee the equal rights of ethnic minorities in politics, the economy, culture, and other areas, as well




                                                                                139
autonomous areas, Sanya City, which enjoys the policy of ethnic autonomous areas, ten towns
with ethnic minority communities are governed by policies for ethnic townships. These areas
account for 48.8% of the province's land area.
Changjiang Li Autonomous County: This is a multi-ethnic county, home to 27 ethnic minorities,
including the Li, Miao, Zhuang, Hui and Han. The Li and Miao are the main e thnic groups living
in the territory. Ethnic minorities account for 39.02% of the population, totaling 90,564 people.
Of these, 86,864 are Li, 1,352 are Zhuang, 675 are Miao and 1,673 belong to other ethnic groups.
The Li people are mainly found in Wangxia Township, as well as in the towns of Qicha, Chahe,
Shiyutian, Shilu and Wulie. As of 2024, Egang Village had a total population of 10,993, of whom
10,770 were ethnic minorities, primarily from the Li group. It is known as "China's largest Li ethnic
gathering village". Pai'an Village, located in Chahe Town, has 126 households and 546 residents,
and was recognized as a "China's Ethnic Minority Characteristic Village" in January 2020. The
Li and Han peoples have formed a unique cultural symbiosis in Changjiang. The Han and Li
people have intermarried for a long time, forming an ethnic relationship through blood ties. They
jointly believe in the culture of King Junling and participate in the folk custom of 'welcoming the
gods'. Under the influence of the Han people’s reverence for literature and learning, they have
also formed cultural carriers such as cloth genealogy.
Lingshui Li Autonomous County is located in the southeast of Hainan Province. It has a total
land area of 110,695.86 hectares and comprises 11 townships and 118 administrative villages,
including Lingmen and Nanpingju, as well as one township farm and 585 natural villages and
1,160 villager groups. Lingshui is a county with a large ethnic minority population, and the main
ethnic groups are the Li, the Han, and the Miao. According to statistics from the seventh national
census, the permanent population of Lingshui Li Autonomous County is 372,511, of whom
187,201 are Han Chinese (50.27%) and 185,310 are ethnic minorities (49.73%). Among them,
181,563 Li people mainly live in Yingzhou Town, Benhao Town, Wenluo Town, Longguang Town,
Guangpo Town, Qunying Township and Timeng Township, while 987 Miao people mainly live in
three villages: Shiba Miao Village, Baishuiling Miao Village and Xiaonanping Miao Village in
Timeng Township. The population of the 28 other ethnic minorities, including Zhuang, Hui,
Mongolian, Uyghur, Manchu, Buyi, Tujia, Korean, Gaoshan, Tibetan and Dai, is small, ranging
from over 100 people to just a few individuals.
The environmental and social assessment team screened the distribution and settlement of
ethnic minorities in cooperation with various project agencies. This was achieved through field
surveys, data collection and a literature review. The results of this screening are shown in
Table 9-6 and 9-7.

Li people: The Li people are the earliest inhabitants of Hainan Island, in terms of language: The
Lingshui Li dialects include the Ha, Qi and Sai dialects. The Sai dialect is mainly found in Tianzai,
Muda and Liao Ci in Yingzhou Town; Danlu; Hongqi; Xinguang; Wuyi; Qunying Township in
Longguang Township; Baimao; Zuguan; Baishi; Yashang; Yayao; and Shiba, among other places.
The Qi dialect is found in Li Yue; Basho; Shipo; Xiaomei; the highlands of England; Longguang
Cemetery Mountain; and other places. The Harbin dialect is found in Beigou, Wuhe, Gulou,
Hongshoe, Wan'an, Gangshan, Xinpo, Juntian, Changwei, Baimao, Luhao, Junchang, Junpu,
Leli, Tianxin, Xinxing, Central, Wanling, Shiguan, Guangxin and Wanxing in Longguang Town;
Wuxing and Wenxin in Wenluo Town; and Zhangxian, Powei and Miaojing in Guangpo Town.
The villages in Lingmenju that are engaged in agricultural production are all in the Harbin dialect
area, while the Liwan operation area is in the Qi dialect area. It is also found in Timeng Township,
Laochang, Gouwei and Yuanjing. Currently, the vast majority of Li people can speak Chinese
and do not have their own written language, instead commonly using Chinese. In terms of cultural
traditions, the Li people have a rich heritage of customs, including Li brocade textiles, pottery -
making skills, boat-shaped houses and tattoos, as well as Danzhou opera, tuning and folk songs,
the Li March 3rd festival, folk songs and dragon boat racing for fishermen, the Changcheng
Qiong opera and military and village folk songs, among other local characteristics and customs.
The Li people mostly live in the mountains of central and southern Hainan Island, which has a
tropical monsoon climate. Their traditional way of life is based on rice farming and planting
tropical crops such as rubber and betel nuts, as well as fishing and handicrafts. In terms of
clothing, the most famous aspect of Li costumes is their exquisite kasuri dyeing s kills and
gorgeous patterns. The most famous of these are kasuri dyeing, double-sided embroidery and
weaving embroidery. The patterns are variously abstract and exquisitely colorful. Festival
culture: The Li people's festivals are mostly related to agriculture and ancestor worship, and
have a strong national flavor. 3 March (3rd day of the 3rd lunar month): This is the grandest of
the Li people's traditional festivals, equivalent to the Spring Festival of the Han people. On this
day, people worship their ancestors and take part in various cultural and sporting activities, such



                                                         141
as singing, dancing, crossbow shooting and swinging. Notably, it is also a "love festival" where
young men and women can find their loved ones. They express their feelings by singing l ove
songs to each other. The "Shanlan Festival", also known as the "Harvest Festival": This festival
celebrates a good harvest. When the upland rice is ripe, the villages celebrate on different days
to thank the gods for their blessings. They hold banquets and activities involving singing and
dancing to pray for good weather in the coming year. Religious beliefs: The Li people's religious
beliefs are mainly primitive nature worship, centered around ancestor worship. Ancestor worship:
This lies at the heart of Li beliefs. They believe that the spirits of their ancestors will bless future
generations, so every family enshrines and worships ancestral tablets on important festivals and
events. Nature worship: Belief in animism. They worship nature gods, such as mountain gods,
stone gods, tree gods and water gods, believing that these gods control people's lives and
livelihoods. Sacrificial ceremonies are often held before important agricultural activities (such as
mountain clearing, sowing and harvesting) to pray for the gods' permission and blessing.
Witchcraft, Taoism and mother goddesses: In traditional Li society, when someone falls ill or a
disaster strikes, people believe it is the work of a ghost. Special religious people, known as "Dao
Gong" (male) or "Mothers" (female), are invited to perform rituals, exorcise ghosts, heal diseases
and communicate with people and gods.
Miao: With a population of over 60,000, the Miao people are the second largest ethnic minority
in Hainan. They are primarily located in the central and southern regions of the island, where
farming and agriculture are their primary sources of livelihood. In terms of language: The 'Miao
dialect' they speak is primarily Hainan Miao. It belongs to the Yao branch of the Miao -Yao
language family within the Sino-Tibetan language family, rather than the Miao language branch.
They have no written language, and the Hmong language is uniform across the island with no
dialect differences. The Hainan Miao call themselves 'Kinmen' or 'Jindimen', and 'Miao' is their
name. In terms of traditional culture, there is Miao batik, Hainan Miao songs and the Sanyuan
dance. In terms of food and clothing, the Miao people in the Project area mainly eat corn and
rice mixed with wheat, red millet, potatoes and beans. The main meat eaten is pork, although
beef and mutton are also consumed. "New Year's pigs" are slaughtered during Chinese New
Year. In terms of clothing, traditional Chinese craft techniques such as weaving, embroidery,
picking and dyeing are maintained. According to field visits and observations, young people
generally do not wear national costumes, except during major festivals or traditional ceremonies,
and mostly wear their own clothes. The same applies to the elderly, who are at home all year
round. Festival culture: The main traditional festivals of the Miao people in the Project area
include the Mountain Festival, the New Year Festival, Cutting Mars and Rushing to the Seedling
Field. However, the traditional festivals of the Miao people differ from region to region. Some
festivals are common in several regions, while others are unique to a single region. Religious
beliefs: In the past, the Miao believed in animism and worshipped nature and their ancestors.
Therefore, their main beliefs include nature worship, totem worship and ancestor worship, as
well as other primitive religious forms. Some Miao people also believe in Chri stianity and
Catholicism. The Miao people who speak the eastern dialect mainly believe in Buddhism and
Taoism.
Annex 9.5.2 Identification of ethnic minorities
The term 'ethnic minority' refers to ethnic minorities in the general sense: unique and
disadvantaged social and cultural groups that have the following characteristics to varying
degrees: a) self-identification as members of unique ethnic minority cultural groups that are
recognized by others; b) collective attachment to residential areas or ancestral territories with
unique geographical characteristics within the Project area and attachment to the natural
resources of these areas and territories; c)traditional cultures, economies, social systems and/or
political systems; d)minority languages that differ from the official languages of the country or
region.
According to the above definition and its four criteria, although some of the Li and Miao ethnic
groups have certain uniqueness in terms of cultural customs and living habits, However, against
ESS7 (see table 9-8 for details), these two ethnic groups have not yet fully met all four criteria



                                                  142
for the identification of "indigenous peoples". Specifically, these two ethnic groups lack a
characteristic traditional system independent of the mainstream system, nor do they form an
exclusive collective belonging to their ancestral home. Therefore, the criteria for ESS 7 are not
triggered. The program will adopt culturally adaptable measures to ensure that minorities can
actively participate and benefit equally, in line with the core principles of the PforR’s policy.

Annex 9.5.3 Impact of the Project on local ethnic minorities
The impact of project implementation on ethnic minorities: Firstly, at the beginning of the Project's
preparation, all activities with a significant adverse impact on ethnic minorities and vulnerable
groups were excluded from the scope of PforR activities. Secondly, none of the physical activities
under this project have a negative impact on the lifestyle or livelihood of ethnic minorities.
Contributing to the improvement of the local environment through ecological restoration activities
and upgrading sewage and non-point source pollution control systems promotes and supports
the local systematic development plan for ethnic minorities. The Project will also create more
development opportunities for residents in ethnic minority areas after its implementation and
completion. For example, the Project has increased opportunities for migrant employment. In the
rural non-point source pollution control project, villagers can increase their income by renting out
improved fields and by going out to work. The assessment also found that, by understanding
provincial and county management methods, the existing ethnic minority affairs management
system can ensure adequate consultation and communication with ethnic minority residents. To
incorporate the views and suggestions of ethnic minorities into the design and implementation of
the Project, benefit-sharing mechanisms will be established at project level, as well as adaptive
measures for ethnic minorities in stakeholder engagement plans, to ensure equal benefits.
Annex 9.5.4 Sampling survey of ethnic minorities in the Project area
The environmental and social evaluation team conducted a sample survey of ethnic minorities in
townships and communities in Lingshui and Changjiang counties that were likely to carry out the
Project's activities. This involved two townships/streets within the Project scope: Qicha Town in
Changjiang County and Coconut Grove Town in Lingshui County. A total of 20 households were
selected using stratified and random sampling methods, yielding 50 valid responses. Of these,
28 were female respondents, accounting for 56%, and all 50 were ethnic minorities, including 37
Li and 13 Miao.
In terms of land resources and the main sources of income, the on-site investigation found that
the Project area is primarily situated within or near urban areas, with an average of 1.15 acres
of cultivated land per capita. Only 20.7% of the population are engaged in agricultural production
activities, primarily grain, fruit and vegetable cultivation. Overall, agriculture accounts for only
14.1% of total household income, with the main sources being non-agricultural income, such as




                                                               143
wages, collective income, dividends and operating income. The per capita annual income of the
sample families is approximately 37,994 yuan.
In terms of lifestyle and cultural customs, the ethnic minority population in the sampled townships
and towns is characterized by large mixed settlements and small Han, Li and Miao settlements.
Following on-site visits and surveys, it was found that almost all respondents believed that they
were no different to the Han Chinese group in terms of social welfare, rights and guarantees, or
the economic, social and political systems. Only certain cultural customs and living habits were
unique. The majority of respondents could communicate in Mandarin, while a small minority
(mainly older people) could only understand or speak their own language. Both groups are mainly
engaged in traditional agricultural production and have no special cultural significance in their
livelihood or ancestral territory. They occasionally go out to work, and their economic income is
not much different. In terms of cultural customs, long-term exchanges and integration mean they
are basically interconnected. This includes the national festival 'March 3rd', celebrated by all
ethnic groups. In terms of beliefs, most of them practice ancestor worship and are not particularly
religious, with relatively few religious believers.
In terms of their attitude towards such projects, most respondents are aware that implementing
environmental protection and ecological restoration projects can greatly improve urban and rural
environmental conditions and infrastructure. They also believe that such projects will not have
an adverse effect on their lifestyle or national culture. Regarding the construction of rural sewage
stations and agricultural facilities, if small-scale land acquisition is inevitable, the village will
prioritize the use of collective construction land and unused land. If the site selection c onditions
are not met, the acquisition of agricultural land will be considered. According to the experience
of previous projects, expropriated households can be compensated if the land is occupied. Those
who meet the social security conditions of landless farmers will be included in the social security
arrangement. At the same time, simple civil engineering during the Project construction period
often brings more local employment opportunities, thus providing additional income. Regarding
non-point source pollution control and land consolidation projects requiring land leasing, the
respondents recognize the importance of a voluntary leasing method, which increases rental
income by improving farming roads, upgrading drainage and irrigation canals, and enhancin g
land utilization and planting efficiency. The increase in land rent can cover not only the
agricultural income from the original land use, but also enable tenants to seek employment
elsewhere and earn a higher income as migrants.
